BACKLOG — future improvements to implement when ready
======================================================

[RESOLVED 2026-07-23] SYNTHETIC TEST DATA (PROB*/BAD* OUTCOME ROWS) CORRUPTED THE LIVE P10.3 BRIER ALERT FOR 4+ DAYS
Priority: was High -- silently corrupted a live model-quality safety signal
  (P10.3 Brier alert) undetected since 2026-07-19; same root-cause class as
  the already-resolved 2026-07-21 KXBADDATE3 incident (see MYSTERY REVERT-
  adjacent entry / project memory), second occurrence of the same failure
  pattern.

Problem:
  Found while reviewing routine `python main.py cron` output: the P10.3
  Brier alert fired "Brier score has exceeded 0.22 for two consecutive
  weeks (0.2687, 0.4525)" on back-to-back cron runs two days apart with
  byte-identical figures despite new settlements happening in between --
  the tell that something was frozen/fake, not a live-recomputed signal
  (`get_brier_over_time()` is in fact a live, uncached SQL query every
  call, so "frozen" pointed at contaminated inputs, not stale caching).
  Root cause: 36 synthetic rows (`PROB0`-`PROB17`, `BAD0`-`BAD17`, all
  `city=None`, `method='ensemble'`) sitting in `predictions.db`'s
  `predictions`/`outcomes` tables, all inserted in a single batch at the
  exact same `predicted_at` timestamp (2026-07-19 21:04:58), with
  fabricated `settled_at` values in Jan/Feb 2026 -- physically before their
  own `predicted_at`, an impossible sequence for a real trade. Almost
  certainly an ad-hoc `python -c` test of the Brier-alert/disputed-row path
  run directly against the live production DB (same failure shape as the
  2026-07-21 KXBADDATE3 incident: `_auto_place_trades()` called ad-hoc
  against real DB paths instead of pytest's auto-sandboxed temp DB), never
  cleaned up. The fabricated pair (0.95-prob "PROB" rows all settling YES,
  0.05-prob "BAD" rows also all settling YES) averages to exactly 0.4525 --
  matching the alert's reported figure to 4 decimal places. Real W27
  (0.2687, 3 genuine multi-day predictions) was legitimate; W28 had ZERO
  real multi-day settlements until this was found -- the alert's "second
  consecutive bad week" was 100% synthetic.
  This wasn't limited to the alert: `brier_score_by_method()` (drives the
  "lifetime Brier 0.3200, ensemble pin not auto-renewing" warning logged on
  every single cron run) joins the same `multiday_predictions JOIN
  outcomes_valid` shape, filtered to `method='ensemble'` -- exactly what
  all 36 fake rows were tagged as. A narrower fix scoped only to the alert
  function would have left the strategy-retirement/pin-expiry path (a
  real live-trading-relevant decision) still corrupted.

What shipped:
  Verified full scope via 3 independent sweeps before touching anything:
  (1) `settled_at < predicted_at` across the whole DB (not just multi-day)
  -- found exactly these 36 rows, nothing else; (2) non-`KX`-prefixed
  ticker scan across `predictions`/`multiday_predictions`/`outcomes_valid`
  -- same 36, no other city affected; (3) batch-identical-`predicted_at`
  scan (>5 rows sharing one exact timestamp) across all cities -- the only
  match besides legitimate same-cron-cycle multi-city batches (6-7 rows,
  multiple real distinct cities each) was this one 36-row, single-city=None
  batch. Confirmed isolated to one incident, no other city/table affected.
  Used the existing `tracker.mark_outcome_disputed()` function (built
  2026-07-18, see DISPUTED-ROW EXCLUSION PREDICATE entry below) instead of
  deleting rows or writing a new bespoke filter -- one call per ticker sets
  `disputed=1`, which every one of the 43 `outcomes_valid`-joined consumers
  (`get_brier_over_time`, `brier_score_by_method`,
  `brier_score_by_method_rolling`, `brier_skill_score`, calibration
  training, etc.) already excludes automatically, with zero new code.
  Non-destructive and reversible -- rows remain as a forensic record,
  simply excluded from scoring. Verified the fix: W28 (100% synthetic)
  disappeared entirely from `get_brier_over_time()`'s output; `ensemble`
  method Brier dropped from the contaminated 0.3200 lifetime figure to a
  real 0.2681. Data-only fix -- no code changed, no commit.
  Note: W26/W27's real Brier (0.2678/0.2687) are both still above the 0.22
  threshold on genuine data, so the P10.3 alert may legitimately fire again
  next run -- that would be a real signal worth investigating on its own
  merits, not more contamination.

Why not now (resolved):
  - The specific contamination found is fully cleaned up. The general risk
    class -- ad-hoc debugging sessions writing directly to production DB
    files instead of an isolated/temp DB -- is NOT fixed by this entry and
    remains open; see note below.

When to revisit:
  - If a similar contamination is found a third time, especially one using
    a valid-looking ticker AND a plausible (non-impossible) settled_at --
    the impossible-timestamp signature that caught both this incident and
    KXBADDATE3 would NOT catch a more careful fabrication. Worth
    considering a lighter-weight guard (e.g. a `test_data` marker column,
    or a habit of always pointing ad-hoc investigative scripts at a copied
    DB) before a third occurrence.

[CLOSED 2026-07-12 -- see below] KALSHI ORDER-WRITE ENDPOINTS MOVING TO /portfolio/events/orders
Priority: was High -- verify before resuming live trading (~2026-07-30 return), not a
  someday item. Found 2026-07-10 via Kalshi's own API changelog; refined
  2026-07-10 via a second research pass (changelog re-fetch + independent
  third-party SDK docs cross-check, both agree).

RESOLVED 2026-07-12: Migrated place_order()/cancel_order() to POST/DELETE
  /portfolio/events/orders per the plan below (commit bc7e10c), then a
  second-opinion review found and fixed one real HIGH bug -- a successful
  POST followed by a failing get_order() follow-up could strand a live
  order under status="failed" with no poller ever picking it up again
  (commit 58a4e3b). 156+ tests pass, lint/mypy clean. This item is done;
  kept below for historical context on the migration decisions.

Problem:
  kalshi_client.py's live order-placement and order-cancellation code
  targets endpoints Kalshi is migrating off of. The split is "reads stay,
  writes move," not a wholesale change:
    - GET /portfolio/orders (kalshi_client.py:313, list resting/executed
      orders) and GET /portfolio/orders/{order_id} (kalshi_client.py:423,
      get single order) are UNAFFECTED -- reads stay on this path
      permanently per Kalshi's own docs.
    - POST /portfolio/orders (kalshi_client.py:364, place_order) and
      DELETE /portfolio/orders/{order_id} (kalshi_client.py:427,
      cancel_order) are the legacy WRITE endpoints being deprecated. The
      new V2 write endpoints are POST /portfolio/events/orders and
      DELETE /portfolio/events/orders/{order_id} (confirmed via both
      Kalshi's changelog and an independent third-party SDK
      -- github.com/TexasCoding/kalshi-python-sdk -- whose docs describe
      the identical old-path/new-path split).
  This is NOT just a URL rename: Kalshi's changelog describes the new V2
  write endpoints as using "a bid/ask single-book shape with fixed-point
  dollar prices and lightweight responses" -- a different request/response
  shape. The third-party SDK's docs show the new response includes
  order_id, remaining_count, fill_count, reduced_by, ts_ms -- diff this
  against what kalshi_client.py currently parses out of the old response
  before assuming the migration is small.
  Timeline: legacy write rate-limit costs escalated to 10x V2-equivalent by
  2026-06-04; deprecation was announced for "sometime between June 18 and
  June 25, 2026." No changelog entry confirms the deprecation was actually
  enforced/completed -- legacy writes may still work today, just at 10x
  rate-limit cost, with no confirmed grace period remaining. No real order
  has ever been placed by this bot yet (ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False), so this
  has not caused a live incident.

What the fix looks like:
  1. Quick check first: hit place_order/cancel_order against DEMO_BASE
     (https://demo-api.kalshi.co/trade-api/v2) and see whether they still
     succeed, return a deprecation error, or already 404/reject.
  2. Migrate kalshi_client.py's place_order (line 364) and cancel_order
     (line 427) to POST/DELETE /portfolio/events/orders[/{order_id}].
     Read Kalshi's live API reference for the exact current request body
     (fixed-point dollar prices, bid/ask single-book shape) and response
     field names before writing the migration -- do not assume the old
     request/response dict shape carries over unchanged.
  3. Leave the two GET /portfolio/orders* call sites (line 313, 423) alone
     -- they are not affected by this migration.
  4. While in there, evaluate the new orderbook_delta WebSocket
     get_snapshot action (see FEATURE CANDIDATES section below) since it's
     adjacent surface area.

Why not now (only reason to defer, not to skip):
  - TRADING_PAUSED=true and ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False mean nothing is
    currently broken in production -- but this should be resolved before
    either flag flips, not discovered live when it does.

When to revisit:
  - Before the Belgium trip ends (~2026-07-30) and live trading is
    considered for resumption. This is a hard prerequisite, not a nice-to-have.

[DEMO_BASE SMOKE TEST -- LIVE ORDER-EXECUTION PATH HAS NEVER BEEN FIRED AT A REAL EXCHANGE]
Priority: High -- hard prerequisite before ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE is ever flipped
  on. User confirmed Belgium return date 2026-07-31; TRADING_PAUSED=true
  lifting on that date is necessary but NOT sufficient for live trading --
  this is the actual remaining gate.

Problem:
  As of 2026-07-19, no order of any kind (real or demo) has ever been
  placed by this bot -- ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False and TRADING_PAUSED=true
  have been set for the entire time the live order-execution code has
  existed. Every session that touched kalshi_client.py's order-mutation
  methods (the V2 create/cancel migration, AMEND ORDER V2) explicitly
  flagged the same residual gap in its own resolution notes: implemented
  and unit-tested against Kalshi's documented request/response shapes
  (verified via live docs fetches), never verified against a real
  request/response round-trip. Kalshi's docs can describe a shape
  slightly wrong, or a real error response can have a shape the code
  doesn't handle the way a mocked test assumes -- the exact failure mode
  a smoke test exists to catch before it's a live-money incident. No
  demo API credentials are even configured in this environment currently
  (checked 2026-07-19: KALSHI_API_KEY_ID is blank; KALSHI_PRIVATE_KEY_PATH
  is set).

What it would look like:
  1. Provision/confirm demo API credentials (Kalshi's DEMO_BASE --
     https://demo-api.kalshi.co/trade-api/v2 -- is a separate account
     from prod, needs its own key pair).
  2. Against DEMO_BASE only, exercise the real round-trip for each
     order-mutation method that's never been live-tested:
     place_order() (a small resting GTC limit order on a real but
     inconsequential demo market), get_order() (confirm the response
     shape matches what place_order's follow-up call assumes),
     amend_order() (reprice the resting order, confirm remaining_count/
     fill_count/average_fill_price parse as expected),
     cancel_order() (confirm the resting order actually clears).
  3. Cross-check each real response against what kalshi_client.py/
     order_executor.py currently assume (field names, fixed-point
     dollar-string format, the count semantics AMEND ORDER V2's own
     resolution flagged -- "total desired fillable count," not "how
     many more").
  4. Only after this passes: consider flipping ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE for a
     real (small-stakes) live order, still gated behind TRADING_PAUSED
     being lifted and every other existing live-money gate
     (MAX_DAILY_SPEND, position limits, kill switch, etc.) untouched.

Why not now:
  - Requires the user physically present with demo credentials and
    deliberate attention on a real (if inconsequential) account action --
    not something to do unattended or as a background task. Also
    naturally batches with the Belgium-return timeline rather than being
    useful earlier (TRADING_PAUSED blocks live trading regardless of
    whether this passes).

When to revisit:
  - After 2026-07-31 (confirmed Belgium return), before ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE
    is ever flipped on. This is the literal next concrete step in the
    live-trading-resumption sequence: lift TRADING_PAUSED -> this smoke
    test -> ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE -> (separately, VM migration + headless
    trade-cycle engine work before any always-on continuous live watcher).

[RESOLVED 2026-07-12] MYSTERY REVERT -- COMMIT 24559a7 SILENTLY
  WIPED ~10 COMMITS OF CALIBRATION/SAFETY WORK UNDER AN UNRELATED COMMIT
  MESSAGE
Priority: Medium-High (a calibration-integrity safeguard has been silently
  missing for ~166 commits; not urgent since TRADING_PAUSED, but a real gap,
  not cosmetic)

PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-12: piece 1 of the restoration priority list below,
  disputed-outcome tracking, is done. Ported forward against current tracker.py
  (not a mechanical port of 31c7226's tracker.py diff -- the schema has grown
  from v23 to v38 since, with ~27 new calibration/Brier/bias/win-rate functions
  added that all needed the same treatment the original only gave to 3).
  Migration v38->v39 adds outcomes.disputed; mark_outcome_disputed()/
  get_disputed_count() added; audit_settlement() calls mark_outcome_disputed()
  on a genuine archive/Kalshi mismatch (matching the original). Surfaced a real
  scope question to the user first -- reproduce the original's 3-function scope
  faithfully, or audit and fix every current settled_yes-consuming function --
  user chose the full audit. Traced every JOIN outcomes / o.settled_yes site in
  tracker.py (33 total) and added disputed-row exclusion to all 30 that use
  settled_yes as a calibration/scoring ground truth; left unchanged (with
  reasoning, independently verified by the review below): the count_settled_*
  sample-size gates (matches the original's own unfiltered get_settled_count()
  precedent), get_history/get_outcome_for_ticker (display/lookup, not
  aggregate), backfill_emos_data/get_emos_training_data/
  get_recent_city_correlations (these train on settled_temp_f, the archived
  actual temperature -- the trusted value a dispute is raised AGAINST, not the
  suspect one), get_unselected_bias (different table, no disputed column), and
  the ensemble_member_scores-based model-accuracy functions (unrelated table).
  Also fixed two incidental dead-code-guard failures surfaced while running the
  full test sweep (unrelated to this piece but caught along the way): wired
  get_disputed_count() into web_app.py's /api/analytics dispatch, and
  allowlisted get_price_history() (from the prior candlesticks-capture session)
  with its own accurate deferred-consumer reason. ~380 lines of new tests
  (mechanism, audit_settlement wiring both paths, and a before/after
  disputed-exclusion test per touched function). Independently reviewed (Agent,
  opus) -- came back clean; the reviewer additionally mutation-tested by
  stripping all 30 filter lines from a scratch copy and confirming exactly 30
  test failures, proving the tests genuinely catch a missing filter rather than
  passing spuriously.

  Piece 2, climate-derived sigma, is also done (2026-07-12, same day).
  Restored climatology.py's compute_sigma_from_climate()/load_all_sigmas()
  against current code -- the original commit (ae86946) bundled this with an
  unrelated NBM-delta bias-correction change (piece 3, still open below);
  only the sigma half was ported this pass. get_historical_sigma() gained a
  var= parameter and now prefers the dynamic per-city/per-month value (from
  the already-cached 30yr climate archives) over the static _HISTORICAL_SIGMA
  table, closing the LV/NOLA sigma gap entry below as a side effect exactly
  as anticipated -- verified end-to-end against the real cached
  data/climate_LasVegas.json/data/climate_NewOrleans.json archives (both
  return sane per-month sigmas in the 1.5-5.5F range, no longer flat
  _DEFAULT_SIGMA=3.5). New autouse conftest.py fixture
  (isolate_dynamic_sigma) prevents the lazy module-global cache from writing
  to the real data/ directory during tests or breaking ~7 existing tests that
  assert exact static-table values -- defaults the dynamic path to
  unavailable per-test, matching this project's existing isolation-fixture
  pattern (neutral_temperature_scaling etc.). 22 new tests
  (tests/test_climatology.py + a new TestDynamicSigma class in
  test_gaussian_prob.py). Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- clean;
  reviewer additionally ran the restored function live against the real
  cached archives (not just mocked tests) to confirm the LV/NOLA payoff
  actually works, and confirmed no NBM-delta scope leaked in.

  Piece 3 (2026-07-12, same day) is now closed too -- all 4 of its
  sub-pieces got a real per-piece disposition rather than a batch port:
    - NBM-delta bias correction: CLOSED AS NOT NEEDED, not restored. Its
      entire premise ("GFS forecast minus NOAA's professionally
      bias-corrected NBM") is dead -- confirmed live against Open-Meteo
      (models=nbm and models=nbm_conus both 400 with "invalid String
      value") that NBM is no longer available there at all; the current
      fetch_temperature_nbm() already silently substitutes model="best_match"
      (an arbitrary, uncalibrated auto-selection), which would make the delta
      noise, not a bias signal. More importantly, it's superseded: this piece
      was built 2026-05-23, silently wiped 2026-05-26, and
      _get_combined_station_bias() (weather_markets.py) was built
      independently 2026-05-30 with no awareness NBM-delta had ever existed
      -- it corrects the bot's forecast toward real settled outcomes (dynamic
      METAR-learned bias, weight growing with sample count), a strictly
      better-grounded signal than correcting toward another model's guess
      ever was. User confirmed closing as not-needed rather than restoring.
    - Stop-loss accuracy tracking: DONE, but rebuilt against the current
      architecture, not ported mechanically. The original targeted
      tracker.live_fills, which today is a narrow slippage-only table
      (#P10.4) with zero rows ever, since no live order has been placed
      (ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False) -- auditing it would find nothing. The real
      settled stop-loss history lives in paper.py's trade ledger instead.
      close_paper_early() gained an optional reason= param, stored as
      exit_reason (separate from the existing outcome="early_exit" value so
      current semantics/tests are unchanged); cron.py's stop-loss call site
      (not its sibling breakeven-stop call site) now passes reason="stop_loss".
      tracker.get_stop_loss_accuracy(stop_loss_trades) takes pre-filtered
      paper trades and joins them against tracker.outcomes (excluding
      disputed rows, same as every other calibration consumer) -- the
      market still settles on Kalshi regardless of whether the bot's own
      position was closed early, so the real outcome is still recoverable.
      paper.get_stop_loss_accuracy() is a thin zero-arg wrapper (filters
      get_all_trades() to exit_reason=="stop_loss", hands them to tracker's
      join) wired into web_app.py's /api/analytics dispatch alongside its
      paper-module siblings (get_rolling_sharpe etc.) -- same
      wire-it-in-rather-than-leave-it-orphaned precedent as every other
      reporting function this session.
    - BETWEEN_FLOOR_MODEL_MAX env var: DONE. The 0.15 model-probability
      threshold was still hardcoded in weather_markets.py's between_floor
      gate; extracted to utils.BETWEEN_FLOOR_MODEL_MAX (default "0.15",
      no behavior change) and added to get_config_fingerprint() alongside
      every other env-configurable constant.
    - BETWEEN_FLOOR_MARKET_MIN env var: CLOSED, not applicable -- nothing
      left to extract. The gate's original "market > 0.30" condition (what
      this env var would have configured) was found buggy and deliberately
      redesigned away in a later fix, unrelated to this session (see the
      comment at weather_markets.py's between_floor gate: "The old condition
      (market > 0.30) was wrong... blocked profitable NO trades while never
      catching the suspicious YES case it was meant for"). The gate now
      compares against the live market price directly, not a hardcoded
      floor -- there's no static "0.30" left to make configurable.
    - Circuit-breaker threshold env-var overrides: CLOSED, not applicable --
      traced against the actual 24559a7 diff and found circuit_breaker.py
      was never one of the 9 files it touched at all. The only
      circuit-breaker-adjacent content that WAS lost (recovery_timeout=300
      settings on weather_markets.py's _ensemble_cb/_nbm_om_cb) is already
      present in current code. This backlog sub-item doesn't correspond to
      any real lost feature -- looks like a stale claim from the original
      research pass, not a genuine gap.

Problem:
  Found 2026-07-12 while investigating the LV/NOLA sigma backlog entry above.
  Commit 24559a7 (2026-05-26, "fix: handle str _date in signals_cache append
  (cron.py)") claims to be a 1-line cron.py fix. Its actual diff is

  Checked each lost piece against current HEAD (166 commits past 24559a7, as
  of 2026-07-12) to separate what's genuinely still gone from what got

  STILL MISSING AS OF THE ORIGINAL 2026-07-12 RESEARCH PASS (all resolved
  since -- see the piece 1/2/3 resolution notes above; kept for historical
  context on what was actually lost):
    - climatology.py's compute_sigma_from_climate()/load_all_sigmas() --
      derived per-city, per-month forecast sigma from a 30yr ERA5 reanalysis

    - Stop-loss accuracy tracking (tracker.py) -- was_stop_loss/

    - BETWEEN_FLOOR_MODEL_MAX/BETWEEN_FLOOR_MARKET_MIN env-var
      configurability for the 0.15/0.30 between-probability floor magic
      numbers (back to hardcoded).
    - Circuit-breaker threshold env-var overrides -- note circuit_breaker.py
      was later fully rebuilt from scratch in a 2026-07-11 session (see
      project memory), but that rebuild does not have env-var-configurable
      thresholds either, so this specific piece is still absent even though
      the file it belonged to has since been substantially rewritten.
    - Sigma-cache validation (_validate_sigma_cache(), warns on values
      outside [1.0, 20.0]F) -- moot on its own since the cache system it
      validated is itself gone; would come back for free if the sigma cache
      is rebuilt.

  CONFIRMED INDEPENDENTLY REAPPLIED SINCE (false alarms, do not re-do):
    - `unretire`/`unretire-strategy` CLI command (main.py) -- present.
    - MIN_BIAS_CORRECTION_TRADES env var + learned-weights TTL-warning
      suppression below that threshold -- present (weather_markets.py:172-173).
    - Gaussian sigma 1.5F effective floor -- present (weather_markets.py:5599).

  NOT re-verified in this pass (lower-value/cosmetic per the original
  31c7226 commit message, worth a quick check before restoring the rest but

  (Day-1 x0.50/Day-2 x0.70/Day-3+ x1.00 -- some horizon-discount concept

[RESOLVED 2026-07-20 -- Step 1 and Step 2 both shipped] HOURLY-DIRECTIONAL TEMPERATURE MARKETS — KXTEMPxxxH
Priority: was Low/Medium -- now Medium-High. Corrected volume data below
  changes the picture substantially from "one city has real live volume."

RESOLVED 2026-07-20 (Step 1 -- schema + safe discovery only, zero
  live-trading behavior change; Step 2, the real probability model, is
  scoped and deliberately deferred to its own future session -- see handoff
  at the end of this entry):
  Re-verified every claim in this entry against live state before touching
  anything, rather than trusting the 2026-07-08 snapshot. The volume
  picture had changed completely: querying Kalshi's API directly (not
  status=open snapshots, full history per series) found 5 of 7 cities
  (NYC, Austin, Chicago, LA, Washington DC) have run continuously and
  liquidly for ~60 days -- 93-99% of all listed hours have real volume,
  averaging 3,400-7,700 contracts/hour, comparable to or exceeding this
  bot's existing daily markets. Only Miami and Boston are genuinely
  unlaunched (near-zero markets ever listed). Volume is broad across the
  day in every city (peak/trough ratio only 4-8x), so no small subset of
  hours captures most of it by volume alone -- scoped instead to the ~2
  hours/city nearest the daily max/min, where existing same-day forecasting
  strength (proven on daily HIGH/LOW) most plausibly transfers, rather than
  all 24 hours (up to ~1,200 markets/day vs ~10-40 for the scoped version).

  Also found real hourly-aware scaffolding already existed and was unused:
  parse_city_date()/enrich_with_forecast() already parsed hourly tickers
  and extracted the hour; get_ensemble_temps()/_fetch_model_ensemble()/
  _get_consensus_probs() already accepted an hour= parameter with local-
  timezone awareness. Smaller build in places than this entry's "What the
  fix looks like" implied. One overclaim corrected: HRRR same-day fetch
  (_fetch_hrrr_temp) is NOT actually live for daily markets either --
  still zero production callers, deliberately left unwired per the
  2026-07-12 dead-code triage pending validation. Only METAR lock-in and
  the live persistence-probability override are genuinely live/reusable.

  Full implementation plan reviewed critically across several passes
  before any code was written (per explicit request) -- caught real gaps
  each pass, not just polish:
  - Wiring market discovery into the scan loop without also gating
    analyze_trade() would let an hourly market's title parse as an
    ordinary "above" condition and fall through into the full daily
    max/min model -- a live-money risk from what should be an inert first
    step.
  - A second, separate contamination path: compute_market_implied_
    distributions() groups by (city, target_date) independently of and
    before analyze_trade() -- an hourly bracket would get silently pooled
    into a daily market's event group and corrupt its distribution fit.
  - A third, found during implementation's own "quick check, not a
    blocking redesign" of find_violations()/the arb-check block: its
    (series, date_str) grouping key is day-level only (no hour), so two
    DIFFERENT hours' ladders for the same city/day would get compared for
    monotonicity as if they were one ladder. Mutation-tested and confirmed
    real -- produced a fabricated "IMPOSSIBLE" arbitrage violation with
    realistic inverted prices. Worse than the other two: find_violations()
    feeds directly into automatic corrective trading, not just a log-only
    signal.

  Shipped, all three fixed at the single-source-of-truth level (a new
  weather_markets._KXTEMP_HOURLY_CITY prefix->city dict, reused by all
  four sites below so they can't independently drift):
  - tracker.py: additive schema migrations v51/v52 (outcomes.settled_value
    REAL, outcomes.settled_var TEXT) -- the "NO MARKET-TYPE SEAM" entry's
    own prerequisite, now justified since a second market type is actually
    being greenlit. settled_temp_f untouched, no backfill (pre-migration
    rows can't be recovered, same reasoning as the v35 ensemble_member_
    scores.var precedent).
  - weather_markets.KNOWN_WEATHER_SERIES: added the 5 active KXTEMP*H
    series (Miami/Boston excluded -- re-check before adding, nothing will
    auto-alert if they activate since check_series_drift()'s KXHIGH/KXLOW
    -only filter doesn't cover this family, same blind spot it already
    accepts for KXRAIN/KXSNOW).
  - weather_markets._parse_city_from_ticker(): explicit KXTEMP*H prefix
    check ahead of the fragile substring chain -- LA and DC genuinely fail
    that chain entirely (LA needs "HIGHLA"/"LOWLA"/"LOWTLA"/an exact "LA"
    hyphen segment, none present in "KXTEMPLAXH"; DC needs "TDC", absent
    from "KXTEMPDCH"); NYC/Austin/Chicago pass today by substring luck.
  - weather_markets.analyze_trade(): returns None immediately for any
    KXTEMP*H ticker, checked by prefix before condition parsing, before
    every other existing gate. Counted via the existing _count_gate()
    mechanism, not a silent no-op.
  - weather_markets.compute_market_implied_distributions(): excludes
    KXTEMP*H before event-grouping, fixed inside the function itself so
    both real callers (cron.py, main.py) are covered.
  - consistency._group_markets(): same exclusion, protecting all 3 real
    find_violations() callers.
  - weather_markets.compute_hourly_temperature_proxy()/
    determine_hourly_target_hours(): new standalone, tested utility --
    infers each historical hour's true temperature from where a finalized
    ladder's result flips yes->no among strikes, averages per local hour
    across history, returns the empirical max/min-hour estimate. Not wired
    to gate anything yet (Step 2's job). Seasonal caveat noted in its own
    docstring: the ~60 days of history available today is all summer, so
    the derived hours are a summer-specific estimate, not permanent --
    re-derive periodically as more history accumulates across seasons.

  ~35 new tests (schema round-trip, city-parsing for all 5 real live
  tickers, all three guards including regression that existing daily/

RESOLVED 2026-07-20 (Step 2 -- real probability model, own settlement, own
  calibration pool, shadow-only rollout; all 7 handoff items above closed):
  Re-verified every handoff claim against live state before writing code:
  fresh determine_hourly_target_hours() (not the stale Step 1 snapshot) gave
  NYC max=14/min=6, Austin max=17/min=7, Chicago max=16/min=6, LA max=12/min=6,
  Washington max=15/min=6 -- confirmed the var-derivation bug still present
  at all 4 named sites plus a 5th related one (tracker.audit_settlement
  derives var from cond_type as a fallback, a different wrong-shape bug, not
  just a dangerous default). Root cause: no trade/prediction record stored
  `var` at all -- place_paper_order() had no var parameter -- so all 5 sites
  independently re-derived it from ticker text, which never matches
  KXTEMPxxxH tickers. User picked the root-cause fix (thread var end-to-end)
  over a narrow per-site patch, and cached-periodic (not per-scan) target-
  hour refresh over live-every-scan, given a full per-city history fetch is
  30k+ markets for NYC alone.

  Plan reviewed critically across 2 rounds (10 then 5 more passes) before any
  code was written -- each pass found real, substantive gaps: (1) the Step 1
  guard sat before EVERY other gate, so narrowing it in place and letting
  target-hour tickers "fall through" would skip liquidity/spread/price gates
  entirely for hourly markets -- fixed by keeping those gates in the path and
  adding the hourly branch point only after them; (2) tracing further found
  an UNCONDITIONAL call to _metar_lock_in() sitting between the extreme-price
  gate and the var-assignment point -- exactly the daily-running-max/min
  function item 7 warns must never touch an hourly ticker -- the branch point
  had to move to before that call, not after; (3) a second and third
  contamination risk found the same way: Phase C's NBM/ECMWF blend and
  get_historical_sigma(), neither hour-aware, sitting further down the same
  daily path -- confirmed the hourly model must be a genuinely separate
  function, not a patched-in-place daily fall-through; (4) discovered the
  daily path already had partial, never-finished hour-aware ensemble/EMOS
  logic (including an existing but unreachable "hourly_thin_ensemble" gate)
  worth extracting and reusing rather than reimplementing.

  Shipped:
  - predictions.var TEXT column (migration v53), populated once by
    log_prediction() from analysis["condition"]["var"] (both the INSERT and
    the ON CONFLICT...DO UPDATE clause -- a same-day re-scan must update var,
    not silently keep the first-ever value), read by all 5 buggy sites
    instead of re-deriving, with a legacy-row fallback to the old
    substring/cond_type derivation.
  - data/hourly_target_hours.json cache + weather_markets.
    refresh_hourly_target_hours()/get_hourly_target_hour_role(), mirroring
    check_series_drift()'s once-per-city-per-day gating, wired into cron.py.
    Live testing caught a real bug here: a transient fetch/parse hiccup
    could produce {"max_hour": None, "min_hour": None}, which the once-per-
    day gate would then lock in as "done for today" until tomorrow --
    fixed to skip caching (and thus skip the done-for-today gate) on a
    None/None result, since every city in this family is confirmed active
    and None/None is never a legitimate steady state.
  - analyze_trade()'s hourly branch: reuses the Step 1 ticker-prefix check,
    looks up the cached target-hour role, gates out immediately if not a
    target hour (new "hourly_not_target_hour" gate replacing Step 1's
    blanket "hourly_not_yet_supported"), otherwise falls through the full
    existing universal gate sequence (liquidity/spread/price/etc.) and
    branches to the new _analyze_hourly_trade() only after the extreme-price
    gate and before _metar_lock_in().
  - _analyze_hourly_trade(): hour+tz-aware ensemble fetch, per-city station-
    bias correction, persistence baseline (reused exactly as-is, item 7's
    hour-proximity gap deliberately still open), _price_and_size() for the
    shared entry-price/edge/Kelly tail (its 4th real caller). Two shared
    helpers -- _compute_ensemble_prob() and _compute_persistence_prob() --
    extracted from the daily path's own EMOS/Gaussian and persistence logic
    so daily and hourly can't independently drift on the numerically subtle
    parts; the daily path itself now calls these same functions, verified
    byte-for-byte behavior-preserving against the full daily regression
    suite. climatological_prob(), _metar_lock_in(), the Phase C NBM/ECMWF
    blend, get_historical_sigma(), and the model-consensus check are all
    deliberately never called from the hourly path (item 7's gaps, plus a
    newly-found one: _get_consensus_probs()'s hour= parameter is a cache-key-
    only no-op, the real fetch always requests daily data).
  - Hourly settlement: tracker._fetch_asos_observations() extracted from
    _fetch_asos_daily_temp() as a shared fetch/parse/local-day-filter core
    (confirmed byte-for-byte identical against the existing DST-edge-case
    test suite); new _fetch_asos_hour_temp() picks the METAR reading nearest
    the target local hour. audit_settlement() branches on the KXTEMPxxxH
    prefix before any daily-specific logic, writes settled_value/settled_var,
    leaves settled_temp_f NULL.
  - Separate 'hourly' pool in ml_bias.train_all_temperature_scaling() --
    own query (ticker-prefix filtered, days_out=0, correctly parenthesized:
    "AND (ticker LIKE ? OR ticker LIKE ? OR ...)" -- the missing-parens
    version would let SQL's AND-binds-tighter-than-OR silently leak
    non-days_out=0 rows in), own 20-sample gate, excluded from the existing
    'sameday' pool by ticker prefix (also correctly parenthesized).
    apply_temperature_scaling() gained a pool="hourly" parameter with the
    same no-fallback-to-other-pools shape as 'sameday'; existing callers
    (no pool arg) are unaffected.
  - Shadow-only rollout: weather_markets._hourly_gates_active() mirrors
    _below_gates_active() exactly (HOURLY_TRADING_ENABLED env var AND >=20
    settled hourly predictions, new tracker.count_settled_hourly_
    predictions()). Routing needed a genuinely new mechanism, not reuse of
    an existing one: today's shadow-vs-real decision is a whole-batch,
    whole-cycle choice keyed only on TRADING_PAUSED -- hourly markets must
    stay shadow-only independent of that flag (including after Belgium
    return lifts it) while daily markets in the same batch place normally,
    so order_executor._auto_place_trades() gained a new per-opportunity
    branch (inside the main loop, `continue`s past just that one
    opportunity) rather than a whole-batch early return.

  ~65 new tests across 6 files (schema/UPSERT round-trip, target-hour cache
  gating including the None/None-not-cached-as-done regression, the real
  hourly model's gate-ordering and _metar_lock_in-never-called safety checks

  shared helpers at their >=5/>=10 member-count boundaries and EMOS-vs-raw-

  sweep; ruff+mypy clean throughout.

  Live sanity check against Kalshi's real API (TRADING_PAUSED=true
  throughout): real fetch produced 3 real hourly analyses for LA markets at
  its live target hour (var=max, method=hourly_ensemble, plausible
  probabilities and side recommendations against real market prices), 40

  _hourly_gates_active() correctly read False (shadow-only, as expected pre-

  Independent review used 3 parallel opus (effort=high) agents, each scoped
  to a different third of the change, specifically to re-derive correctness
  from the actual code rather than trust this narrative. Two came back
  clean (one cosmetic stale test comment, fixed; one test-depth gap in the
  SQL-paren coverage, closed with a dedicated regression test proven to
  catch the exact mutation). The third found one real, substantive issue
  before the gate ever opens: _analyze_hourly_trade()'s consensus flag was
  computed as ensemble_prob-vs-blended_prob agreement, but blended_prob is
  85% ensemble_prob + 15% persistence -- so it would agree almost always,
  granting _price_and_size()'s consensus Kelly bonus (x1.25, raised cap) to
  the least-validated model on a near-tautological basis. Fixed to
  hardcoded False until a genuinely independent second source (NWS/
  climatology) supports hourly markets -- unlike precip/snow's consensus
  check, which genuinely compares 3 independent sources. Also flagged
  (accepted, matches item 7's already-documented deferred scope): persistence
  reuses the observed daily max for var="max" hourly markets, not an
  hour-H-specific reading -- a real semantic gap, but explicitly deferred by
  design, not a regression.

  When to revisit: this entry is now fully closed. Item 7's gaps remain
  intentionally open (metar-lock-in hour-analog, persistence hour-proximity
  weighting, hourly climatology, is_stale() threshold tuning) -- revisit
  once real hourly paper-trading data exists to judge them against, per
  item 7's own guidance. HOURLY_TRADING_ENABLED stays unset (shadow-only)
  until >=20 settled hourly predictions accumulate -- watch --auto's 5-
  minute cadence is far more likely to catch Kalshi's ~1-hour hourly-ladder
  window than the periodic cron/loop cadence (item 6); confirm actual
  catch-rate from real logs before judging how long that takes.

Original problem (kept for history):
  Kalshi's "Climate and Weather" category also lists an "Hourly Directional
  [City] Temperature" market family, structurally invisible to this bot:
  check_series_drift() only ever diffs KXHIGH*/KXLOW* prefixed series, so
  this family never surfaces as a gap no matter how much volume it gets.
  Confirmed live 2026-07-08: KXTEMPMIAH, KXTEMPBOSH, KXTEMPLAXH, KXTEMPCHIH,
  KXTEMPAUSH, KXTEMPDCH, KXTEMPNYCH all exist; only KXTEMPNYCH currently has
  open markets (24 of them, e.g. KXTEMPNYCH-26JUL0804-T76.99 -- an hourly
  threshold, not a daily high/low). The other 6 cities are dormant right now.

What the fix looks like:
  This isn't a ticker-list fix -- it needs a per-hour threshold-crossing
  probability model instead of the daily high/low ensemble blend this bot
  runs today. The good news: the same-day nowcasting infra this would lean
  on (live METAR observation override, persistence baseline, HRRR same-day
  fetch -- see analyze_trade()'s days_out==0 path in weather_markets.py, and
  cron.py's "Same-day markets... re-enabled" same-day trading logic) already
  exists and is live for daily markets, not still-deferred as an earlier
  version of this backlog entry assumed. Still needs new work though: the
  existing pipeline reasons about "will today's high/low cross X," not
  "will the temp at hour H cross X" -- the per-hour target and the shorter
  settlement window are a real design difference, not just reused as-is.

  Calibration follows the same precedent already established for same-day
  vs multi-day: ml_bias.train_all_temperature_scaling() fits a dedicated
  'sameday' T from days_out=0 rows only, with apply_temperature_scaling()
  enforcing zero fallback to the global/multi-day T (their probability
  distributions are too different to share a scale -- see commit chain
  c773474 -> 9f5bb40, 2026-06-02/05). An hour-level model needs the same
  treatment: its own training pool and its own T, not folded into either
  the daily same-day pool or the multi-day pool. Don't assume the existing
  'sameday' calibration path could just absorb hourly rows -- it can't
  without the same care taken to keep the pools separate.

Why not now (superseded -- both conditions below have since fired, see
  RESOLVED note above):
  - No existing model for the hour-level target specifically (only daily).
  - Only 1 of 7 cities in this family is currently even active.
  - Worth confirming KXTEMPxxxH volume is durable (not a one-off) before
    investing in an hour-level model.

When to revisit: N/A -- both Step 1 and Step 2 resolved. See the Step 2
  RESOLVED note above's "When to revisit" for the remaining intentionally-
  deferred gaps (item 7) and the shadow-gate sample-floor condition.

[PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-21 — Rain Step 1+2 shipped, snow/hurricane/St. Petersburg still open] RAIN / SNOW / HURRICANE MARKETS — UNTOUCHED CATEGORY SURFACE
Priority: was Low -- rain is now Medium-High (real, currently-liquid product
  the bot was silently blind to); snow/hurricane/rain's own probability
  model (Step 2) remain Low, unchanged.

Problem:
  "Climate and Weather" has 287 series total; this bot only ever looks at
  ~45 of them (KXHIGH*/KXLOW*, 20 tracked cities). Live-checked 2026-07-08:
  16 KXRAIN* city series exist, 2 currently with real open volume
  (KXRAINDENM -- Denver rain, 7 open markets; KXRAINSTPM, 7 open markets);
  ~23 snow series and ~40 hurricane series (path/category/landfall by city)
  exist but were all dormant/closed at check time. Separately, a handful of
  real weather markets (RAINNYC, KXRAINMIA, KXRAINNOSB) live entirely
  outside the "Climate and Weather" category (filed under "World"), so even
  widening check_series_drift's prefix filter within that one category
  wouldn't catch those.

What the fix looks like:
  Not a ticker-coverage fix -- each market type needs its own forecasting
  model with no shared architecture with the temperature-ensemble blend
  this bot runs today: precipitation-probability modeling for rain,
  snowfall-total modeling for snow, storm-track/intensity modeling for
  hurricanes. Treat as three separate potential product lines, not one
  task. If ever prioritized, rain is the most promising starting point --
  it already has real live volume (Denver/St. Paul) and precip-probability
  modeling is a smaller lift than storm-tracking.

Why not now:
  - No existing model architecture for any of the three.
  - Effort scales per market type, not incrementally with the current bot.
  - check_series_drift()'s KXHIGH*/KXLOW*-only filter is a deliberate
    simplification of an already-noisy check; widening it without picking
    a market type to actually act on would just add more unactionable noise.

When to revisit:
  - If there's real appetite to add a new market type (not just "cover more
    tickers") -- start with rain given current live volume.

  STEP 2 HANDOFF (separate future session, own plan + review -- do not
  build speculatively without re-checking these first):
  1. Real monthly-accumulation probability model in analyze_trade(),
     replacing today's unconditional None-return guard for KXRAIN*M
     tickers. No data provider gives monthly exceedance probability
     directly (confirmed this session against every provider this bot
     already uses) -- the model is a synthesis job, not a fetch. Recommended
     combo, researched and partly live-verified this session: NOAA ACIS
     StnData (`http://data.rcc-acis.org/StnData`, POST JSON, `elems:
     [{"name":"pcpn","interval":"dly"/"mly","duration":"dly"/"mly",
     "reduce":"sum"}]`, unauthenticated public API, this bot has never
     touched it) for (a) real month-to-date actual precip and (b) 30yr daily
     history to build an empirical per-city-month distribution of
     "remaining-days-of-month total" (bootstrap from historical years' D-to-
     month-end sums, not a parametric fit -- precip totals are right-skewed
     and bounded at 0), combined with the known actual-to-date value.
     Optionally tilt with Open-Meteo's Seasonal API (`seasonal-api.
     open-meteo.com/v1/seasonal`, `monthly=precipitation_mean`, ECMWF SEAS5,
     live-tested this session and confirmed working) as a directional nudge
     -- mean-only, no per-member spread, so it can adjust central tendency
     but can't itself supply distribution shape. NOAA CPC's monthly precip
     outlook (`mapservices.weather.noaa.gov/.../cpc_mthly_precip_outlk`) is
     categorical/tercile only, not a numeric CDF -- secondary signal at most,
     don't plan around it as a primary source. `_fetch_ensemble_precip`
     (existing single-day fetcher) is only practical for the final ~2 weeks
     of a month (16-day forecast cap) -- not a monthly solution on its own.
  2. Fix `_parse_market_condition()`'s real, currently-deferred bug: for
     KXRAIN*M tickers it silently collapses all 7 (or 4, NYC) ladder rungs
     into one identical `{"type": "precip_any"}`, discarding the real
     per-bracket threshold -- which lives in Kalshi's own `floor_strike`/
     `yes_sub_title`/`strike_type` market fields (confirmed via live raw
     JSON dump this session), NOT in a `-P<n>` ticker suffix or "inch" text
     in the title (real title is just "Rain in Denver in Jul 2026?"). Must
     be fixed before or alongside item 1 -- the model needs the real
     threshold to compare against.
  3. MANDATORY before any monthly-rain prediction/trade is ever logged: the
     position-sizing fail-open gap found this session. `MAX_CITY_DATE_
     EXPOSURE`/correlated-city penalties (paper.portfolio_kelly_fraction,
     order_executor.py's per-date cap) both key off `target_date_str` being
     a single-day string and silently skip when it's None -- which it
     always is for these tickers (no day component to parse). Once Step 2
     gives these tickers a real (non-None) grouping key, decide deliberately
     how monthly rain positions should be capped (extend the exposure system
     to accept a month-string key, treat the bracket's month as a synthetic
     date, or something else) -- don't let this silently start bypassing the
     caps just because target_date_str stops being None.
  4. Ladder/sibling grouping: `compute_market_implied_distributions()`'s
     current blanket exclusion needs to become real (city, month) grouping.
     `fit_market_implied_distribution()`'s weighted-least-squares machinery
     was confirmed this session to be structurally reusable (works off
     generic (lo, hi, mid_price, weight) tuples) but needs new sigma sanity
     bounds for an inches scale -- current bounds (0.1-50.0) are tuned for
     °F. NYC's ladder has only 4 brackets (not 7, a Kalshi listing choice,
     confirmed via settled history) -- handle variable ladder sizes.
  5. Settlement: `outcomes.settled_value` (float) is reusable for the
     monthly cumulative total, but `settled_var`'s existing semantic (a
     max/min-hour discriminator, from the hourly work) doesn't map cleanly
     onto "this is a monthly total" -- needs a new sentinel value or its own
     column, a real design decision, not a free reuse. `tracker.
     audit_settlement()` currently bails via `_parse_city_date()` returning
     None before reaching any settlement logic -- monthly rain needs its own
     settlement path triggered at month-end, not the "call once near a known
     instant" shape used for daily/hourly (a month's total is only final
     after the month ends, not observable at one point in time the way a
     daily high or an hourly reading is).
  6. Consensus-bonus precedent to follow, not rediscover: hourly Step 2's
     independent review caught that `_analyze_hourly_trade()`'s `consensus`
     flag was near-tautological (its two inputs weren't independent enough
     to justify `_price_and_size()`'s Kelly bonus) and had to be hardcoded
     `False` with a documented reason. A monthly-rain model will face the
     identical question the moment it has more than one signal (e.g. the
     ACIS-empirical estimate vs. the Seasonal-API-tilted one) -- verify real
     independence before wiring any consensus bonus, don't assume it.
  7. Shadow-only rollout: same `_gates_active()` pattern as every other new
     signal in this file (env var + sample-count floor via a new tracker
     count function) -- do not enable real sizing until enough settled
     monthly-rain predictions exist to validate real edge.
  8. Open question, not yet resolved: which NWS station does each city's
     rain market actually settle against. The pattern observed this session
     (Seattle=CLISEA, Denver implied CLIDEN, St. Petersburg=CLISPG) looks
     like the same per-city station this bot's temperature markets already
     use, but verify against each market's real `rules_secondary` text
     before assuming `metar.MARKET_STATION_MAP` transfers as-is -- don't
     guess.
  9. Snow and hurricane are separate, still fully open items (see this
     entry's own "Why not now" above) -- re-scout snow Nov-Mar, hurricane's
     per-city landfall markets Aug-Oct, before assuming either is ready.

  Independent Agent(opus, effort=high) review before push found one real
  MEDIUM adjacency bug, contradicting this entry's own "no changes needed,
  fully model-name-agnostic" framing for the two aggregate weight functions:
  introducing a brand-new, initially-thin model name into
  ensemble_member_scores perturbs BOTH downstream weight-learning aggregates,
  which treat "whatever model names are present" generically but gate on
  ALL of them together, not per-model. (1) weather_markets._weights_from_mae()
  (feeds _model_weights()'s ensemble-blend tier 1) used a GLOBAL (not
  per-city) all-or-nothing `return None` the moment ANY tracked model
  anywhere had fewer than min_n observations -- worse than the reviewer
  first described (per-city), confirmed by re-reading get_member_accuracy():
  `n = stats["n"]` is a global row count. This meant onboarding
  ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble would have silently disabled icon/gfs's MAE-based
  weighting for EVERY city until ECMWF alone crossed 20 global observations.
  Fixed: skip the thin model, keep computing real weights for the rest
  (strictly improving, no pre-existing-behavior change -- previously ANY
  thin model already fully blocked everything, so this only ever unblocks
  cases that were already broken). Mutation-tested (reverted to `return
  None`, confirmed the new regression test fails with exactly the predicted
  symptom, restored). (2) tracker.get_model_weights() (feeds
  _forecast_model_weights()'s daily-blend tier 1) had a documented "any thin
  model -> equal weight for all" fallback -- a genuine design call, not just
  a bug, since fixing it changes pre-existing 2-model semantics too (e.g.
  today's rare case of one of icon/gfs being thin while the other isn't).
  Presented 3 options via AskUserQuestion (exclude thin models from the
  softmax entirely / grandfather icon+gfs and gate only over legacy models /
  leave as-is and just document); user picked excluding thin models
  (rejected grandfathering as permanent hardcoded-model-list debt matching a
  pattern this codebase has been burned by before -- mos.py's city list,
  the metar.py duplicate dict; rejected leave-as-is since the bug is
  directly caused by this diff and well-scoped to fix, not "massively out
  of scope"). Fixed the same way as (1): a model below MIN_OBSERVATIONS=10
  is excluded from the softmax, not equal-weighted alongside proven models.
  Updated tests/test_signal_quality.py's test_insufficient_observations_
  returns_equal_weights (renamed, rewritten for the new "all thin -> {}"
  behavior) and added a new one-thin-one-not test proving the well-observed
  model gets full weight, not a diluted split. Mutation-tested the same way.
  946 tests pass across the widened sweep (adds test_signal_quality.py,
  test_phase4.py, test_tracker.py to the file list above); ruff+mypy clean
  after this follow-up too.
  ecmwf_ifs025 (the daily-blend product, still unconsequential-to-instrument
  per this entry's original "more consequential" framing) remained
  un-instrumented as of this point in the session.
  Won't pay off in an actual learned weight for weeks: needs >=10 fresh
  settled observations per city in tracker.get_model_weights()'s 30-day
  window (same MIN_OBSERVATIONS gate icon/gfs already use), and TRADING_PAUSED
  is still true as of this session (Belgium return 2026-07-31) so real
  paper-trade volume needed to fill that window hasn't been accruing.

Original problem (resolved, kept for history):
  ECMWF's per-model forecast accuracy is never captured anywhere, so it can
  never earn a learned weight the way icon_seamless/gfs_seamless can.
  paper.py's _score_ensemble_members() only ever logs icon_forecast_mean and
  gfs_forecast_mean to tracker.ensemble_member_scores (see the comment left
  in model_means there) -- no ecmwf_forecast_mean field exists anywhere in
  the trade-entry -> settlement -> scoring pipeline. _forecast_model_weights()
  and _model_weights() (weather_markets.py) both correctly fall back to a
  static seasonal default for ECMWF forever, since the tracker data that
  would let them do better structurally can't exist yet.

  Note there are TWO separate ECMWF products in play, tracked independently:
  ecmwf_ifs025 (deterministic, used by the daily 3-model blend in
  get_weather_forecast()) and ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble (ML ensemble, used by
  get_ensemble_temps()'s probability blend). Fixing one does NOT give the
  other a learned weight -- they're unrelated model runs on different
  Open-Meteo endpoints (FORECAST_BASE vs ENSEMBLE_BASE).

What the fix looks like:
  1. Decide which ECMWF product to instrument first. Recommend ecmwf_ifs025
     (the daily-blend one) since that's the one that was actually silently
     dropped from fetches until the 2026-07-07 fix (commit 5a3d80b) -- it's
     the more consequential of the two for real trade decisions.
  2. Add an ecmwf_forecast_mean field and thread it through the same path
     icon_forecast_mean/gfs_forecast_mean already take: weather_markets.py's
     analyze_trade() (near _get_consensus_probs(), ~line 4478) -> the analysis
     dict returned to callers -> order_executor.py/main.py's calls into
     paper.open_paper_trade(...) -> paper.py's trade schema -> finally added
     to _score_ensemble_members()'s model_means dict (~paper.py:1153 as of
     2026-07-10).
  3. _get_consensus_probs() (weather_markets.py ~line 4274 as of
     2026-07-10) currently only
     calls its generic, model-agnostic _model_prob_and_mean() helper for
     "icon_seamless" and "gfs_seamless". Extending it for
     ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble would be mechanically easy (same ENSEMBLE_BASE/
     _ensemble_cache infrastructure already used there). Extending it for
     ecmwf_ifs025 instead requires NEW plumbing mirroring this pattern
     against FORECAST_BASE, since that's a different endpoint entirely --
     don't assume this is a one-line change once ecmwf_ifs025 is picked.
  4. Redesign the currently-binary model_consensus check
     (abs(icon_p - gfs_p) > 0.12) for 3 models -- decide between an
     all-pairwise-agreement check or a max-min-spread check. This is a real
     design decision, not just plumbing -- don't rush it.
  5. Once the field exists, add "ecmwf_ifs025": trade.get("ecmwf_forecast_mean")
     to _score_ensemble_members()'s model_means dict.

Why not now:
  - The urgent bug (ECMWF silently excluded from live fetches) is already
    fixed and does not depend on this -- ECMWF now always gets fetched with
    a reasonable seasonal-default weight regardless.
  - This is new instrumentation across ~4 files, not a bug fix -- meaningfully
    more invasive than the fetch-list fix.
  - Won't pay off for weeks even after shipping: needs 10+ fresh settled
    trades per city (same MIN_OBSERVATIONS/min_n gates icon/gfs already use)
    before the learned weight would ever activate.
  - Requires a real design decision (which ECMWF product, how to redesign the
    3-way consensus check) that deserves its own scoping pass, not a
    rushed addition to an unrelated bug-fix session.

When to revisit (ecmwf_ifs025 only -- ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble is done, see
  above):
  - Have bandwidth for a multi-file instrumentation change, not a quick fix
    (though smaller than this note originally implied -- model_temps["ecmwf"]
    in analyze_trade() is already the fetched value, no new plumbing needed).
  - Feeds _forecast_model_weights()'s daily blend, a different/more
    consequential consumer than ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble's _model_weights()
    (get_ensemble_temps() pipeline), so still worth doing even though the
    aifs025 product is now covered.

[3-WAY MODEL_CONSENSUS CHECK -- ECMWF_AIFS025_ENSEMBLE'S PROBABILITY ISN'T WIRED IN YET]
Priority: Low (the underlying weight-learning field is done; this is a
  trade-quality-gate refinement, not a correctness bug)

Problem:
  analyze_trade()'s model_consensus check (weather_markets.py, the
  "Model consensus check" block) is still the original binary
  abs(icon_p - gfs_p) > 0.12 comparison -- it does not consider
  ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble at all, even though _get_consensus_probs() now
  fetches that model's mean via the same _model_prob_and_mean() helper used
  for icon/gfs (2026-07-23, see the resolved TRACK ECMWF FORECAST ACCURACY
  entry above). _model_prob_and_mean() computes a real member-vote-fraction
  probability for ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble as a side effect of computing its
  mean -- _get_consensus_probs() just doesn't return it yet (deliberately
  scoped out of the 2026-07-23 session, at the user's explicit choice, to
  keep that session to "ship the weight-learning field only").

What the fix looks like:
  1. Extend _get_consensus_probs()'s return tuple with ecmwf_prob (cheap --
     _model_prob_and_mean("ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble") already computes it,
     currently discarded via `_, ecmwf_mean = ...`).
  2. Decide how to fold a 3rd probability into model_consensus. Note this is
     NOT purely mechanical: icon_p/gfs_p are real member-vote-fraction
     probabilities from live multi-member ensembles (same methodology,
     directly comparable). ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble's probability, once wired
     in, WOULD also be a genuine member-vote-fraction probability from the
     same ENSEMBLE_BASE infrastructure -- so unlike the ecmwf_ifs025
     alternative (which has no members at all, only a single deterministic
     point value), a 3-way check here IS apples-to-apples methodologically.
     Still a real design decision: all-pairwise-agreement (max spread across
     all 3 pairs) vs. a simpler max-min-spread check across all 3 probs.

Why not now:
  - Deliberately deferred by explicit user decision on 2026-07-23 to keep
    that session scoped to the weight-learning field alone.
  - Changes live trade-gating behavior (model_consensus feeds
    "near_threshold"/downstream Kelly-adjacent signals) -- deserves its own
    scoping pass, not a rider on an unrelated instrumentation change.

When to revisit:
  - Whenever model_consensus's trade-quality signal is next being tuned, or
    once enough settled ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble observations exist to know
    whether its member-vote probability actually disagrees with icon/gfs in
    a way worth gating on (rather than guessing at the 3-way threshold blind).

[CLOSED 2026-07-12 -- evaluated live, not switching] OPEN-METEO ENSEMBLE MEAN
  API -- SIMPLER/CHEAPER THAN CURRENT MEMBER-BY-MEMBER FETCH
Priority: was Medium (efficiency + data-quality improvement, not a bug fix)

CLOSED 2026-07-12: made live test calls to the actual endpoint (not just docs)
  and found three real blockers, not one:
  1. Daily spread does not exist as a variable at all -- requesting
     temperature_2m_max_spread (or any daily _spread variant) 400s with
     "Cannot initialize ForecastVariableDaily from invalid String value."
     Spread is HOURLY-ONLY. Since this bot needs daily-high/low uncertainty,
     using this API would mean fetching hourly spread and picking the value
     near the forecast daily max/min hour -- reintroducing complexity, not
     eliminating it. Not the "get uncertainty for free" win it looked like.
  2. Spread comes back in Kelvin-degrees (hourly_units reports
     "temperature_2m_spread":"K") even when temperature_unit=fahrenheit is
     explicitly requested -- the mean value correctly converts to F, spread
     does not. A Kelvin-degree spread is NOT numerically equal to a
     Fahrenheit-degree spread; using it unconverted as sigma in
     gaussian_probability() would silently understate uncertainty by ~44%
     (missing x1.8 factor). Easy to get wrong silently.
  3. ECMWF AIFS mean (ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble_mean) returned null for daily
     max/min at the one live test point (NYC) -- same failure mode already
     documented in this repo's fetch_temperature_ecmwf() comments for the
     deterministic endpoint.
  Also re-confirmed and corrected the model-name guess yet again on live
  verification: ICON mean is dwd_icon_eps_ensemble_mean_seamless, GFS mean is
  ncep_gefs_ensemble_mean_seamless (NOT gfs_ensemble_seamless_mean -- GFS's
  ensemble is branded GEFS at Open-Meteo, guessing wrong 400s), ECMWF AIFS
  mean is ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble_mean (NOT ecmwf_aifs_025_ensemble_mean).
  Verdict: not a clean drop-in win as originally framed. Closing rather than
  leaving open-ended -- if ever revisited, it needs to solve the
  hourly-only-spread problem first, which is real added complexity, not a
  simplification.

Problem:
  Open-Meteo launched an Ensemble Mean API in March 2026 that returns mean
  and spread (standard deviation) directly per ensemble model, computed
  server-side from individual members. This bot's current approach
  (weather_markets.py's _model_prob_and_mean()/get_ensemble_temps(), used
  for icon_seamless/gfs_seamless and, per the TRACK ECMWF entry above,
  potentially ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble) fetches every individual ensemble
  member and computes mean/spread itself. Found 2026-07-10 via web search,
  not yet verified against the live Open-Meteo endpoint or this repo's
  actual fetch code in detail.

UPDATE 2026-07-12 (research pass, no code changed):
  Re-confirmed weather_markets.py's current fetch approach is still
  accurate as described above -- get_ensemble_temps() (weather_markets.py:2933)
  still calls _fetch_model_ensemble() per model and builds all_temps itself;
  no change since 2026-07-10.
  Confirmed via 2 independent fetches of open-meteo.com/en/docs/ensemble-mean-api
  that the endpoint is real:
  base URL https://ensemble-api.open-meteo.com/v1/ensemble, daily variables
  temperature_2m_max/temperature_2m_min are supported, response shape is
  {variable} for mean + {variable}_spread for std-dev, data retained since
  March 2026 (individual members only kept 3 days, so the mean/spread
  series is also the only way to get real historical ensemble data beyond
  that window -- a second reason to care about this beyond raw efficiency).
  IMPORTANT correction to the original note: the `models` parameter uses
  DIFFERENT string values than the raw per-member API this bot calls today
  -- e.g. `ecmwf_aifs_025_ensemble_mean` (mean API) vs this bot's
  `ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble` (raw API, note both the underscore placement and
  the "_mean" suffix differ), and `gfs_ensemble_seamless_mean` vs
  `gfs_seamless`. This is not a drop-in endpoint swap with the same model
  identifiers -- confirm the exact spelling with one live test call before
  writing any code, not from docs-summary text alone (same caution that
  mattered for the Kalshi V2 order-endpoint migration this session).

(Original "what the fix looks like" section removed 2026-07-12 -- superseded
  by the CLOSED verdict above, which found 3 real blockers a simple
  model-name fix wouldn't address.)

[CLOSED 2026-07-12 -- not currently achievable, see below] CLIMATE INDEX
  TABLES (AO/NAO/ENSO) MISSING 10 OF 20 CITIES
Priority: was Low (signal degradation, safe-side default fallback already in
  place)

CLOSED 2026-07-12: two findings that together make this not a boundedly-
  scoped task right now, not just a low-priority one.
  First, git-archaeology on climate_indices.py (git log -p on the file, only
  7 commits total) found the ao_sens/nao_sens/enso_sens dicts for the
  ORIGINAL 10 cities appear once, in the very first commit, and have never
  been modified since. No docstring, comment, docs/ file, or commit message
  anywhere references a study, NOAA regression, or any data source -- unlike
  _PDO_TEMP_COEFF/_PNA_TEMP_COEFF's explicit scoping comments nearby. These
  read as plausible hand-authored estimates from initial repo creation, not
  values derived from any real analysis -- so "follow whatever methodology
  produced the first 10" (the fix this entry originally proposed) has no
  methodology to follow.
  Second, even if a real regression were attempted from scratch: queried
  data/predictions.db's outcomes table for settled_temp_f coverage -- 231
  total rows, spanning only 2026-05-19 to 2026-07-09 (under 8 weeks, one
  season, ZERO winter data). AO/NAO effects are largest in winter, which is
  exactly the regime this window can't see. Per-city counts are 3-14 rows
  even for the best-covered cities. A regression against monthly AO/NAO/ONI
  values with this little same-season data would be statistically
  meaningless -- and wouldn't even be reproducible for the original 10
  cities using this repo's own data, let alone extendable to 10 more.
  Verdict: a real, data-backed fix needs decades of external per-city
  historical daily temperature (NOAA GHCN/CLI archives) regressed against
  NOAA CPC's public AO/NAO/ONI series -- genuine external research, not
  something derivable from what's in this repo today. The only thing
  achievable right now is extending the same unscientific hand-authored-
  estimate pattern the original 10 already use, which would be internally
  consistent with the file's actual origin but shouldn't be presented as a
  data-driven fix. Closing rather than leaving open-ended; revisit only if
  someone is willing to do the external research this actually requires.

Problem:
  climate_indices.py's ao_sens/nao_sens/enso_sens dicts inside
  temperature_adjustment() (climate_indices.py:212-251) only have the
  original 10 cities (NYC, Boston, Chicago, Miami, LA, Dallas, Phoenix,
  Seattle, Denver, Atlanta) -- none of the 10 cities added later to
  CITY_COORDS (Austin, Washington, Philadelphia, OklahomaCity, SanFrancisco,
  Minneapolis, Houston, SanAntonio, LasVegas, NewOrleans) appear. Confirmed
  this isn't an intentionally-scoped subset the way _PDO_TEMP_COEFF/
  _PNA_TEMP_COEFF (climate_indices.py:354-367) explicitly are (those have
  inline comments restricting them to "west-coast cities" / "central and
  eastern US", and the caller documents the scoping) -- no such comment
  exists for ao_sens/nao_sens/enso_sens. temperature_adjustment() is called
  unconditionally for every city in analyze_trade() (weather_markets.py:5550),
  silently falling back to generic sensitivities (.get(city, 0.5) etc.,
  climate_indices.py:253-255) for the 10 newer cities -- half the tracked
  roster gets untuned AO/NAO/ENSO adjustments.

(Original "what the fix looks like" section removed 2026-07-12 -- superseded
  by the CLOSED verdict above, which found no real methodology exists to
  follow and no data currently exists to build one from scratch.)

  class)

RESOLVED 2026-07-12 (second pass, same day): all 6 fields now have a real
  decision, not just documentation. max_city_date_exposure, method_kelly_gate,

  in paper.py (MAX_CITY_DATE_EXPOSURE=0.25, _METHOD_MIN_SAMPLES=50) and
  main.py (guaranteed_edge < 0.05) were moved into utils.py as real

  config.py's fields derive their defaults from utils.py via new

  functions (same pattern as _live_max_days_out). kelly_cap was similarly
  consolidated (_live_kelly_cap()) so its two independently-hardcoded "0.25"
  literals can't diverge later, even though it was already safety-netted.
  min_kelly_fraction and partial_exit_pct -- confirmed still zero consumers
  anywhere -- were deleted from BotConfig entirely (plus partial_exit_pct's
  validate() check), rather than inventing unspecified trading semantics.
  _DEAD_FIELD_ALLOWLIST in tests/test_config_divergence_guard.py updated to
  match: the 3 "misleading" entries became "enforced via utils.X" entries
  (like breakeven_trigger_pct), and the 2 unimplemented entries were removed
  along with their fields. Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- no bugs
  found, all three live-value literals confirmed exact matches to prior
  hardcoded behavior. Pushed together with the dead-code-scan work below.

UPDATE 2026-07-12 (documented + guarded, NOT wired/deleted): re-verified all
  5 fields live while building tests/test_config_divergence_guard.py (see
  the NO AUTOMATED GUARD entry above). One correction to the KELLY_CAP claim
  below: it's stale -- utils.py's KELLY_CAP is now os.getenv-backed (fixed
  in an earlier 2026-07-11 session, `float(os.getenv("KELLY_CAP", "0.25"))`)
  -- so it's no longer "not even os.getenv-backed", it's just still a
  SEPARATE env read from config.py's own kelly_cap field (same default,
  coincidentally, so no live divergence -- but still two independently
  hardcoded "0.25" literals that could diverge later). All 5 fields (plus a
  6th found the same way: max_days_out, which WAS a live divergence --
  "3" vs "5" -- fixed same session) are now individually documented with a
  concrete reason in _DEAD_FIELD_ALLOWLIST, and the new guard test would
  catch either field silently going MORE wrong (a value mismatch) even
  though it doesn't fix the "config field lies about being configurable"
  problem itself. The actual "wire up or delete" decision for all 5 is
  still not made -- still needs the dedicated pass described below.

Problem:
  Following the same config.py/utils.py divergence pattern already found
  and fixed 3 times in this project (BREAKEVEN_TRIGGER_PCT,
  MAX_SAME_DAY_SPEND, PAPER_MIN_EDGE), grepped every BotConfig field name
  across the whole codebase (excluding config.py/utils.py/tests/) and found
  5 more fields that are parsed from env but never actually read by real
  trading logic:
    - KELLY_CAP (config.py:201) -- the real cap enforced everywhere
      (paper.py:634,1532; weather_markets.py:4360) is utils.py:64's
      hardcoded KELLY_CAP=0.25, which isn't even os.getenv-backed (its own
      comment says "Operative production cap is 0.25"). The env var is
      fully inert on top of an already-inert config field.
    - MAX_CITY_DATE_EXPOSURE (config.py:216-218) -- the real cap enforced
      in paper.py:1390-1408 is a separate hardcoded module constant of the
      same name, paper.py:161 (=0.25). Setting the env var has zero effect.
    - METHOD_KELLY_GATE (config.py:213-215) -- the real per-method Kelly
      gate is a hardcoded local _METHOD_MIN_SAMPLES=50 in paper.py:517-527,
      unrelated to this field/env var.
    - MIN_ARB_EDGE (config.py:226-228) -- STALE CLAIM CORRECTED 2026-07-10:
      arb auto-placement HAS since been built (main.py's _analyze_once arb
      block, ~main.py:1542-1660, paper-only, with volume gates + $25
      per-city exposure cap + live-gate check) -- but it gates on a
      HARDCODED `v.guaranteed_edge < 0.05` (main.py:1602), not the config
      field. So MIN_ARB_EDGE (default 0.03) is still fully inert, and the
      fix is now trivial: replace the hardcoded 0.05 with the config field
      (deciding deliberately whether 0.03 or 0.05 is the right default).
    - min_kelly_fraction (config.py:202-204) -- no Kelly-sizing code
      anywhere references a minimum-fraction floor.

What the fix looks like:
  For each: either wire the config field into the real enforcement point
  (replacing the hardcoded constant), or delete the dead field/env var if
  it's not actually wanted. MIN_ARB_EDGE and min_kelly_fraction may be
  genuinely unimplemented features rather than divergence bugs (no
  hardcoded shadow value exists for them, unlike the other 3) -- worth
  distinguishing "should wire this up" from "should delete this" per field
  rather than treating all 5 identically.

Why not now:
  - Not urgent: the real values enforced today (utils.py's KELLY_CAP=0.25,
    paper.py's MAX_CITY_DATE_EXPOSURE=0.25) are reasonable production
    values -- this is a "the env var lies about being configurable"
    problem, not a "wrong value in production" problem.
  - 5 fields is enough scope to warrant a dedicated pass rather than a
    drive-by fix, similar to how PAPER_MIN_EDGE's fix turned into a
    multi-session effort once the full blast radius was traced.

When to revisit:
  - Next time someone tries to actually change one of these 5 values via
    .env and is confused why it has no effect -- that's the actual trigger
    that surfaced the first 3 instances of this pattern too.

RESOLVED 2026-07-19: Picked up expecting to implement it per the plan below;
  re-verification before writing code flipped the diagnosis entirely. Three
  independent findings, each checked directly against live code/data rather
  than trusted from this entry's prior wording:
  (1) record_observation() has ZERO production callers anywhere in the
  codebase (confirmed via repo-wide grep for the function name and for every
  `import metar`/`from metar import` site) and no data/metar_observations.json
  file exists on disk -- it was never actually exercised in production, not
  just missing forecast_high as this entry assumed.
  (2) git history shows it WAS wired in once: commit a023bb2 (Apr 17, "Phase
  4") hooked record_observation() into paper.py's settle_paper_trade() with
  FABRICATED proxy temperatures (threshold +/-3F, not real METAR reads).
  Commit 39e08a6 (May 16, "fix: implement all P0/P1/R1-R21 audit findings")
  deliberately REMOVED that hook ("paper: remove proxy METAR injection") --
  matching docs/audit_findings.md's C20 finding that fabricated temperatures
  feeding a real bias model is a corrupting feedback loop. The current
  all-None state is the result of a considered fix killing a bad
  implementation, not an oversight.
  (3) The job this function was meant to do is already live elsewhere, done
  correctly: weather_markets._get_combined_station_bias() (weather_markets.py
  :320, called at :5971 on every forecast) already blends a static per-city
  bias table with tracker.get_dynamic_station_bias() -- a dynamic correction
  computed from REAL settled temperatures (ensemble_member_scores.
  predicted_temp vs actual_temp, sourced from outcomes.settled_temp_f, the
  official Kalshi settlement value) with a smooth 10-to-50-sample blend
  ramp. This is the same "superseded by an already-live different approach"
  shape as apply_station_bias and 10 other functions deleted in the
  2026-07-12 dead-code sweep -- except metar.py was never covered by that
  scan (scoped only to paper.py/tracker.py/weather_markets.py), so this
  sibling instance sat undiscovered. get_station_bias() itself also had zero
  production callers even if it worked.
  Note: the live dynamic mechanism isn't contributing correction yet either
  -- var-tagging (needed to separate max/min bias) shipped 2026-07-10
  (commit bd63c5f) but every row in ensemble_member_scores today (269 rows)
  predates that, so it's 100% on the static-table fallback right now. Same
  "waiting on the trading pause to end" gap as every other log-only signal
  in this file, not a design flaw -- activates automatically once >=10
  var-tagged settlements/city accumulate post-Belgium.
  Fix applied: deleted get_station_bias(), record_observation(),
  get_obs_count(), and the _load_obs/_save_obs/_OBS_PATH/_OBS_LOCK/
  _MIN_OBS_FOR_MODEL JSON-store machinery from metar.py (now dead `json`/
  `threading`/`Path` imports removed too), updated the module docstring
  (dropped the "station-level observation recording" bullet), and removed
  the two now-empty test classes (TestRecordObservation, TestGetStationBias)
  from tests/test_phase4.py. Building a second, differently-shaped bias
  correction (monthly granularity, separate JSON store) alongside the
  already-live tracker-based one would risk double-correcting the same
  forecast -- the same reasoning that killed bayesian_kelly_fraction in the
  2026-07-12 sweep. 66+169 = 235 tests pass across
  test_phase4/test_metar/test_settlement_monitor/test_weather_markets/
  test_station_bias; ruff+mypy clean.

Original problem (superseded, kept for history):
  metar.py:437-461 get_station_bias() does real filtering/threshold work
  (station lookup, proxy-observation exclusion, _MIN_OBS_FOR_MODEL/

  both still open.

What the fix looks like:

  observations before a real per-station bias model can be computed. Scope
  that storage change first, then implement the actual bias model.

Why not now:
  - Currently safe (callers correctly skip the correction when None is
    returned) -- this is a missing feature, not a live bug.
  - Needs the forecast_high storage prerequisite before the real work can
    start.

UPDATE 2026-07-12 (research pass, no code changed): re-verified still
