[MOSTLY RESOLVED 2026-07-12] MIXED-TIMESTAMP-FORMAT BUG CLASS -- RECURRING, NO ROOT-CAUSE FIX
Priority: was Low-Medium (individually low-impact so far, but a well-established
  recurring pattern -- fifth occurrence would not be surprising)

RESOLVED 2026-07-12 (mostly): get_brier_over_time (tracker.py:1471) already
  uses the correct strftime('%Y-%m-%d %H:%M:%S') cutoff (not .isoformat()) --
  fixed sometime before this date, this entry's "queued for its own fix
  pass" note is stale. Separately, added utils.sql_normalize_iso_column()
  as the shared "centralize all cutoffs through one helper" fix this entry
  asked for, and used it to consolidate the 3 remaining hand-duplicated
  instances of the underlying strftime/replace normalization expression
  (execution_log.py's was_recently_ordered/was_ordered_recently, tracker.py's
  v21->v22 settled_at migration) -- pure refactor, no behavior change,
  pushed af39a67. A full audit at that time found no remaining unfixed
  instances of the raw bug (mismatched-format comparison) anywhere in
  tracker.py/execution_log.py. NOT built: the "cheap regression test that
  greps for .isoformat() feeding a SQL bind parameter" lint-style guard --
  the shared helper reduces the chance of a NEW instance (nothing left to
  copy-paste wrong), but doesn't structurally prevent someone writing a
  fresh ad-hoc .isoformat() cutoff by hand. Worth adding if a fifth instance
  ever appears despite the helper existing.

Problem:
  A 2026-07-10 Fable adversarial review of tracker.py found the *identical*
  bug three separate times in one pass: get_brier_over_time,
  get_model_brier_scores, and get_recent_city_correlations each built a
  Python .isoformat() cutoff ('...T...+00:00') and compared it
  lexicographically against a column written by SQLite's datetime('now')
  ('YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM:SS') -- silently dropping the entire boundary day every
  time, since ' ' (0x20) < 'T' (0x54) in a TEXT comparison. This is the exact
  same bug class the v22 migration already fixed once for
  outcomes.settled_at (see the migration's own comment: "Mixed formats
  corrupt date-range queries that rely on lexicographic order"). Four
  independent occurrences of one mistake in the same file means a fifth is
  a when, not an if, absent a structural fix. (get_recent_city_correlations
  and get_model_brier_scores were fixed in the same 2026-07-10 session;
  get_brier_over_time's cutoff bug was found MEDIUM-confirmed and is queued
  for its own fix pass.)

What the fix looks like:
  Either centralize all "N days/weeks ago" cutoffs through one helper
  (e.g. _sql_cutoff(days) returning SQLite-format text, or pushing the
  cutoff into SQL via datetime('now', ? || ' days') the way
  get_member_accuracy/get_model_weights already do) instead of hand-rolling
  (datetime.now(UTC) - timedelta(...)).isoformat() at each call site, or add
  a cheap regression test that greps tracker.py for .isoformat() feeding a
  SQL bind parameter and fails the build/pre-commit hook.

Why not now:
  - Each individual instance found so far has been LOW/MEDIUM severity, not
    a live-trading-critical bug -- this is about stopping the pattern, not
    an urgent fix.
  - A real fix (the shared-helper version) touches every date-cutoff query
    in the file -- worth its own careful pass with tests, not a drive-by.

When to revisit:
  - Next time tracker.py is opened for other reasons, or the next time this
    exact bug shape is found a fifth time -- at that point the case for the
    structural fix (not just another one-off patch) becomes hard to ignore.

[MOVE OFF LOCAL CRON -- HOST ON A SMALL ALWAYS-ON VM]
Priority: Medium (not a code bug, but the user's stated auto-run reliability
  problem is real and this is the actual fix for it)

Problem:
  This bot's scheduled runs (cron.py, invoked via Windows Task Scheduler on
  a laptop) have caused reliability issues per the user directly -- a
  travel laptop closing its lid, losing wifi, or just not being on defeats
  the whole point of unattended scheduled scanning. cron.py itself is a
  genuine one-shot process (confirmed while building the [RESTING EXIT
  ORDERS] entry above -- no `while True` loop, no persistent state between
  invocations) that depends entirely on an external scheduler staying
  alive, which a travel laptop structurally can't guarantee.

  Original plan (per the user, "a long time ago") was AWS. Re-evaluated
  from scratch 2026-07-13 rather than assuming that's still the best fit.

What the fix looks like:
  Move scheduling off the laptop onto a small always-on VM. This bot's
  entire persistence model (SQLite DBs in tracker.py/execution_log.py,
  JSON stores for paper trades/WS orderbook cache/sigma cache/config hash,
  the Kalshi private key file) assumes durable local disk between runs --
  that rules out pure serverless (Lambda-style, ephemeral filesystem) and
  GitHub Actions (ephemeral runners; would need a git-commit-back or
  Artifacts hack to fake persistence) without a real storage migration
  first. A plain VPS keeps the current architecture untouched: just swap
  Windows Task Scheduler for real Unix cron or a systemd timer running the
  same `python cron.py` invocation.

  11 hosting options researched and ranked 2026-07-13 (full comparison
  with current pricing/reliability sources in that session's transcript,
  not reproduced here in full):
    - RECOMMENDED: Hetzner Cloud or DigitalOcean, ~$5-12/mo. Cheapest real
      VPS tier with no vendor-reliability red flags. DO has free built-in
      monitoring/alerting as a bonus; Hetzner is cheaper at equivalent
      specs. Linode/Vultr are close seconds, no compelling reason to pick
      them over Hetzner/DO specifically.
    - AWS EC2 (t4g.micro) and Azure (B1s) both priced out higher than
      Hetzner/DO with no functional benefit for a workload this small --
      note for AWS specifically: t4g.micro is NOT covered by the standard
      12-month free tier (that's t3.micro/t2.micro, or a t4g.small promo
      through end of 2026 only) -- budget for cost from day one if AWS is
      ever picked instead.
    - AVOID despite being $0/mo, specifically because the user's problem is
      unpredictable auto-run failures: Oracle Cloud "Always Free" (2026
      reports of account-approval opacity, a June 2026 capacity halving --
      4 OCPU/24GB -> 2 OCPU/12GB -- with zero notice, and "idle
      reclamation" that can throttle/kill a low-traffic instance) and
      GitHub Actions scheduled workflows (silently disables a workflow
      after 60 days of repo inactivity, on top of the persistent-disk
      mismatch above -- the same "silently stops working" failure category
      the user is trying to escape, not a fix for it).
    - Google Cloud e2-micro Always Free is a genuine $0/mo dark horse (no
      Oracle-style complaints found), but has no SLA on free-tier
      resources and only 1GB RAM -- tight if this box is also meant to run
      continuously (see sizing note below).
    - Render/Railway/Fly.io (PaaS with built-in cron+volumes) work
      architecturally but cost more than a plain VPS for no benefit here;
      Fly.io specifically has a reputation for surprise bills from
      compounding metrics (volume storage, snapshots, inter-region
      traffic all billed separately).
    - Home Raspberry Pi + Tailscale is a legitimate $0/mo-recurring option
      that sidesteps cloud-vendor risk entirely (stays online at home
      while the user travels, which is the actual scenario being solved)
      but shifts the single point of failure to home internet/power, with
      the user as the only support line if hardware fails.

  User's answers when asked (2026-07-13, via AskUserQuestion): pay ~$5/mo
  and prioritize reliability over $0 (rules out Oracle/GCP free tier);
  size the box for eventually running `watch --auto --live` continuously
  plus the deferred always-on-watcher piece from the [RESTING EXIT ORDERS]
  entry above, not just periodic cron.py -- pushes toward a 2GB-RAM tier
  (Hetzner CX22-equivalent, or DigitalOcean's ~$12/mo droplet) rather than
  the cheapest 1GB option; starting fresh, no existing cloud accounts to
  factor into the decision.

  Setup shape once started (not yet done): Ubuntu, SSH key-only access, a
  free stateful firewall (Hetzner) or DO's built-in cloud firewall
  (inbound SSH only from the user's IP, everything else outbound-only,
  which this bot needs freely for Kalshi/Open-Meteo/NWS/notification
  webhooks), clone via a read-only deploy key (not a personal SSH key),
  scp over .env and the Kalshi private key file (never committed), real
  cron/systemd timer for the schedule, drop "desktop" from NOTIFY_CHANNELS
  (won't fire headless -- Pushover/Discord/email already work and need no
  code changes, just env vars), periodic snapshot plus an independent
  rsync/scp of the SQLite DBs back to the user's own storage (don't rely
  solely on the provider's snapshot).

Why not now:
  - Explicitly parked by the user ("we are not doing anything now") --
    the comparison and decision are done, nothing has been executed. No VM
    created, no code changed.

When to revisit:
  - Whenever the user is ready to actually execute. Use the decision
    above (Hetzner or DigitalOcean, ~$12/mo tier, sized for continuous
    operation) rather than re-running the hosting comparison from scratch
    unless something material has changed (a provider's pricing/free-tier
    terms, or the user's requirements).
  - UPDATE 2026-07-16 (user clarification, no code changed): the trigger
    is live trading actually going live (or becoming concretely imminent),
    not just the ~2026-07-30 Belgium-trip-end date passing. Don't resurface
    this as ready-to-execute purely because the trip has ended -- confirm
    live trading is genuinely about to start first.
  - RE-VERIFIED 2026-07-20: still parked, zero infra progress (no
    Dockerfile/compose/systemd/Task-Scheduler config anywhere in the repo),
    cron.py still has no `while True` (one-shot, confirmed). Its real
    prerequisite (THE ONLY LIVE-ORDER PATH IS THE INTERACTIVE WATCH CLI --
    NO HEADLESS TRADE-CYCLE ENGINE, above) is still unshipped beyond a small
    dedup/is_stale slice -- don't start the VM move before that engine
    exists. Note for future sessions: the dead-man's-switch heartbeat
    (>48h-gap push notification, shipped 2026-06-28, predates this entry)
    is a detection/alerting mechanism only -- it does NOT fix the underlying
    laptop-lid/wifi/scheduler reliability problem this entry exists to
    solve; don't mistake it for "already fixed another way."

[RESOLVED 2026-07-13] RESTING EXIT ORDERS + OCO ORDER GROUPS
Priority: was High (live risk-management hole, not just an optimization)

RESOLVED 2026-07-13: resolved as "event-driven protective exits," a
  materially different design than the "OCO with a resting take-profit +
  resting stop-loss" plan below -- two research findings during design
  invalidated that plan's core mechanics, surfaced to and confirmed with the
  user before writing any code:
    1. Kalshi has no stop/conditional order type at all (confirmed directly
       against Kalshi's own V2 create-order API docs -- time_in_force is
       only fill_or_kill/good_till_canceled/immediate_or_cancel). A resting
       LIMIT sell fills when price RISES to meet it -- the opposite of what
       protects a falling position. A "resting stop-loss order" cannot work
       mechanically; a real stop-loss must cross the spread immediately the
       instant it triggers, not rest passively.
    2. Take-profit isn't a real concept in this bot today. paper.py's
       exit_target field (the take-profit price this plan assumed existed)
       was found to be fully dead -- threaded through place_paper_order's
       signature and checked by check_exit_targets(), but grepping every
       real call site in the repo, none of them ever actually sets it. This
       bot's actual exit strategy is 100% signal-triggered (price
       stop-loss, breakeven-stop, model-flip/edge-gone), not a fixed price
       target -- there was nothing to "rest a GTC sell at."
  User chose (via AskUserQuestion) to build event-driven protective exits
  only, explicitly declining to also invent a take-profit mechanism from
  scratch: doing so would risk cutting winning trades short before their
  statistical edge fully resolves (this bot trades multi-day probabilistic
  edge, not price momentum), with no settled-trade volume yet to calibrate
  a target against.

  What shipped: live positions previously had ZERO automated exit
  management of any kind (not "poll-based," genuinely none -- verified by
  exhaustive grep: execution_log.py's orders table only ever transitioned a
  filled live order through to natural Kalshi settlement, no live-position
  tracker existed, and paper.py's check_stop_losses/check_breakeven_stops/
  check_model_exits only ever operated on paper.get_open_trades()).
  execution_log.py gained 4 columns (peak_profit_pct, exit_reason,
  exit_price, entry_prob) + record_live_early_exit()/
  update_live_peak_profit(); order_executor.py gained
  _get_live_open_positions() (adapts execution_log rows into
  check-function-compatible dicts), _update_live_peak_profits() (peak math
  replicated from paper.update_peak_profits rather than calling it -- that
  function ignores its own parameter and re-reads paper's own JSON store
  internally, confirmed by an independent review reading its body),
  _check_live_position_exits() (reuses paper.check_stop_losses()/
  check_breakeven_stops() completely unmodified -- both verified
  storage-agnostic, operating purely on their passed-in list), and
  _check_live_model_exits() (mirrors the existing paper-only
  _check_early_exits()'s exact gates -- 12h minimum hold, 24h
  pre-settlement skip, 25pp forecast-shift threshold -- against live
  positions instead). Every triggered exit fires via _exit_live_position():
  an immediate_or_cancel sell at the guaranteed-cross price
  (paper._liquidation_price, traced against kalshi_client's V2 side/price
  mapping to confirm it actually crosses for both yes and no), re-running
  only the kill-switch/trading-paused gate (not daily-loss/spend/
  max-open-position -- closing a position reduces exposure, matching the
  same reasoning already applied to _replace_live_order and the manual sell
  path in main.py's cmd_order). Wired into both main.py's cmd_watch --live
  loop and cron.py's _cmd_cron_body (right after the existing
  _recover_pending_orders crash-recovery call) -- cron.py itself still
  never places a live order (unrelated, pre-existing: only watch --auto
  --live does), so this wiring exists to protect a position opened during
  an earlier watch session that's still open when a later cron run fires,
  not because cron can create new live exposure.

  Deliberately deferred, not part of this resolution:
    - A truly always-on watcher that reacts between cron cycles (closing
      the multi-hour manual-cron-cadence gap this entry was originally
      about) -- these checks still only run once per cmd_watch/cron cycle.
      Discussed explicitly with the user: this is more an ops/deployment
      question (does a travel laptop even stay on? systemd service on a
      persistent host?) than application code, and there's no live position
      to protect yet anyway (ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False). Tie this to whatever
      comes of the separate "stop relying on local cron entirely" discussion
      -- a small always-on VM would double as the natural host for this
      watcher too.
    - WS `fill`-channel wiring for faster fill detection -- deferred
      alongside the watcher above, since the existing REST-based
      _poll_pending_orders poll already covers what a periodic-check design
      needs; the fill channel's real payoff only shows up once something
      is actually always-on. Confirmed via a live docs fetch that the
      channel is real, account-wide (no market_tickers filter required),
      with fields order_id/market_ticker/side/action/count_fp/
      yes_price_dollars/is_taker/ts_ms.
    - order_groups as a fill-rate safety cap -- still just the 15s
      rolling-window circuit breaker it was already corrected to be in the
      2026-07-12 update below, not used anywhere in this design.
    - Take-profit (see above -- declined, not just postponed, unless a
      future session has real settled-trade data to design one from).

  Two independent opus reviews given this is the only backlog item this
  session that adds NEW live order-placement code (not modifying existing
  paths). Round 1 (adversarial) found one real HIGH bug: the exit-price
  lookup read _get_current_book()'s REST-fallback shape (raw integer cents,
  or *_dollars-only keys) as if it were already a normalized dollar float --
  meaning stop-loss/breakeven protection would silently never fire on
  exactly the cron path this feature was built for (a fresh process always
  starts with an empty WS cache, so every cron run hits the REST fallback).
  Fixed by routing through the same _coalesce_cents_or_dollars helper the
  sibling model-exit check and pre-existing reprice code already used
  correctly. Also caught and fixed a real fee-formula inconsistency:
  the exit PnL calc applied the taker fee to gross proceeds unconditionally
  including on a loss, diverging from the established convention (fee only
  discounts a genuine WIN, verified across weather_markets.py/paper.py and
  the pre-existing natural-settlement code) -- fixed to the win/loss
  asymmetric form, independently re-derived as an exact generalization of
  the existing settlement formula (substituting exit_price=1.0 or 0.0
  reproduces the original win/loss branches exactly). Round 2 (verification)
  confirmed both fixes correct and complete, added a regression test using
  the genuine raw-cents shape (not another disguised dollar-float mock),
  and found one new narrow LOW issue -- multiple live positions sharing one
  ticker would collapse to one entry in a ticker-keyed dict, silently
  leaving the other unprotected for a cycle -- inherited from paper.py's
  own ticker-keyed check-function design (cron.py's paper stop-loss/
  breakeven handling has the identical `next(t for t in trades if
  t["ticker"]==ticker)` one-match pattern already live in production, so
  this was fixed narrowly in order_executor.py only rather than touching
  the shared, already-relied-upon paper.py functions): positions are now
  grouped by ticker (list per ticker, not one dict slot), and every
  position under a flagged ticker is exited, not just one -- erring toward
  over-inclusive (a healthy same-ticker position exits a cycle earlier than
  its own individual threshold required) rather than the failure mode this
  whole entry exists to prevent (a position silently left unprotected).
  118+ tests pass across the affected scope; ruff/mypy clean.

  Also fixed the same day, found while running the broader regression
  sweep (confirmed via git stash it failed identically on the prior commit
  with none of this session's changes applied, so genuinely unrelated to
  this backlog item): tests/test_paper.py's
  TestMonteCarloCholesky::test_past_date_trade_excluded_from_simulation was
  failing -- root cause was the TEST, not monte_carlo.py itself. It built
  its "past"/"future" fixture dates from local machine date.today(), but
  simulate_portfolio()'s actual skip logic compares against
  utils.utc_today(). On a machine whose local date is already a day ahead
  of UTC, "yesterday, local" lands on the same calendar day as "today,
  UTC" -- the skip condition (`_tdate < utc_today()`) never fires, and the
  trade wrongly falls through into the clamping path the test was trying
  to prove it never reaches. Fixed both this test and its sibling
  (test_past_date_only_portfolio_returns_empty_result, same pattern, not
  yet failing only because its 2-day margin happened to still clear the
  gap) to build fixture dates from utils.utc_today() instead, matching the
  System Under Test's actual reference frame.

Problem (original framing, superseded by the resolution above):
  All exits are poll-based: check_exit_targets()/check_model_exits()/
  stop-losses only run when a cron or watch cycle happens to execute. On a
  manual-cron cadence (e.g. ~3 runs/day during the Belgium trip) an open
  position can sit through its stop level for hours with zero protection.
  Kalshi's API supports order_groups (OCO — linked orders where one fill
  auto-cancels the others) and a WebSocket `fill` channel; the bot uses
  neither (kalshi_ws.py:301 subscribes only to ticker + orderbook_delta,
  fills are discovered by polling _poll_pending_orders()).

UPDATE 2026-07-12 (research pass, no code changed) -- IMPORTANT CORRECTION
to the order_groups claim above:
  Re-confirmed kalshi_ws.py still subscribes only to ticker + orderbook_delta
  (kalshi_ws.py:329) and kalshi_client.py has no order_group/fill support at
  all -- that part of the problem statement still holds.
  But fetched docs.kalshi.com/api-reference/order-groups/create-order-group
  directly and Kalshi's order_groups is NOT an OCO mechanism -- the original
  "linked orders where one fill auto-cancels the others" claim is wrong.
  It's actually a risk-management circuit breaker: contracts_limit sets a
  max matched-contracts count over a rolling 15-SECOND window; once hit,
  ALL orders in the group are cancelled and no new ones can be placed until
  reset. There is no field or documented behavior for "one order filling
  cancels the others" -- that's a self-built OCO concept this bot would
  still have to implement client-side (rest both legs, watch for either to
  fill via polling or the `fill` WS channel, cancel the other manually).
  order_groups' real use case is closer to protecting a market maker's
  resting quotes from a fast adverse-selection burst, not linking a
  take-profit and a stop-loss together -- still possibly useful for THIS
  bot's resting exits (cap how much can fill against a stale resting order
  in a 15s window) but as an extra safety layer, not as the OCO primitive
  the fix plan below assumed it would be.
  The WebSocket `fill` channel IS real and confirmed subscribable via
  `channels: ["fill"]` (docs.kalshi.com/websockets/websocket-connection) --
  that half of the plan holds.
  The market-maker rebate claim also needs correcting: Kalshi runs several
  DIFFERENT incentive programs, not one. Fetched
  help.kalshi.com/en/articles/13823851-liquidity-incentive-program directly:
  it pays a $10-$1,000/day share of a reward pool (Score / Total Participants'
  Scores * Reward Pool) for maintaining resting-order "Target Size" (100-
  20,000 contracts), NOT a flat percentage-of-fees rebate -- doesn't match
  the original "1%, capped $7,000/week" figure at all. Kalshi also has a
  separate Volume Incentive Program, Liquidity Provider Program, Combo
  Incentive Program, and a formal fee-rebate Market Maker Program referenced
  in CFTC filings (which may be where the original 1%/$7,000 figure came
  from, unconfirmed) -- these are genuinely different programs with
  different mechanics and eligibility, not one program with one number.
  Any real revenue-angle evaluation needs picking a specific program and
  reading its actual terms once this bot is resting real exit orders, not
  citing a single rebate percentage upfront.

What the fix looks like:
  When a live position opens, immediately rest a GTC sell at the take-profit
  price; implement OCO linking CLIENT-SIDE (order_groups does not do this
  for you -- see correction above): watch for either the take-profit or the
  stop leg to fill (via the `fill` WS channel or polling) and cancel the
  other manually. Subscribe to the WS fill channel to replace/(augment)
  _poll_pending_orders polling. Exits then execute continuously regardless
  of scan cadence, and resting exits get maker pricing instead of taker.
  order_groups' contracts_limit could still be layered in as an extra
  safety cap on a resting exit order's fill rate, separately from the OCO
  logic above.

  Note (revenue-angle, needs its own research pass once this ships -- see
  the multiple-distinct-programs correction above): don't assume a single
  rebate number; identify which Kalshi incentive program actually applies
  to this bot's real resting-order pattern and read its current terms
  directly before quoting a figure.
  Also see the endpoint-deprecation entry at the top of this file: Kalshi's
  order-mutation endpoints (used here for placing/canceling the resting
  exit orders) were migrated to /portfolio/events/orders this session (see
  kalshi_client.py's place_order/cancel_order) -- build any new order-group
  logic on top of that V2 path, not the old deprecated one.

Why not now: N/A -- resolved (as event-driven protective exits, see above).

When to revisit: N/A -- resolved. See the deliberately-deferred list above
  (always-on watcher, WS fill channel, take-profit) for what's still open.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-12] MAKER EXECUTION UPGRADES — REPRICING + MAKER-AWARE
  FEE MODEL
Priority: was High (systematically understated edge on every trade analyzed)

PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-12: problem 2/3 (maker-aware fee model) is done;
  problems 1/4 (repricing/chase logic, fill-quality instrumentation) are
  still open. Verified Kalshi's real fee formula directly against the
  primary source (kalshi.com/docs/kalshi-fee-schedule.pdf, effective July 7,
  2026, obtained and read in full) rather than trusting third-party
  summaries -- several independent secondary sources (pm.wiki, marketmath.io)
  claimed maker fee is universally 25% of taker (0.0175 x P x (1-P)), which
  is WRONG for this bot's markets specifically: the real schedule has a
  maker multiplier M that defaults to 0 for the general event-contract
  schedule, and is only nonzero (giving the 25%-of-taker rate) for ~50
  explicitly-listed non-standard series (KXNFL*, KXNBA*, KXCPI, KXFED, etc.)
  -- none of which are this bot's weather markets. So maker fee is genuinely
  and exactly $0 here, confirming utils.py's original "Maker orders pay 0%"
  comment was correct all along, and problem 3's formula-shape concern
  (0.07 x p x (1-p) vs flat-fraction-of-winnings) turned out to be moot in
  practice: 0 x anything = 0, so the shape mismatch doesn't matter while
  every fill is a maker fill.
  Added utils.KALSHI_MAKER_FEE_RATE (0.0, PDF-cited). Traced every
  KALSHI_FEE_RATE call site across the repo (not just kelly_fraction()/
  net_ev as originally scoped -- the same bug also lived in paper.py's
  settle_paper_trade()/get_attribution(), order_executor.py's live-
  settlement P&L feeding the daily-loss safety counter, and
  monte_carlo.py's portfolio VaR risk gate; scope was surfaced to and
  confirmed by the user before implementing) and switched every site that
  models this bot's own maker-executed trades to the maker rate, while
  deliberately leaving backtest.py's 3 naive-strategy comparison benchmarks
  and kelly_fraction()/bayesian_kelly()'s own generic default parameters at
  the taker rate. Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- traced the safety-
  gate-adjacent sites specifically (daily-loss counter, VaR gate) and
  confirmed the change doesn't remove a safety margin (loss-side P&L is
  unchanged; only previously-phantom fee on wins was removed); found one
  LOW gap (KALSHI_MAKER_FEE_RATE missing from get_config_fingerprint()'s
  drift-detection snapshot), fixed same session. 665 tests pass across the
  full affected scope (weather_markets.py, paper.py, order_executor.py,
  monte_carlo.py, backtest.py, web_app.py, main.py), 3 tests had hardcoded
  0.07-fee P&L expectations corrected to reflect the real $0 maker fee.

  UPDATE (same session, user-flagged): two display sites were still showing
  the stale taker-only fee after the first pass. Added BotConfig.
  kalshi_maker_fee_rate (mirrors kalshi_fee_rate's pattern, own validation)
  and wired it into /api/config (dashboard Settings tab) and the CLI
  settings menu, which previously only showed KALSHI_FEE_RATE with no
  visibility into the rate actually driving sizing. Separately, re-examined
  cmd_simulate()'s "Simulation Sandbox" (main.py) -- originally called out
  of scope as "a symmetric educational game" -- and found that framing was
  wrong: its "Model:" P&L explicitly claims to show what analyze_trade()'s
  own recommendation would have earned (it calls analyze_trade() directly),
  so recomputing that P&L with the taker rate while analyze_trade() itself
  now uses the maker rate was a real internal-consistency bug, not a
  self-contained toy. Fixed by splitting into _user_fee (taker -- a human
  manually taking the displayed price) and _model_fee (maker -- matches
  analyze_trade()'s real assumption). Added a regression test
  (tests/test_backtest.py) since none of the existing cmd_simulate tests
  exercised the interactive P&L path. All tests pass, lint/mypy clean.

  UPDATE (same session, requested full re-review): a second independent
  opus review of the accumulated diff (all 3 rounds) found the math correct
  everywhere but surfaced 3 more instances of the same underlying pattern --
  user-facing display TEXT still hardcoding "~7% fee"/"7% fees", not
  computation this time: main.py's cmd_market Edge line ("after ~7% fee"),
  cmd_backtest's Sim P&L caption ("7% fees"), and cmd_analyze's table
  legend ("after Kalshi's ~7% fee"). None affected sizing, P&L, or safety
  gates -- purely stale captions describing numbers that were already
  computed correctly. Fixed to generic "after fees"/"maker fees" wording
  (not hardcoding a specific percentage, since KALSHI_MAKER_FEE_RATE is
  itself env-overridable). No test pinned the stale strings. All tests
  pass, lint/mypy clean -- this closes the fee-model half of this backlog
  item.

RESOLVED 2026-07-12 (repricing half, separate later pass): problem 1
  (reprice-or-cancel logic) and problem 4 (fill-latency/adverse-selection
  instrumentation) are done, closing this backlog item in full. Scoped via
  two AskUserQuestion checkpoints before writing code -- depth source for
  reprice decisions (chose: WS ticker-tick cache, already streamed/proven
  via the flash-crash gate, over fixing the separately-broken
  orderbook_delta full-depth application, which top-of-book doesn't need
  for this bot's order sizes) and reprice cadence (chose: reuse the
  existing 5-min cmd_watch loop, not a new continuous watcher).

  Policy per pending live order, once per ~5-min cycle (order_executor.py's
  new _reprice_or_cancel_pending_orders, called from cmd_watch right after
  the existing fill-status poll): ticker not in this cycle's fresh scan ->
  leave alone; the existing _validate_trade_opportunity() gate no longer
  passes -> cancel outright, no age minimum; younger than 2 minutes ->
  leave alone; edge still clears the REAL taker fee (recomputed with
  KALSHI_FEE_RATE, not the maker rate analyze_trade() actually used) and
  rested >= 4 minutes -> cancel-verify-unfilled, replace as an
  immediate-or-cancel taker order at the current opposing price; fresh
  midpoint differs from the resting price by >= 1 cent -> cancel-verify-
  unfilled, replace as a new resting GTC order at the fresh midpoint (still
  $0 fee); otherwise leave resting. Every cancel-then-replace goes through
  a hardened _cancel_and_verify_safe_to_replace() (reuses the existing
  _finalize_cancel fill-check pattern) before ever placing a replacement --
  never risks a duplicate position. execution_log.py gained filled_at/
  market_mid_at_fill (captured once, at the moment a fill is first
  detected) and replaces_order_id (links a reprice chain) for the
  adverse-selection instrumentation ask.

  Independently reviewed TWICE given this is the highest-risk change of the
  whole backlog pass (Agent, opus both times) -- first pass found 2 MEDIUM
  + 1 LOW real issues, all fixed same session: (1) the WS-book usability
  check used `is not None`, but a one-sided book's missing side defaults to
  0.0 not None in kalshi_ws.py's own ticker parser, so a one-sided book was
  wrongly treated as usable -- fixed to require both sides > 0, and the
  test that had asserted the old behavior was corrected to mock the real
  0.0 sentinel instead of an unrealistic None; (2) a code comment claimed a
  same-cycle-placed order couldn't reprice-churn because placement and the
  reprice check read "the same scan data" -- traced and found that's false
  (placement re-fetches a fresh market via client.get_market() right before
  pricing; the reprice check reads the WS cache or older scan data --
  genuinely different snapshots) -- fixed with a real blanket minimum-age
  gate applied to both the reprice-improve and taker-cross branches, not
  just relying on the (wrong) assumption; (3) the cancel-safe-to-replace
  check only verified fill_count==0, not that the order was actually
  confirmed off the book -- _finalize_cancel collapses an unrecognized/
  in-flight status (e.g. "resting") to "canceled" for its two pre-existing
  callers, which don't need the distinction, but that meant a still-
  resting order could pass as "safe to replace" -- fixed by threading
  Kalshi's raw unmodified status through as a third return value and
  requiring that specifically. A second, narrower re-verification pass
  after these fixes confirmed all three were implemented correctly, traced
  every call site of the changed _finalize_cancel signature, and found two
  minor test-coverage gaps (fixed: a test whose docstring credited the
  wrong gate after fix #2, and a missing test for the age window between
  the two gates) -- no new bugs. One informational finding (taker-cross
  only fires for temperature markets today, since precip/snow analyze_trade
  paths don't store entry_price) documented, not fixed -- fails safe
  (reprice-improve still works for those markets). One pre-existing,
  narrow settlement-integrity gap unrelated to this feature's core
  correctness (an order that fills exactly as _finalize_cancel's post-
  cancel verification query itself fails could escape settlement
  reconciliation) was spawned as a separate follow-up task rather than
  fixed inline in an already-large diff.

Problem:
  The live path already places GTC limit orders at the midpoint
  (order_executor.py:626-643) — i.e. maker execution exists. But:
  1. No repricing/chase logic exists anywhere (verified: zero hits for
     reprice/amend/requote) — an unfilled order sits 24h (gtc_cancel_hours)
     then cancels. Midpoint resting orders suffer adverse selection: they
     fill preferentially when the market moves against the model.
  2. kelly_fraction() (weather_markets.py:4361-4377) charges the 7% taker
     fee on every trade's EV/sizing, while utils.py:59's own comment notes
     "Maker (limit) orders pay 0%." The bot understates its net edge and
     skips trades it could profitably take at maker pricing.
  3. Fee formula shape is also off (conservative direction): it models "7%
     of winnings, on wins"; Kalshi's real taker fee is 0.07 x p x (1-p)
     charged upfront win-or-lose. Compounds with (2).
  4. No fill-rate / time-to-fill / adverse-selection tracking exists, so
     none of the above can be tuned empirically yet.

What the fix looks like:
  [DONE, see resolution notes above] pass an execution-style-aware fee_rate
    into kelly_fraction()/net_ev instead of flat KALSHI_FEE_RATE.
  [DONE, see resolution notes above] Reprice-or-cancel logic driven by the
    existing kalshi_ws.py book feed (improve toward the ask as edge allows;
    cross as taker only when edge clears the taker fee); log fill latency
    and post-fill price drift per order to measure adverse selection.

Why not now: N/A -- fully resolved.

When to revisit: N/A -- fully resolved. Adverse-selection TUNING (as
  opposed to the instrumentation that now exists to support it) is a
  natural follow-up once enough live fill data accumulates.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-12] HISTORICAL MARKET-PRICE CAPTURE VIA CANDLESTICKS ENDPOINT
Priority: was Medium-High (unlocks execution research the two entries above need)

RESOLVED 2026-07-12: shipped the capture side (analysis passes deliberately
  deferred, per "When to revisit" below). Added kalshi_client.get_candlesticks()
  (GET /series/{series_ticker}/markets/{ticker}/candlesticks, verified against
  live Kalshi docs -- fixed-point "_dollars"/"_fp" response shape, not the
  legacy cents shape) and a new tracker.py price_history table (migration
  v37->v38) with log_price_candles()/get_price_history() helpers. Wired into
  sync_outcomes() as a backfill-on-settlement, not per-cron-cycle polling --
  it fires exactly once per market, right when that market's outcome is first
  recorded (pending query already excludes tickers with an existing outcome
  row), fetching the market's full OHLC history in one call via its
  open_time/close_time range. Backfill failure is isolated in its own
  try/except so it can never block outcome recording. Independently reviewed
  (Agent, opus): found and fixed one real MEDIUM issue before commit -- initial
  1-minute candle resolution over a multi-day open window risked silently
  under-capturing exactly the long-open weather markets this feature targets
  (Kalshi's undocumented-but-plausible per-request period cap), logged only at
  debug so the failure would have been invisible. Fixed by switching to hourly
  resolution (still plenty for the deferred edge-decay/adverse-selection
  analysis) and bumping the failure log to warning. 25 new tests, lint/mypy
  clean. Pushed ba3527e. TRADING_PAUSED untouched; no order-placement/gate
  code was touched.

Problem:
  Zero references to Kalshi's /markets/{ticker}/candlesticks endpoint (or
  any price-history capture) exist in the codebase. The bot cannot answer
  "does my edge decay as the market converges to the forecast — when is the
  optimal entry?", cannot benchmark against real price paths (the current
  "Follow market" backtest benchmark uses scan-time prices only), and
  cannot measure maker-fill adverse selection.

What the fix looks like:
  Log OHLC candles for tracked markets (fetch per cron cycle, or backfill
  on settlement); store in a new price_history table keyed by
  ticker/period. Then: entry-timing analysis (edge vs hours-to-close),
  real-price benchmark replay, and post-fill drift measurement.

Why not now:
  - Pure new instrumentation + storage; payoff is analytical, arrives only
    after weeks of accumulated candles.

When to revisit:
  - Ship the capture early (it's cheap and data accumulates only from when
    it ships); do the analysis passes once maker-execution work is picked
    up.
  - UPDATE 2026-07-16 (no code changed): concretizing this per the
    ENABLEMENT TRIGGER pattern introduced in the FORECAST RUN-TO-RUN TREND
    SIGNAL entry above -- check `SELECT COUNT(*) FROM price_history` (and
    ideally distinct ticker count) periodically; the analysis passes
    (entry-timing, real-price replay, drift measurement) are worth doing
    once there's a real multi-week window of candles, not tied strictly to
    maker-execution work being picked up if that stays deferred longer than
    the data does.

[PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-16] FORECAST RUN-TO-RUN TREND SIGNAL
Priority: was Medium (new alpha source, mostly existing plumbing) -- now Low
  until the enablement trigger below fires; this is a data-collection phase,
  not an active development item.

PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-16: the LOGGING half is shipped; the BLEND half
  (directional lean and/or sigma-widening) is deliberately not built yet --
  scoped via AskUserQuestion before coding (data-source symmetry, series
  length, blend usage) and the user chose log-only for this pass, matching
  every other new-signal entry in this file's own precedent (candlestick
  capture, trade-flow signal, this entry's own original wording).
  Live-verified against the real Previous Runs API (2026-07-16) before
  writing code: a future target_date returns real non-null data when queried
  with forecast_days instead of past_days (the pre-existing
  _fetch_previous_run_daily, built only for backfilling PAST dates, returns
  None for a future one); the existing lead clamp of 1-7 is correct (lead=8
  confirmed all-null live); Open-Meteo accepts multiple previous_dayN
  hourly variables in one request, so a 4-point lookback costs the same 3
  HTTP calls (one per model) as a 2-point one would -- this is why 4 points
  were shipped instead of 2, at no extra API cost, so jumpiness (needed for
  the sigma-widening half, when it's built) doesn't require a second schema
  migration later.
  Shipped: tracker.get_forecast_run_trend(city, target_date, days_out, var) --
  weights the same 3 models as backfill_emos_data's EMOS ens_mean
  (_PREVIOUS_RUN_MODEL_MAP, via _model_weights) across leads N..N+3 (clamped
  to 1-7), so every point in the series uses identical apples-to-apples
  methodology, not a mismatch between a live ensemble mean and a single
  deterministic control run. Returns {"points": [...], "delta": ...,
  "jumpy": ...} or None (days_out<1 -- same-day markets use the METAR
  pipeline instead; unknown city; fewer than 2 usable leads). Cached
  (ForecastCache, 4h TTL, 30min TTL on a negative/failed result so a
  transient API hiccup doesn't blank the signal out for a full 4h) keyed on
  (city, target_date, days_out, var) -- var included because a HIGH and LOW
  market on the same city/date need independently cached series. Wired into
  tracker.log_prediction() as a new run_trend param (3 new columns:
  run_trend_points JSON, run_trend_delta/run_trend_jumpy scalars, schema
  v39->v42). 18 new tests (tests/test_tracker.py) -- fetch parsing/omission/
  failure modes, weighted-delta/jumpy computed from known per-model values
  with intentionally UNEQUAL weights (proves real weighting, not an average
  disguised as one), cache-hit-avoids-second-network-call, log_prediction
  round-trip, and the extraction-helper's field-mapping/malformed-input
  cases (see below). Mutation-tested the weighted-mean line (swapped to a
  plain average on a scratch edit, confirmed the delta/jumpy test fails with
  the exact expected wrong numbers, reverted) -- confirmed the test genuinely
  checks weighting rather than passing spuriously.

  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- found the log-only guarantee held
  and the schema migration was safe, but ONE real MEDIUM issue: the initial
  design called get_forecast_run_trend() directly inside
  weather_markets.analyze_trade(), which put up to 3 sequential HTTP calls
  (up to ~60s worst case on a cache miss) on the live order-placement
  critical path -- analyze_trade's caller only places the order after it
  returns, so a slow fetch would delay an already-fully-decided trade's
  submission even though the fetch itself never touched blended_prob/kelly/
  edge. Fixed by moving the call entirely out of analyze_trade: new
  tracker.get_forecast_run_trend_from_analysis(analysis) extracts city/
  target_date/days_out/var from an analyze_trade()-shaped dict and is now
  the ONLY caller of get_forecast_run_trend, invoked from
  order_executor._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis and main.py's two direct
  log_prediction call sites (cmd_market, cmd_order) -- all of which run at
  LOG time, which for real trades already happens AFTER order placement
  (order_executor._auto_place_trades' own docstring), fully decoupling the
  fetch from fill timing. Side benefit: markets that get analyzed but never
  traded or shadow-logged now skip the fetch entirely, where the original
  design would have fetched for every scanned market regardless of outcome.
  Also fixed 2 LOW robustness gaps the same review surfaced:
  _fetch_previous_run_leads now checks the `hourly` field is actually a
  dict before indexing into it (a malformed API response could otherwise
  raise AttributeError outside the function's own try/except), and
  get_forecast_run_trend's model-weighting/statistics section is now
  wrapped in its own try/except so the function's "never raises" docstring
  claim is actually enforced by the function itself, not just inherited
  from whatever happened to call it. A second finding -- the real
  data/predictions.db had drifted to PRAGMA user_version=40 while already
  having all 3 new columns (caused by this session's own now-fixed
  _SCHEMA_VERSION=40 typo briefly existing while all 3 migration entries
  were already in _MIGRATIONS, and something triggering init_db() against
  the real DB during that window) -- confirmed harmless and self-healing
  (duplicate-column guard), but corrected immediately anyway by calling
  tracker._run_migrations() once by hand rather than leaving it for the
  bot's next natural run.

ENABLEMENT TRIGGER (the actual ask: when to turn this from log-only into a
  real blend input) -- do NOT wire it into blended_prob/sigma/kelly until:
  1. A meaningful number of settled trades have a non-NULL run_trend_delta/
     run_trend_jumpy (check: predictions JOIN outcomes WHERE
     run_trend_delta IS NOT NULL AND settled_temp_f IS NOT NULL). Apply the
     same sample-floor precedent already used elsewhere in this file before
     trusting a per-signal statistic (ACCURACY_MIN_SAMPLE=20,
     SPRT_MIN_TRADES=20, MIN_BIAS_CORRECTION_TRADES=50) -- don't invent a
     new, lower bar just because this signal is new.
  2. A real accuracy check has been run against that data: does a positive
     run_trend_delta (forecast trending warmer) actually correlate with the
     forecast being LOW (i.e. the true value came in even higher), the
     directional-persistence hypothesis this entry is built on? Does high
     run_trend_jumpy actually correlate with larger forecast error (the
     sigma-widening hypothesis)? Both are testable directly against
     settled_temp_f once #1 is satisfied -- don't wire in blend/sigma
     changes on the strength of the mechanism sounding plausible alone.
  3. Only then: revisit the original "What the fix looks like" below for
     the actual blend/sigma wiring, gated behind tracked accuracy like every
     other signal source in this file (see the ENSEMBLE spread bias, NWS
     weight decay, and dynamic bias-correction gates already live in
     weather_markets.py for the established pattern to match).
  This same trigger shape (accumulate -> check correlation against real
  settlement data -> only then wire into the blend) applies to every other
  log-only-shipped signal in this file -- see RICHER ML CALIBRATION
  FEATURES and GENERALIZED PER-MODEL ACCURACY TRACKING below, and the
  candlestick capture / public trade-flow signal entries, all of which have
  the same "ship the logging, evaluate later" shape and the same risk of
  being logged forever and never actually revisited without an explicit
  check-back condition like this one.

Problem (original framing, still accurate for the blend/sigma half):
  The Open-Meteo Previous Runs API is already integrated — but only in
  tracker.py (~2231) / backtest.py for EMOS backfill. The live path never
  compares the current model run against the previous run. Run-to-run
  revision carries signal: a forecast trending warmer across consecutive
  runs tends to keep trending while markets anchor to the older number, and
  high run-to-run jumpiness is a principled reason to widen sigma.

What the fix looks like (still open -- logging half only is done above):
  Feed the now-logged delta/jumpy series as (a) a small directional lean in
  the blend and/or (b) a sigma-widening term when jumpiness is high, once
  the ENABLEMENT TRIGGER above is satisfied.

Why not now:
  - The enablement trigger above hasn't fired yet -- zero settled trades
    have a run_trend_delta value as of 2026-07-16 (the column didn't exist
    until today). Needs real elapsed time + trading activity, not more
    engineering effort.

When to revisit:
  - Check the ENABLEMENT TRIGGER's sample-floor query periodically (e.g.
    whenever this file is next open for other reasons, or paired with the
    DATA-DRIVEN SIGMA FROM SETTLED HISTORY entry's own settled-count check
    below, since both are gated on the same kind of settled-trade volume
    growing over time).

[RICHER ML CALIBRATION FEATURES]
Priority: Medium (model architecture is fine; the feature vector is the
  bottleneck)

Problem:
  The GradientBoosting bias model trains on exactly [our_prob, month,
  days_out, 0.0] (ml_bias.py:204) — four features, the fourth literally
  always zero. Ensemble spread, ICON/GFS disagreement, data_quality score,
  condition_type, and sigma-used are all computed at trade time and
  discarded before training.

What the fix looks like:
  Thread 2-3 of the highest-value candidates (ensemble spread and model
  disagreement first) through the predictions table into the training rows;
  let the existing `features` importance command arbitrate which earn their
  place. Do NOT add many at once — the 200-samples-per-city training gate
  means feature count must stay small relative to data.

Why not now:
  - Needs schema addition + weeks of newly-logged rows before retraining
    can use them (existing rows lack the new fields).
  - RE-VERIFIED 2026-07-20: still exactly [our_prob, month, days_out, 0.0]
    (ml_bias.py:204); no ensemble_spread/model_disagreement/data_quality/
    sigma_used columns exist yet on multiday_predictions. Nothing unblocked.

When to revisit:
  - Ship the logging side early (same "data accumulates only from when it
    ships" logic as candlesticks); retrain when enough enriched rows exist.

Original problem (Pass 1 resolved; Pass 2/new-sources still open):
  The existing entry covers instrumenting ECMWF specifically. The general
  version: per-model accuracy is stored as one hardcoded column per model
  (icon_forecast_mean/gfs_forecast_mean), so every new source requires the
  same multi-file plumbing again. Meanwhile free, unconsumed sources exist:
  GEM EPS and UKMO ensembles on the same Open-Meteo ensemble API already
  called, and Google WeatherNext (GraphCast/GenCast lineage) via BigQuery.
  (Verified 2026-07-10: zero code references to gem/ukmo/weathernext.)

What the fix looks like:
  Build the plumbing once as a generic model->forecast_mean mapping (new
  table or JSON column) instead of per-model columns; then adding any
  source is config + fetch only, and each self-calibrates via the existing
  learned-weight machinery. Note the research caveat: pure-AI models
  underperform physics models on record-breaking heat/cold — keep physics
  models in the blend and let learned weights arbitrate.

Why not now:
  - Same reasons as the ECMWF entry (multi-file instrumentation, weeks
    before learned weights activate) — plus a schema-design decision
    (generic table vs columns) that should be made once, deliberately.
  - RE-VERIFIED 2026-07-20: still exactly icon_forecast_mean/
    gfs_forecast_mean, no generic mapping. Repo-wide grep for gem/ukmo/
    weathernext/graphcast/gencast: zero hits, confirming the free-source
    claim still holds. Its own prerequisite, TRACK ECMWF FORECAST ACCURACY
    above, is still open/unresolved — the "when picking up ECMWF" trigger
    hasn't fired.

When to revisit (Pass 2 -- wiring up real new sources onto the now-generic
  mechanism):

    same _model_prob_and_mean/ENSEMBLE_BASE infra as icon/gfs/
    ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble. Full 16-day horizon.
  - UKMO: use model="ukmo_global_ensemble_20km" (NOT "ukmo_seamless",
    confirmed dead/null). Real horizon is shorter than requested -- only

    assuming full 16-day coverage like GEM.
  - Add both to batch_prewarm_ensemble()'s model list (mirrors how
    ecmwf_aifs025_ensemble was already added there) so real scans hit warm
    cache instead of a new per-call fetch.
  - Add both to KNOWN_FORECAST_MODEL_NAMES when wired up, or

[RESOLVED 2026-07-19] LIQUIDITY-AWARE SIZING + DYNAMIC EDGE THRESHOLD
Priority: was Medium (consolidates two existing loose ends into one
  feature).

RESOLVED 2026-07-19: split the two original mechanisms by risk profile
  rather than shipping both live, after a scoping pass that found the
  2026-07-18 UPDATE's "319 real fills" framing overstated what that data
  could actually do -- tracker.price_improvement has no volume/open_interest
  column and no join key back to book depth at fill time (price_history,
  which would let you reconstruct that, still has 0 rows); even the weak
  proxy check (does the bot's own order quantity correlate with fill
  slippage magnitude?) showed no relationship (corr ~= -0.03 to -0.07,
  n=319). So neither original mechanism could be empirically calibrated --
  both are reasoned defaults, same as the 2026-07-12 originals were.
  Given that, the two pieces were deliberately NOT shipped with equal
  confidence:
  1. paper.liquidity_kelly_scale(market) -- LIVE. Revives the deleted
     slippage_kelly_scale's exact tier shape (volume+open_interest summed;
     500/200/50 -> 1.00/0.85/0.70/0.50), wired into order_executor.py's
     _auto_place_trades sizing math (line ~2352, multiplied into adj_kelly
     right alongside corr_kelly_scale -- same call site, same pattern).
     Chosen to ship live because it fails safe: a wrong multiplier only
     ever produces a smaller (or zero) bet, never a wrong-direction one,
     and every existing position-size guardrail (MAX_TOTAL_OPEN_EXPOSURE,
     KELLY_CAP, corr_kelly_scale's own floor, daily-loss/drawdown halts)
     still sits downstream of it as a safety net.
  2. weather_markets._liquidity_edge_scale(volume, open_interest) --
     LOG-ONLY. Matches code_review_plan.md's Phase 5 Feature 3 design
     exactly (confirmed via git archaeology -- never built there). Computed
     as gated_edge = adjusted_edge / liquidity_edge_scale at the scan-loop
     level (cron.py's cmd_cron, main.py's _analyze_once) -- deliberately
     NOT inside analyze_trade() itself (mirrors run_trend's/market_implied's
     precedent of keeping unvalidated signals out of the live trade-decision
     function) and NEVER used for STRONG/MED/MIN classification. Kept
     log-only because a wrong multiplier here is a correctness risk, not
     just a sizing one -- it sits upstream of every existing safety net,
     and could in principle inflate a weak signal into STRONG rather than
     just under-sizing a good one (the same failure class as this project's
     own past T-bucket sign-inversion and net_edge cap-ordering bugs). See
     ENABLEMENT TRIGGER below for what's required before this changes.
  Logged into 2 new predictions columns (liquidity_edge_scale, gated_edge --
  migration v46/v47) via order_executor._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis,
  reading a.get("liquidity_edge_scale")/a.get("gated_edge") (same
  scan-paths-only pattern as market_implied -- cmd_market/cmd_order log
  NULL for both).
  8 new tests for liquidity_kelly_scale (tests/test_paper.py), 8 for
  _liquidity_edge_scale (tests/test_weather_markets.py), plus extensions to
  test_prediction_kwargs.py (2 tests) and test_tracker.py (2 tests). A real
  bug caught mid-build (not by review): main.py's first-draft wiring
  computed gated_edge from raw `edge` while cron.py's used `adjusted_edge`
  -- would have made the two scan paths log incomparable values, silently
  corrupting the future correlation check below. Caught by re-reading the
  two call sites side by side before moving on, fixed to derive both from
  adjusted_edge consistently.
  Independent opus review caught one real, live-money bug before push:
  paper.liquidity_kelly_scale (and both log-only call sites) read only the
  legacy market.get("volume")/market.get("open_interest") field names --
  but the current Kalshi API returns volume_fp/open_interest_fp, and
  nothing normalizes one to the other. Every other volume/OI consumer in
  this codebase (analyze_trade()'s own liquidity gate, is_liquid() partly,
  parse_market_price, schema_validator.py) already coalesces
  X_fp or X or 0 -- this new code was the one exception, and would have
  silently applied the worst-case 0.50 Kelly multiplier to every live
  trade on a market that only carries the _fp fields (which is the live,
  current-API case), halving position sizes with no error and no log.
  Confirmed via the reviewer's own repro (a genuinely deep book,
  volume_fp=2000/open_interest_fp=3000, correctly liquid but returned 0.50
  pre-fix instead of the correct 1.00). Fixed all 3 call sites
  (paper.liquidity_kelly_scale; cron.py/main.py's
  log-only _liquidity_edge_scale call sites) to match analyze_trade()'s
  exact coalescing pattern. Added 2 new tests proving the _fp names are
  read and take precedence over legacy names when both are present --
  the review's own note: the original tests only exercised plain field
  names, "exactly why they pass while live behavior breaks," so green
  tests alone hadn't caught this. Also surfaced, not fixed here (separate,
  lower-severity, pre-existing): is_liquid() (weather_markets.py) has the
  same plain-names-only gap, masked in practice by its own OR-fallback on
  real bid/ask quote presence -- worth a future look, filed as its own
  consideration rather than silently patched as a drive-by here.
  696 tests pass across the full scoped run (test_tracker.py, test_paper.py,
  test_weather_markets.py, the cron/shadow-prediction cluster,
  test_trade_improvements.py, test_live_execution.py), lint clean.

ENABLEMENT TRIGGER (the actual ask: when to wire gated_edge into
  STRONG/MED/MIN classification instead of adjusted_edge) -- do NOT change
  the classification threshold until:
  1. A meaningful number of settled trades exist with non-NULL gated_edge
     (same sample-floor precedent as every other signal in this file --
     ACCURACY_MIN_SAMPLE=20 / SPRT_MIN_TRADES=20 -- don't invent a lower bar
     just because this signal is new).
  2. A real check has been run against that data: among trades gated_edge
     would have downgraded a tier (STRONG under adjusted_edge but only MED
     or below under gated_edge), did those trades actually perform worse
     (win rate, Brier score) than trades that stayed at the same tier under
     both? If thin-book downgrades really did underperform, that's the
     evidence to wire gated_edge in. If not, close this as not-applicable
     rather than activating it on the mechanism sounding plausible alone --
     same discipline as every other log-only signal's enablement trigger.
  3. liquidity_kelly_scale's own tiers (500/200/50 -> 1.00/0.85/0.70/0.50)
     are equally uncalibrated and worth the same settled-outcome check once
     enough live/paper fills exist under this scale specifically -- not
     blocking since it already fails safe, but worth revisiting.

Problem (as originally scoped, first fragment now stale -- see resolution
above):
  Two already-tracked fragments make one coherent feature:
  - paper.slippage_kelly_scale() (paper.py:1843) is a complete 4-tier
    volume/OI Kelly multiplier with zero callers (see [ORPHANED FUNCTIONS])
    -- DELETED 2026-07-12, no longer exists; see UPDATE above.
  - "Dynamic edge threshold by market liquidity" was planned in
    code_review_plan.md Phase 5, never built (see [MINOR CLEANUP]) --
    still true as of 2026-07-18.
  Net effect today: a signal in a 5-contract-deep book is sized and gated
  identically to one in a 5000-contract book.

What the fix looks like (needs re-scoping, see UPDATE -- this is the
original, now-invalid plan, kept for context):
  Wire slippage_kelly_scale() into the sizing path (paper.py ~600-650);
  scale the effective min-edge requirement up as book depth/volume drops
  (thin books = your own fill moves the price = need more edge). Synergizes
  with maker-execution work: thin books are where maker fills are slowest
  and adverse selection worst.

Why not now (original, superseded -- see resolution above): N/A, resolved.

When to revisit: N/A for the Kelly-size scale (shipped live). See the
  ENABLEMENT TRIGGER above for the edge-threshold divisor (log-only today).

  test_menu_ux.py -- 395 tests) all pass, lint clean.
  Checked all of is_liquid()'s 4 real call sites (main.py:1032 cmd_market
  display flag, main.py:1380 liquid_opps/no_quote_opps split, main.py:1786
  tradeable-liquid summary count, main.py:2249 top-picks filter) -- none
  gate live order placement, so is_liquid()'s own fix is a genuine (if
  small) behavior change in the correct direction: a market with real _fp
  volume and no quotes yet (first-to-post) now correctly counts as liquid.
  Independent opus review clean, given the extra scrutiny warranted by
  is_stale() touching cron.py's real scan loop: confirmed the coalescing
  precedence exactly matches analyze_trade()'s reference gate, confirmed
  no case exists where real liquidity (either field-name convention) gets
  misclassified as stale, confirmed the newly-un-skipped near-close-market
  set has no timeout/rate-limit interaction (cache-warm, CPU-bound,

  just an unused extra key), and ran a broader sweep (holder variables

  was missed. One cosmetic, non-blocking note: is_stale() omits the
  explicit `, 0` default on its plain-volume fallback that is_liquid()
  includes -- functionally identical (the trailing `or 0` covers it
  either way), not worth a follow-up on its own.

FOLLOW-UP BUG, FOUND AND FIXED 2026-07-19 (same day, later -- caught live
via `python main.py cron`, not via review): the fix above corrected the
field NAME (read volume_fp/open_interest_fp, not just legacy volume/
open_interest) but not its TYPE. volume_fp/open_interest_fp are
FixedPointCount strings on the real API (e.g. "10.00"), not numbers --
`market.get("volume_fp") or market.get("volume") or 0` returns that
string as-is when present, and `volume > 0` raises TypeError comparing a
str to an int (no implicit str/int ordering in Python 3). This crashed
cron.py's entire scan loop in production the moment any market actually
had real volume: a live `python main.py cron` run scanned 480 markets,
crashed via is_stale() on the first market with nonzero volume_fp, and
reported "no actionable signals found" -- not because there were none,
but because analysis never got a chance to run for the cycle.
is_liquid() has the identical bug but never crashed in practice --
`has_yes or has_no or volume > 0` short-circuits before reaching
`volume > 0` for any market with real bid/ask quotes, masking it the
same way the original field-name gap was masked.
Root cause of why the original fix's own regression tests didn't catch
this: both new tests added for the fix above used plain Python ints for
volume_fp/open_interest_fp (`"volume_fp": 500`), not strings matching the
real API's FixedPointCount shape -- an int never triggers a str/int
comparison error, only a real API response (or a correctly-typed test
fixture) does. Same lesson as this entry's own "matches Kalshi's real
field names, not just any truthy value" discipline, one level deeper:
matching the field name isn't enough, the fixture's VALUE TYPE has to
match too.
Fixed by wrapping both reads in float(...), matching every other
volume_fp/open_interest_fp reader in this file (analyze_trade's own
liquidity gate, market-implied-distribution weighting). Fixed the 2
existing under-typed tests to use real string fixtures ("500.00" not
500), and added 3 new regression tests reproducing the exact crash
(string volume_fp present and nonzero; string volume_fp present and
genuinely zero, confirming the fix didn't break the zero case;
is_liquid()'s masked equivalent with no quotes so the short-circuit
can't hide it). Mutation-tested both fixes independently by reverting
each float() wrapping and confirming the new tests reproduce the exact
live TypeError, then restoring. Verified end-to-end against the real
crash scenario twice more via actual `python main.py cron` runs (prod
API, TRADING_PAUSED=true so no order-placement risk) -- no crash, and
the resulting gate breakdown (between_no_metar/extreme_price/liquidity/
min_volume/model_mkt_gap/model_spread/retired_method/spread summing to
exactly 480) confirmed every market was legitimately filtered by
pre-existing gates, not silently mis-handled by a lingering bug.
367 tests pass across the full regression sweep (every file touching
is_stale/is_liquid); ruff/ruff format/mypy clean.

Independent second-opinion review (Agent, opus), requested given this
touches the real production scan loop: found the fix above was NOT the
full extent of this bug class -- grepped every .py file (not just
weather_markets.py) for volume_fp/open_interest_fp reads and surfaced 3
more unguarded sites with the identical root cause, none caught by this
session's own earlier review:
  1. weather_markets._liquidity_edge_scale (HIGH) -- both real callers
     (cron.py's cmd_cron, main.py's _analyze_once) pass the raw coalesced
     string straight in; the function's own body does
     `(volume or 0) + (open_interest or 0)`, which on two strings is
     STRING CONCATENATION (no error at that line), then crashes one line
     later at `liq >= 500`. Worse than is_stale()'s bug: a non-empty
     string is always truthy, so this fires even for a genuinely-zero
     "0.00", not just a real nonzero value. This call sits INSIDE the
     exact same cmd_cron scan loop already fixed above, reached only for
     markets that clear every analyze_trade-internal gate -- the day's
     480-market verification run happened to hit zero such markets (hence
     "no crash" was observed), which is exactly why this was missed by
     re-running cron rather than reading the code: the next actionable
     market would have reproduced the identical scan-loop-crashing
     failure this whole entry exists to fix.
  2. main.py's cmd_market whale-alert print (MEDIUM) -- same
     volume/open_interest > threshold comparison, interactive-CLI-only
     (not the live scan loop), but still a real crash on the normal live
     shape.
  3. main.py's cmd_market Vol table column (LOW, cosmetic only) -- no
     crash (tabulate just str()s whatever's in the cell), but displayed
     the raw fixed-point string unconverted instead of a clean number.
  Fixed all 3: _liquidity_edge_scale now converts volume/open_interest to
  float() internally (at the function itself, not each call site, so
  both current callers are fixed by one change and any future caller is
  protected too) -- also dropped its now-inaccurate `: int` type hints,
  since real callers were never passing ints. Whale-alert wrapped in
  float() to match. Vol column wrapped in float() for display
  consistency. 2 new tests for _liquidity_edge_scale (string-input
  addition proven not concatenation; string "0.00" proven not truthy-
  masking a real zero), mutation-tested (reverted the float() wrapping,
  confirmed the exact TypeError reproduces, restored). No dedicated test
  added for the whale-alert/Vol-column fixes (pure CLI display output,
  matching this same code's own prior "not proportionate to unit-test in
  isolation" precedent from the original field-name fix) -- verified
  manually instead against the real API shape.
  416 tests pass across a wider regression sweep (cron/market-implied-
  distribution/p1-remaining/paper/weather_markets/menu-ux/trading test
  files); ruff/ruff format/mypy clean.

Problem (as originally scoped, is_liquid()-only -- scope grew, see
RESOLVED note above):
  Found 2026-07-19 while an opus review of the LIQUIDITY-AWARE SIZING
  feature (entry above) caught a real bug: new code that read only
  market.get("volume")/market.get("open_interest") silently broke on the
  current Kalshi API, which returns volume_fp/open_interest_fp instead.
  Every other volume/OI consumer in this codebase already coalesces
  X_fp or X or 0 (analyze_trade()'s own liquidity gate, parse_market_price,
  schema_validator.py) -- except is_liquid() (weather_markets.py:3810),
  which does `volume = market.get("volume", 0) or 0`, plain-names-only,
  same gap class as the bug just fixed. It hasn't caused a visible
  incident because is_liquid() ORs volume against real bid/ask quote
  presence (`has_yes or has_no or volume > 0`) -- a market with only _fp
  volume but real quotes still returns True via the quote check, masking
  the gap for any market that actually has live prices. The gap only bites
  a market with real _fp volume/OI but genuinely empty bid/ask (a
  first-to-post scenario) -- is_liquid() would incorrectly call it
  illiquid there, even though it may have meaningful open interest.

What it would look like:
  One-line fix: `market.get("volume_fp") or market.get("volume", 0) or 0`,
  matching the exact coalescing pattern already used everywhere else.
  Worth grepping for any other bare `market.get("volume"` /
  `market.get("open_interest"` reads while in there, in case this class of
  gap exists elsewhere too.

Why not now:
  - Masked today (the quote-presence OR covers the common case); not
    causing a live incident. Cheap enough to fix opportunistically next
    time is_liquid() or its test file is open for other reasons, not
    worth a dedicated pass on its own.

When to revisit:
  - Whenever weather_markets.py's liquidity-related code is next open, or
    if a real case of "is_liquid() said illiquid but the market clearly
    had volume" ever gets reported/observed.

[DATA-DRIVEN SIGMA FROM SETTLED HISTORY + CLI-REPORT SETTLEMENT FETCH]

  recorded deferral)

Problem:
  _HISTORICAL_SIGMA is a static city table; sigma feeds gaussian_probability()

  get_historical_sigma() (weather_markets.py:2294-2313) now tries a dynamic

  motivate it.

  Compute per-city (and per-season, matching the existing table's shape)

  back to the static table below a sample-size floor. Build the CLI-report

  sigma gap as a side effect.

When to revisit:
