[RESOLVED 2026-07-20, smallest useful version] JOINT FULL-LADDER BRACKET SELECTION
Priority: was Medium-Low (real EV improvement, real design work)

RESOLVED 2026-07-20: Re-verified before designing anything -- the "Why not
  now" blocker ("sequence after maker-execution + liquidity-aware sizing
  land") was checked directly and confirmed cleared: both landed since
  (2026-07-12 and 2026-07-19 respectively). Also checked how often the
  Problem statement's scenario actually occurs against real trading data
  (predictions.db, ~3 months of live paper trading, 200 real non-shadow
  rows): grouping by (city, target_date, ~10-min scan-cycle bucket) and
  excluding HIGH+LOW pairs (which are NOT mutually exclusive -- a city's
  HIGH and LOW markets settle independently, so per-market-independent
  Kelly is already correct for those, not a gap this entry is about) found
  genuine same-series sibling co-occurrence only 5 times in 3 months
  (Seattle, Houston, Dallas, San Francisco, Phoenix) -- roughly once every
  2-3 weeks, not a frequent problem. Given that low trigger rate, user chose
  the "smallest useful version" this entry's own "What the fix looks like"
  section already named, over the full joint-Kelly/simplex solve (real new
  optimization machinery on a live-money sizing path, for something firing
  ~5x/quarter -- not proportionate).
  Also found the Problem section overstated the gap: paper.
  portfolio_kelly_fraction() already enforces a real per-event capacity
  constraint (MAX_CITY_DATE_EXPOSURE cap, proportional room-scaling,
  directional-concentration penalty, correlated-city penalty), and
  correctly reflects trades placed earlier in the SAME cron cycle (its
  get_city_date_exposure() re-reads live state each call, and
  place_paper_order() writes synchronously before the next opp is
  processed) -- it's greedy/sequential, not jointly optimal, but not "blind"
  to same-cycle siblings either.
  Fix shipped: order_executor._auto_place_trades() now groups opps by
  (city, target_date, var) right after the existing edge*kelly sort (var
  mirrors _score_ensemble_members' HIGH->max/LOW(T)->min ticker convention,
  keeping HIGH/LOW ungrouped). For any group with >1 member, each sibling's
  ci_adjusted_kelly is pre-scaled by its share of the group's total edge
  (equal split if total edge is 0) before being passed into the existing,
  untouched portfolio_kelly_fraction() call -- a bounded, local change (one
  new grouping pass + one multiplication) rather than a new solver or any
  change to portfolio_kelly_fraction()'s own signature/callers.
  4 new tests (tests/test_trading.py): proportional 3:1 edge-ratio split
  hand-computed (0.12*0.75=0.09, 0.12*0.25=0.03), singleton-opp
  backward-compatibility (scale=1.0, unaffected), HIGH+LOW siblings
  confirmed NOT grouped (both keep full room), zero-total-edge equal-split
  fallback. Mutation-tested: reverting the one-line scale multiplication
  was confirmed to break exactly the 2 tests that depend on it (proportional
  split, equal split) while leaving the other 2 (singleton, HIGH/LOW)
  passing, confirming the tests are load-bearing rather than tautological.
  229 tests pass across the wider order_executor/trading regression sweep
  (test_trading, test_shadow_predictions, test_dedup, test_risk_control,
  test_drawdown_tiers, test_execution_proof, test_backlog_batch,
  test_live_execution, test_p0_10_paper_prelog); ruff+mypy clean.

Original problem (kept for history):
  Market analysis is per-bracket independent; nothing chooses the optimal
  COMBINATION of sibling brackets for one city/date against the model's
  full temperature distribution. (The arb auto-trade block in main.py:1542+
  only fires on sum-to-1 violations — different mechanism.) Sequential
  per-market Kelly with position caps is not the same as jointly allocating
  across mutually-exclusive outcomes of one event.

What the fix looks like:
  Group candidate signals by event (city/date/series) before sizing; solve
  the joint Kelly allocation across the group (mutually-exclusive outcomes
  make this a clean simplex problem) instead of greedy per-market sizing.
  Smallest useful version: within an event group, cap total exposure and
  allocate proportionally to per-bracket edge rather than first-come.

Why not now:
  - Real sizing-math design work + touches the same order-placement path as
    several entries above; sequence it after the execution work stabilizes.

When to revisit: N/A -- resolved (smallest useful version shipped). If the
  same-series sibling co-occurrence rate ever climbs materially above the
  observed ~5x/quarter (e.g. once the bot trades more cities/markets
  concurrently), the full joint-Kelly/simplex solve becomes worth
  reconsidering -- re-check the trigger rate against real data rather than
  assuming it changed.

[CLOSED 2026-07-20 -- not a simplification, no concrete use case] WEBSOCKET orderbook_delta get_snapshot -- SIMPLER BOOK INITIALIZATION
Priority: was Low (nice-to-have simplification, not a bug)

CLOSED 2026-07-20: Re-confirmed the 2026-07-12 research finding still
  holds -- there is no REST-call redundancy in kalshi_ws.py's book-init
  path to simplify (it's already snapshot-via-WS, zero REST involvement),
  and this bot still always subscribes up front to every scanned ticker, so
  get_snapshot's narrower "one-off book peek for a ticker outside the
  active subscription list" use case still has no concrete call site.
  Closing outright rather than leaving open with nothing to act on --
  get_snapshot itself isn't going anywhere (it's a standing Kalshi WS
  feature, not a deprecating one), so if a real one-off-peek use case shows
  up later this can be re-opened as a fresh entry with that use case named,
  rather than carried forward indefinitely as a "someday" line with no
  actionable next step.

Original problem (kept for history):
  Kalshi added a get_snapshot action to update_subscription on the
  orderbook_delta WebSocket channel (April 2026): it returns a one-off
  orderbook_snapshot response for requested markets without subscribing to
  them or affecting the existing delta stream. Found 2026-07-10 via web
  search, not yet checked against kalshi_ws.py's current book-init logic in
  detail.

UPDATE 2026-07-12 (research pass, no code changed) -- premise doesn't apply
as originally framed:
  Checked kalshi_ws.py's actual book-init path: there is no separate REST
  call for it at all. The only REST get_orderbook() call anywhere
  (kalshi_client.py:346) is used once, in main.py's `analyze` CLI command
  (main.py:1262), purely to print a human-readable orderbook table -- it has
  nothing to do with the live WS trading pipeline. Confirmed via
  docs.kalshi.com/websockets/orderbook-updates that subscribing to
  orderbook_delta for a ticker already triggers Kalshi's own automatic
  orderbook_snapshot message first, then incremental deltas -- and
  kalshi_ws.py's parse_message() already handles that exact
  "orderbook_snapshot" message type (kalshi_ws.py:88). So there's no
  REST-call redundancy to remove; book init is already snapshot-via-WS with
  zero REST involvement.
  get_snapshot's real, narrower value for this bot: a one-off book peek for
  a ticker that is NOT in the persistent per-cycle subscription list (e.g.
  previewing a candidate market's current book before deciding whether to
  add it to cron.py's per-cycle _ws.subscribe() call), without growing the
  subscription list or opening a second connection. That's a smaller,
  different use case than "simpler book initialization" as originally
  framed -- there's no current call site that needs it (this bot always
  subscribes up front to every scanned ticker), so it stays a nice-to-have
  pending a concrete use case, not a simplification of existing code.

What the fix looks like:
  No current call site needs this. If a future feature wants a one-off book
  check for a ticker outside the active subscription list (rather than
  simplifying anything that exists today), use update_subscription's
  get_snapshot action for that instead of adding a new REST call or growing
  the persistent subscription list.

Why not now:
  - Unverified against this repo's actual current book-init code path;
    purely a simplification if it applies, no functional gap being closed.
  - Re-verified 2026-07-12: it doesn't apply as a simplification (there's no
    existing REST-call redundancy to remove) -- only relevant if/when a
    concrete one-off-book-peek use case appears.

When to revisit: N/A -- closed. Re-open as a new entry if a concrete
  one-off-book-peek use case (outside the active subscription list) ever
  actually appears.

[PUBLIC TRADE-FLOW SIGNAL]
Priority: Low-Medium (cheap to capture, speculative value)

Problem:
  kalshi_ws.py subscribes only to ticker + orderbook_delta (line 301);
  Kalshi's public `trade` channel (executed trades feed) is unused. Signed
  taker flow between scans would show when someone with a faster pipeline
  moved first on a model run — useful as a caution flag (widen required
  edge) or confirmation (market converging toward our stale signal).

What the fix looks like:
  Add the trade channel to the WS subscription, accumulate signed flow per
  ticker between scans, expose to analyze_trade() as a small adjustment or
  gate input. Evaluate on paper before giving it any weight.

Why not now:
  - Value unproven; WS client currently only runs during watch mode, so
    coverage between manual cron runs is zero anyway — worth more once the
    bot runs continuously.

When to revisit:
  - Once loop/watch runs continuously again post-Belgium.

[NWS AFD (AREA FORECAST DISCUSSION) PARSING]
Priority: Low (stretch/novel — highest differentiation, least proven)

Problem:
  Each WFO publishes an AFD where human forecasters state confidence and
  explicit disagreement with model guidance ("models overmixing, expect
  highs 2-3F below guidance") — exactly the correction the recurring
  NWS-bias investigations hunt for statistically, published free per city
  per day. Nothing consumes it.

What the fix looks like:
  Fetch AFDs via the same IEM afos API already scoped for the CLI-report
  fetch (shared city->WFO table — build once for both). LLM-extract a
  per-city confidence score + directional lean vs guidance; feed as a
  small bounded blend adjustment, gated behind tracked accuracy like any
  other source.

Why not now:
  - Adds an LLM dependency + per-day API cost to the pipeline; extraction
    quality needs its own evaluation before the signal can be trusted;
    depends on the same WFO table as the CLI-report fetch (build together).

When to revisit:
  - Alongside the CLI-report fetch (shared infrastructure), or as a fun
    standalone experiment scored in shadow mode first.

[CITY-LOCAL AFTERNOON SAME-DAY SWEEP]
Priority: Low (mostly covered by loop/watch when they run)

Problem:
  By early afternoon a day's high is substantially determined and METAR
  lock-in gets very sharp, but there is no scan timed to each city's local
  ~2pm. loop (every 4h) and watch (every 5min) cover this incidentally when
  running; the manual-cron cadence does not.

What the fix looks like:
  A lightweight `cron --sameday-only` mode (skip multi-day scan + batch
  prewarm; METAR + same-day markets only) cheap enough to run at each
  city's local afternoon window, or an extra loop-mode wake timed to the
  2pm ET / 2pm PT bands.

Why not now:
  - Marginal over a continuously-running loop; only meaningfully valuable
    during manual-cadence periods like the current trip.

UPDATE 2026-07-20 (research pass, no code changed) -- premise checked
  against live state and found weaker than "valuable during manual-cadence
  periods like the current trip" implies:
  - Confirmed TRADING_PAUSED=true right now (.env), and is_trading_paused()
    gates _auto_place_trades() entirely -- no paper or live trade is placed
    regardless of when cron runs, until Belgium return (2026-07-31). This
    feature's actual point (catch the same-day lock-in signal before it's
    missed so a trade can be placed on it) is inactive for the whole
    remaining window it would otherwise help with. The only live value

    since a later same-day scan produces an equally or more confident

  - Likely superseded, not just delayed: this entry's own "why not now"
    already scopes the value to manual-cadence gaps specifically -- and the
    already-decided fix for manual-cadence unreliability is the MOVE OFF
    LOCAL CRON entry (VM running `watch --auto --live` continuously).
    Once that lands, watch's 5-minute cadence covers every city's local
    afternoon window for free and this feature has no remaining job.
    Building it now risks throwaway work for the gap between today and
    whichever of (Belgium return, VM move) happens first.
  - Recommendation if picked up again: re-check both triggers (has
    TRADING_PAUSED cleared? has the VM move executed?) before building --
    if the VM move has landed, close this as superseded rather than

When to revisit:

[RESOLVED 2026-07-17] REAL NBM VIA IEM NBS STATION BULLETINS -- REPLACE THE SILENT best_match SUBSTITUTE
Priority: was Medium-High -- the bot believed it had an "nbm" ensemble
  member; it actually had an arbitrary auto-selected model.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  fetch_temperature_nbm() no longer fetched NBM at all -- Open-Meteo removed
  the model -- and requested models: "best_match" instead, an uncalibrated
  auto-selection, yet still fed model_temps["nbm"] in analyze_trade's
  Phase-C extended ensemble and _compute_ensemble_spread. mos.py already
  integrated IEM's MOS API but only ever requested GFS/NAM.

CORRECTION during implementation -- the original entry's field-name claim
  was wrong:
  This entry's own "Live-verified 2026-07-16" note claimed NBS rows carry
  "n_x (the NBM day-max/night-min field)". Re-verified live 2026-07-17
  against 7 stations across all 4 CONUS timezones: n_x is None on every
  single NBS row, for every station. The actual field carrying the daily
  extreme is "txn" (confirmed against IEM's raw CSV export, where it's an
  unlabeled trailing column matching the classic NWS raw-MOS-bulletin "X/N"
  convention), and it is populated only on rows whose forecast-valid time
  lands exactly on a 00Z or 12Z boundary -- not a dedicated always-present
  field the way n_x was assumed to be. This also meant the "Why not now"
  risk below (per-station 12-hourly semantics, same timezone care as CLI
  settlement) was real and had to be solved, not just verified-and-shipped:
  which of the 00Z/12Z rows is the local daytime max vs. nighttime min
  depends on each station's UTC offset in general, but empirically (checked
  KNYC/Eastern, KMDW/Central, KDEN/Mountain, KLAX/Pacific) the 00Z-ending
  12h period is ALWAYS the higher (max) value and 12Z-ending ALWAYS the
  lower (min), station-timezone-independent -- because CONUS UTC offsets
  are always whole hours, so each station's ~12h local daytime window
  always falls entirely inside one UTC-anchored period or the other, never
  split. This is a genuine, verified, general rule for all 20 traded
  cities, not a KNYC-specific coincidence.

What shipped:
  mos.py: new _fetch_nbs_daily_extremes(station, city_tz) parses every
  available txn row into {(local_date, "max"|"min"): temp_f} using the
  00Z=max/12Z=min rule above (local_date computed by converting ftime to
  the station's timezone and taking .date(), which safely lands inside the
  12h period without crossing local midnight for any CONUS zone). Cached
  per (station, city_tz), 1h TTL, matching _MOS_CACHE_TTL. New public
  fetch_nbm_iem(station, target_date, city_tz, var) wraps it. Also removed
  two now-redundant local `from datetime import UTC, datetime` imports
  mos.py had (dead weight once UTC/datetime moved to the top-level import
  this entry's datetime.strptime parsing needed anyway).

  weather_markets.fetch_temperature_nbm() now tries fetch_nbm_iem() first
  (via _metar_station_for_city(city), which covers all 20 traded cities --
  NOT mos.py's 6-city _MOS_CITIES subset used by GFS/NAM MOS, per this
  entry's original "extend beyond" note), and only falls back to the old
  Open-Meteo best_match substitute when NBS has no coverage for that
  station/date (expected for same-day markets -- NBS's own forecast
  horizon is short and same-day rows are frequently absent in the current
  cycle; the METAR pipeline already covers same-day elsewhere in this
  codebase). No changes needed to analyze_trade's Phase-C ensemble or
  _compute_ensemble_spread -- both already consume fetch_temperature_nbm()'s
  return value, so the real-vs-substitute swap is fully transparent to them
  ("wire it in now" was the explicit choice made here, not log-only-first,
  since this replaces an already-live-blended signal's data source rather
  than introducing a brand-new one).

  Tests: tests/test_mos_nbs.py -- the 00Z=max/12Z=min rule verified against
  both an Eastern and a Pacific station (proving it's genuinely
  timezone-derived, not hardcoded), a mutation-proof swapped-assignment
  check, off-cycle/missing-txn row handling, cache-hit/network-failure
  behavior. tests/test_nbm.py updated (the IEM path is tried first, so its
  two pre-existing Open-Meteo-mock tests needed mos.fetch_nbm_iem patched
  to return None to keep exercising the fallback path they were written
  for) plus two new tests for the IEM-first preference and the
  no-station-mapped skip path. Mutation-tested the max/min assignment by
  hand-flipping it and confirming 6 of the new tests fail with the exact
  expected wrong values, then reverting.

  Drive-by fix: tests/test_forecasting.py's
  test_log_prediction_called_with_forecast_cycle (an AST-based check that
  main.py's log_prediction call passes forecast_cycle=) was stale --
  broken by the 2026-07-17 LOG_PREDICTION KWARGS ASSEMBLY TRIPLICATED
  consolidation (main.py now passes it via
  **_prediction_kwargs_from_analysis(...), not a literal keyword) but not
  caught at the time because that session's test run didn't include this
  file. Updated the AST check to accept either form; mutation-tested by
  stripping the unpack from main.py and confirming the test fails, then
  reverting via git checkout.

  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) before commit, matching this
  project's standard for anything touching a live probability-blend input.
  Confirmed the core claims sound (00Z=max/12Z=min holds for every CONUS
  offset including Phoenix's no-DST America/Phoenix, no off-by-one-day in
  the local-date attribution, tests genuinely correct not just plausible)
  and caught one real bug fixed before commit: fetch_temperature_nbm's
  Open-Meteo fallback opportunistically dual-writes both max and min
  _NBM_CACHE entries from one HTTP response (an existing optimization,
  pre-dating this entry) -- but NBS has per-var coverage gaps at its ~3-day
  horizon edge (a date can have a real IEM max with no IEM min yet, or vice
  versa), so the unconditional dual-write could silently clobber a real,
  already-cached IEM value with the Open-Meteo best_match placeholder,
  order-dependently, with no error raised -- reintroducing the exact bug
  this entry exists to fix. Fixed: the fallback now only opportunistically
  writes the OTHER var's cache slot when it isn't already fresh. Added
  tests/test_nbm.py::test_openmeteo_fallback_does_not_clobber_iem_value_for_other_var,
  mutation-tested by restoring the old unconditional-dual-write and
  confirming it fails (60.0 instead of the real 81.0), then reverting.
  Also hardened mos.py's ftime parsing per the review's second finding: if
  IEM ever changes the timestamp format, every txn row would silently fail
  to parse and the feature would permanently no-op to the Open-Meteo
  fallback with no signal -- now logs a warning when every txn-bearing row
  fails to parse, rather than looking identical to genuine no-coverage.

Known residual (not fixed here, correctly out of scope):
  - Pairs naturally with the NBM PROBABILISTIC QUANTILES entry below (same
    IEM/NBM surface, still open) -- scope together if picked up next.
  - fetch_mos()'s existing GFS/NAM path filters rows by
    `ftime.startswith(date_str)` where ftime is UTC and date_str is
    typically a local target date -- a latent timezone bug distinct from
    this entry's txn/n_x issue, not touched here. Worth its own backlog
    entry if revisited.
  - A pre-existing, unrelated flaky test was discovered and fixed in a
    separate commit: tests/test_data_freshness.py::
    test_enrich_with_forecast_stamps_data_fetched_at was failing when run
    in the same session after tests/test_forecasting.py (two tests in
    TestDynamicCacheTTL wrote directly into weather_markets' shared
    _forecast_cache/_ensemble_cache singletons without cleanup, leaking a
    stale cached timestamp into any later test hitting the same
    ("NYC","2026-04-15") key). Fixed via an autouse fixture that
    snapshots/restores both caches around that test class.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-17] DISCRETIZATION-CONSISTENT T-BUCKET THRESHOLDS -- HALF-DEGREE CONTINUITY
Priority: was Medium-High -- systematic, direction-consistent probability
  skew on every tail-bucket trade; bordered a correctness issue, not just a
  feature idea.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  _parse_market_condition already reasons explicitly about integer
  settlement for between-buckets -- B87.5 -> [86.5, 88.5], with a comment
  that brackets "must tile without gaps" (weather_markets.py:3719-3723).
  But T-buckets kept raw integer thresholds: T92 -> {"above", 92.0}, and
  every prob path taking condition raw (_forecast_probability,
  ensemble_cdf_prob, EMOS, nws_prob, ...) used that raw value directly,
  so the ladder didn't tile under the code's own between-bucket
  convention -- dropping probability mass near every tail-bucket boundary.

CORRECTION during implementation -- the original "What it would look
  like" below had the sign backwards:
  This entry's own original proposal ("above: val-0.5; below: val+0.5")
  was never live-verified and turned out to be wrong. Before writing any
  code, fetched real rules_primary text from 8 live Kalshi T-bucket
  markets across 4 cities (KXHIGHNY/CHI/DEN/MIA) via the API. Every
  sample showed the same pattern: a "T{val} above" ticker's actual rule
  is "greater than {val}" -- e.g. T86 "above" has subtitle "87° or above"
  and rules_primary "is greater than 86" -- meaning integer settlement
  must be val+1 or higher, not val or higher as this entry originally
  assumed. Matching the between-bucket code's own already-committed
  tiling convention (a "85-86" between-bucket is B85.5 -> [84.5, 86.5]),
  the correct continuous boundary is val+0.5 for above and val-0.5 for
  below -- the OPPOSITE sign from the original proposal. Shipping the
  original proposal as written would have shifted every T-bucket
  threshold a full 1.0°F in the wrong direction (turning a 0.5°F bug into
  a 1.0°F bug on the other side), not fixed it. Full ladder check around
  a boundary: T67-below (wins <=66) -> 66.5; B67.5 -> {67,68}; T68-above
  (wins >=69) -> 68.5. Integer 68 lands in exactly B67.5 and not in
  T68-above (68 > 68.5 is false) -- tiles with no gap or overlap.

What shipped:
  _parse_market_condition (weather_markets.py) now returns a second,
  sibling key on above/below condition dicts: "prob_threshold" (val+0.5 /
  val-0.5), alongside the existing "threshold" (raw ticker/rule value,
  UNCHANGED). Deliberately did not mutate "threshold" in place -- several
  consumers must keep comparing against the literal raw rule value
  (tracker.audit_settlement's archive cross-check against Kalshi's actual
  rule text, weather_markets._metar_lock_in's same-day METAR lockout
  check, and condition_threshold= DB/logging bookkeeping in
  main.py/order_executor.py) and mutating threshold would have silently
  corrupted all three. A single shared helper, utils.prob_threshold(condition)
  (falls back to raw "threshold" for between/precip conditions, which
  don't have "prob_threshold"), is now the one place every genuine
  continuous-probability consumer reads from, instead of each site
  reimplementing its own shift/fallback -- avoiding the
  triplicated-logic-one-drifts pattern already hit elsewhere in this file
  (LOG_PREDICTION KWARGS, KALSHI CENTS/DOLLARS NORMALIZATION). Updated
  every genuine probability-math call site: ensemble_cdf_prob,
  _forecast_probability, _bootstrap_ci, _get_consensus_probs (model-
  consensus safety gate), analyze_trade's EMOS exceedance/interval calls,
  raw ensemble-fraction fallback, gaussian_probability call, extended-
  ensemble (NBM/ECMWF) raw fraction, near-threshold detection, the
  climate-index adj_condition shift (now shifts both threshold and
  prob_threshold by index_adj so they stay consistent), and the
  persistence-baseline _tlo lookup -- plus nws.py's nws_prob and
  obs_prob, climatology.py's _climatological_prob_inner, and backtest.py
  (so backtest results keep matching live behavior). Confirmed
  audit_settlement, _metar_lock_in, settlement_monitor.py, and the DB/
  logging call sites were left untouched and still read raw "threshold".
  Tests (tests/test_weather.py): parse-time above/below prob_threshold
  values, a tiling-identity test (between-bucket upper == adjacent
  T-bucket's prob_threshold, live-ticker-verified), utils.prob_threshold's
  fallback behavior, and mutation-proof tests for _forecast_probability
  and ensemble_cdf_prob (forecast/members placed exactly in the old
  gap -- verified these fail if the fix is reverted, by actually
  reverting one line, running the suite, confirming the expected failure,
  then restoring it).

  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) before commit: re-derived the
  sign/magnitude from the tiling argument independently (confirmed
  correct), audited every touched call site (confirmed each is a genuine
  probability computation, not a should-stay-raw site), searched for
  missed consumers, and checked the None-handling `or 0` idiom used at
  two sites for a silent-remap-of-a-real-0.0-threshold bug (confirmed
  safe -- T-ticker thresholds are always half-integers, never exactly
  0.0, and both sites are already type-guarded so the fallback can't
  fire on a real market anyway). No bugs found.

Known residual (not fixed here, correctly out of scope):
  - sigma_audit.py's _forecast_prob() replicates the Gaussian CDF from DB
    columns threshold_lo/threshold_hi, which tracker.py populates from
    the raw (unshifted) threshold by design -- so this diagnostic-only
    script still carries the same tail skew. Revisit if/when sigma_audit
    output is used for more than diagnostics.
  - nws.py's nws_prob_from_quantiles() is dead code (only referenced by
    tests/docs/backlog, not wired into analyze_trade or any live path,
    confirmed via the existing NBM PROBABILISTIC QUANTILES entry above).
    If it's ever wired in, its caller must pass prob_threshold, not raw
    threshold.
  - Calibration-reset interplay (per-city Platt/temperature scaling may
    have been partially absorbing the average skew this fixes) not
    separately audited post-ship -- watch get_calibration_by_city /
    condition-type Brier over the next batch of settled trades per this
    entry's original note.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-19] AMEND ORDER (V2) -- REPLACE CANCEL-VERIFY-REPLACE IN THE REPRICE LOOP
Priority: was Medium -- removes the exact client-side race window the
  reprice feature needed hardened plumbing to work around, and halves
  write-call count per reprice.

RESOLVED 2026-07-19:
  Re-verified the endpoint shape against Kalshi's live docs before coding
  (https://docs.kalshi.com/api-reference/orders/amend-order-v2) rather than
  trusting this entry's 2026-07-16 summary alone -- confirmed POST
  /portfolio/events/orders/{order_id}/amend, request {ticker, side, price,
  count, client_order_id?, updated_client_order_id?, exchange_index?},
  response {order_id, client_order_id, remaining_count?, fill_count?,
  average_fill_price?, average_fee_paid?, ts_ms}. One clarification the
  original entry didn't capture: count is NOT "how many more to add" --
  it's the order's TOTAL desired fillable count (already-filled +
  desired-remaining-resting), the same semantics as create-order's count.
  For this bot's only use (reprice at an unchanged quantity), that means
  passing the same count used at original placement, unchanged -- Kalshi
  computes the filled/still-resting split internally.
  Shipped kalshi_client.amend_order() (V2 fixed-point body via the existing
  _to_v2_side_price mapping, deterministic updated_client_order_id via the
  same hash-based idempotency pattern as place_order, client_order_id
  included only when the caller has it) and order_executor._amend_live_order
  (mirrors _replace_live_order's gate-recheck + execution_log bookkeeping
  shape). Wired into _reprice_or_cancel_pending_orders's reprice-improve
  branch only (same order, new price) -- the taker-cross branch stays on
  cancel+replace exactly as before, since it changes time_in_force to
  immediate_or_cancel, a different order type amend cannot express, matching
  this entry's own original scoping.
  Execution_log design decision (surfaced via AskUserQuestion -- amend keeps
  the SAME exchange order_id, unlike cancel+replace's genuinely-new one, so
  this needed a real call): user chose the "new row, chained via
  replaces_order_id" option over "update the row in place", matching this
  entry's own "Log replaces_order_id chains the same way" plan. The old
  row gets a new status="amended" (deliberately distinct from "canceled" --
  the original order was never actually canceled, just repriced).
  Found and fixed a real live-money correctness gap this design choice
  would otherwise have introduced, caught by tracing every consumer of
  orders.status before finalizing the new status string (per
  [[feedback_trace_all_call_sites]]): execution_log.get_today_live_spend()
  (the MAX_DAILY_SPEND gate's data source) sums quantity*price across every
  row NOT IN ('failed','canceled','cancelled') -- 'amended' wasn't in that
  exclusion list, so an amended order's old row AND its new row would both
  count, double-counting the same resting position's capital on every
  reprice and inflating the live spend cap toward premature (fail-safe-
  direction, not fail-unsafe, but still a real bug) halts. Fixed by adding
  'amended' to that query's exclusion list. Checked every other
  orders.status consumer in execution_log.py (was_recently_ordered,
  was_traded_today, was_ordered_this_cycle: harmless either way, since the
  new row already signals "traded" regardless of the old row's status;
  get_open_live_positions's exact status='pending' match and
  order_executor._count_open_live_orders's exact status='pending' match:
  both naturally exclude 'amended' already, no change needed) -- only
  get_today_live_spend needed the fix.
  Adjacency note, NOT fixed (flagging per this project's convention rather
  than silently folding it in): execution_log.log_order_result() always
  overwrites response/error/error_code/error_type (not COALESCEd) even when
  the caller only means to update status -- _amend_live_order's mark-old-
  row-as-"amended" call inherits this same pre-existing behavior already
  present in _finalize_cancel's cancel-marking call (nulls out the old
  row's response JSON on every cancel too, not something this change
  introduced). Worth a real fix if execution_log.py is next open for
  other reasons.
  Not verified against DEMO_BASE (no live/demo order was actually placed) --
  ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False and TRADING_PAUSED throughout this session, same
  as every other live-order-path change to date; implemented and tested
  against the documented shape (live docs fetch above), matching how the
  original V2 create/cancel migration was done. Worth a real demo-order
  smoke test whenever live trading is actually being prepared to resume.
  20 new tests: kalshi_client.amend_order() body construction (V2 side/price
  mapping reused correctly, client_order_id included/omitted correctly,
  updated_client_order_id deterministic+idempotent, raw response passthrough
  -- tests/test_kalshi_client.py::TestAmendOrder, 7 tests);
  order_executor._resolve_amend_status's fill/no-fill/partial-fill/
  unparseable boundary cases (4 tests, mutation-tested by flipping the
  remaining_count<=0 comparison and confirming the boundary test fails for
  the right reason, then restoring); get_today_live_spend's 'amended'
  exclusion (2 tests, one directly proving the double-count bug by running
  the pre-fix query alongside the real one and asserting they diverge);
  updated 2 existing reprice-branch tests
  (test_rested_past_blanket_gate_but_not_taker_gate_reprices_not_crosses,
  test_price_moved_reprices_as_new_maker_order) from asserting cancel_order/
  place_order calls to asserting amend_order calls, since those tests were
  exercising an implementation detail (the mechanism) that genuinely
  changed by design, not just an outcome; replaced
  test_fill_race_during_cancel_skips_replacement (which tested the
  cancel+verify fill-race protection this change makes moot for the
  reprice-improve branch -- amend's atomicity closes that race window by
  construction) with test_amend_that_crosses_the_book_is_logged_as_filled,
  proving the analogous scenario (amend's own price change immediately
  crosses the book) is read correctly from the SAME atomic response instead
  of a separate verification call; added 2 new execution_log bookkeeping
  tests for the amend success/failure paths (old row -> "amended" only on
  success, left "pending" on failure so a future cycle can retry).
  602 tests pass across the full scoped regression sweep (every test file
  touching order_executor.py/kalshi_client.py/execution_log.py); ruff +
  ruff format + mypy clean.
  Independent second-opinion review (Agent, opus) caught one real issue
  before push: _amend_live_order's try/except wrapped BOTH the exchange
  amend_order() call AND the two subsequent execution_log bookkeeping
  writes in one block -- if the exchange call succeeded but a bookkeeping
  write then raised (e.g. a genuine SQLite "database is locked", plausible
  given web_app.py's dashboard and the WS thread can touch the same DB
  concurrently), the new row got marked "failed" even though the order had
  genuinely repriced live on the exchange, orphaning it (never picked up
  again by _poll_pending_orders' status='pending' filter). Fixed by
  splitting into two try/except blocks: only the amend_order() call itself
  can produce a "failed" classification and a False return; once a
  response is in hand, a bookkeeping failure is logged loudly (error, not
  warning) but the function still returns True, since the exchange-side
  reality is what matters for whether a future cycle should retry.
  New regression test (test_amend_exchange_success_survives_bookkeeping_
  failure) mocks execution_log.log_order_result to raise after a
  successful amend_order() call and asserts True is still returned --
  mutation-tested by reverting to the single-try-block shape and
  confirming the test fails with the exact predicted symptom (an
  unhandled RuntimeError instead of a clean True), then restoring. 126
  tests pass in the two most directly affected files after the fix; ruff/
  ruff format/mypy clean.

Problem (as originally scoped, still accurate for historical context):
  kalshi_client.py exposes only place/get/cancel (place_order :401,
  get_order :551, cancel_order :560) -- no amend. So
  _reprice_or_cancel_pending_orders (order_executor.py:779) does a
  3-step cancel -> verify-unfilled -> replace via
  _cancel_and_verify_safe_to_replace (order_executor.py:683), whose
  fill-race handling required threading raw API status through
  _finalize_cancel (the 2026-07-12 review's fix #3) and still leaves the
  "fills exactly as the post-cancel verification query fails" settlement
  gap that got spawned as its own follow-up. Verified via docs search
  2026-07-16: Kalshi has Amend Order (V2) -- POST
  /trade-api/v2/portfolio/events/orders/{order_id}/amend (same V2
  events-orders family this repo migrated to on 2026-07-12), body
  {ticker, side, price, count, client_order_id, updated_client_order_id},
  response {order_id, remaining_count, fill_count, ts_ms}; plus a
  separate Decrease Order endpoint. Amend is a single atomic exchange-side
  operation -- no client-side window where the order is gone-but-not-
  replaced or filled-mid-sequence.

What it would look like (DONE 2026-07-19, see resolution above):
  Add amend_order() to kalshi_client.py (V2 fixed-point shape -- read the
  live docs page for exact field encoding before coding, same caution as
  the create/cancel migration); in _reprice_or_cancel_pending_orders, use
  amend for the reprice-improve branch (same order, new price) and keep
  cancel+IOC-replace only for the taker-cross branch (different order
  type). Log replaces_order_id chains the same way (execution_log already
  has the column).

Why not now (resolved):
  - Docs note queue position is preserved only on size decrease (price
    amends go to the back -- no queue-priority win, "only" atomicity +
    rate-limit savings); ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE=False means no live orders
    exist to reprice yet, so this naturally batched with the next
    order-path session (this one). Not verified against DEMO_BASE (no
    live/demo order was actually placed this session) -- worth a real
    demo-order smoke test whenever live trading is actually being
    prepared to resume; see resolution above.

When to revisit:
  - N/A, closed. If DEMO_BASE verification is wanted before live trading
    resumes, that's the one remaining piece -- see resolution above.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] MARKET-IMPLIED TEMPERATURE DISTRIBUTION FROM THE FULL LADDER
Priority: was Medium -- turns data already fetched every scan into a
  per-event consensus signal; cheap, log-only ship.

POST-RESOLUTION REGRESSION, FIXED 2026-07-19 (see the "is_liquid() (AND 4
  MORE SITES)..." entry for the full narrative): fit_market_implied_
  distribution()'s weighting line read plain market.get("volume") only,
  never the current API's volume_fp -- so on real live data every sibling
  bracket's weight computed as 0, and the fit almost certainly returned
  None on every real scan since it shipped below. The "verified...
  essentially exact" claim in the original resolution was true of the fit
  math (checked against synthetic fixtures using plain "volume"), but
  those fixtures never matched real API field-name shape, so the bug was
  invisible to the test suite that shipped with this feature. Fixed with
  the same `volume_fp or volume or 0` coalescing used everywhere else in
  this codebase, plus a new regression test built from live-API-shaped
  fixtures (volume_fp only, no "volume" key) confirming a real fit comes
  back. Lesson for future signals in this codebase: a synthetic-fixture
  test proving the MATH is correct is not the same as proving the
  function works against real API data shape -- verify field names
  against a real live payload (or at least against analyze_trade()'s own
  known-correct coalescing pattern) before calling a new market-data
  consumer "verified."

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: shipped as scoped in "What it would look like" below,
  with two design decisions surfaced to and confirmed by the user via
  AskUserQuestion first (call-site scope; liquidity-weight field), plus one
  reversal caught by re-deriving rather than restating a first-pass
  recommendation (the delta column -- see below).
  weather_markets.fit_market_implied_distribution(siblings) fits a Normal
  (mean, sigma) by weighted least squares: each liquid bracket's mid-price
  is the implied probability mass over its threshold (above/below/between),
  weighted by volume (chosen over open_interest because is_liquid() -- the
  same function gating the thin-book floor -- only ever checks volume,
  keeping one definition of liquidity instead of introducing a second).
  Reuses _forecast_probability's exact above/below/between mass formula
  conceptually, but reimplements it as a vectorized numpy expression rather
  than calling it per-point per-optimizer-iteration: profiling showed scipy.
  stats.norm.cdf's per-call overhead dominates (~200ms/fit via the
  non-vectorized version vs ~29ms vectorized, for a 6-bracket event) --
  documented inline so a future reader doesn't "simplify" it back to the
  slow, more-obviously-DRY version. weather_markets.
  compute_market_implied_distributions(markets) groups a scan's full market
  list by (city, date) via parse_city_date and fits each event once.
  Verified against a synthetic ladder built from a known Normal(70,5) (and
  separately an all-"between" ladder, since real weather markets are
  commonly all-between with no above/below siblings at all): fit recovered
  (70.0009, 5.0013) -- essentially exact.
  Wired into predictions via 3 new columns (implied_mean, implied_sigma,
  fit_residual -- migration v43/v44/v45, tracker.log_prediction()) and
  order_executor._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis (reads a.get(
  "market_implied"), doesn't compute it -- can't, since a single-market
  analysis dict has no sibling visibility).
  Scope decision (confirmed via AskUserQuestion): computed only in the two
  full-scan paths, cron.py's cmd_cron and main.py's _analyze_once (the
  cmd_watch path) -- each already holds the full sibling ladder for free
  from one get_weather_markets() call, computed once before the per-market
  loop/ThreadPoolExecutor starts and attached onto each market's own
  analysis["market_implied"] during the loop. Deliberately NOT wired into
  cmd_market/cmd_order's single-market lookups -- those never see siblings
  and forcing an extra live fetch to backfill a log-only research signal
  onto an interactive/order-placement path wasn't worth it; their rows
  simply log NULL for these 3 columns, matching the entry's own "every
  scan" framing.
  Liquidity-weight and delta-column decisions were reviewed a second time
  at the user's request ("review your recommendations") rather than just
  restated: the liquidity-weight choice (volume) held up, strengthened by
  tracing is_liquid()'s actual logic (see above). The delta-column
  decision reversed: tracing forecast_temp_f's real source (analysis.get(
  "forecast_temp"), a plain temperature for above/below/between markets --
  precip's own path reuses the same key for inches, but that's out of
  scope here) showed implied_mean - forecast_temp_f is a trivial
  single-column subtraction between two already-stored scalars, unlike
  run_trend_delta's genuinely-computed multi-point statistic -- storing it
  as a 4th column would buy no real query simplification, so it was
  dropped from the plan; compute it on demand when the correlation check
  eventually runs.
  A live-fetch attempt to verify the volume-vs-open_interest choice
  empirically against real current market data failed cleanly (this
  environment has no KALSHI_API_KEY configured) -- documented as a real
  gap rather than silently treated as verified; the code-precedent
  argument (is_liquid() consistency) stood in for it.
  Real bug caught by the scoped test run, not by review: cron.py's/main.py's
  new `enriched.get("_date").isoformat()` lookup crashed with AttributeError
  on a live test (test_cron_integration.py::test_cron_gate_allows_when_
  adjusted_edge_above_threshold) whose hand-built enriched fixture used a
  plain ISO string for _date instead of a real date object --
  enrich_with_forecast() itself always sets a real date object, but nothing
  guarantees every "enriched"-shaped dict a test hands to this code does.
  Fixed by tolerating both (hasattr(_ev_date, "isoformat")) at both call
  sites rather than "fixing" the test to match an assumption the code
  shouldn't have made in the first place.
  New tests/test_market_implied_distribution.py (13 tests: known-distribution
  recovery for a mixed and an all-between ladder, thin-book gate, zero-
  volume/illiquid/non-temperature exclusion, a mutation check that volume
  actually weights the fit not just reads it, degenerate-fit rejection, and
  event grouping). Extended tests/test_prediction_kwargs.py (3 tests) and
  tests/test_tracker.py (3 tests, mirroring TestLogPredictionRunTrend).
  Scoped test run: the new file plus test_prediction_kwargs.py,
  test_tracker.py (full, 219 tests), the cron/shadow-prediction cluster
  (test_cron_integration.py, test_cron_group_c.py, test_cron_trade_updates.py,
  test_main_cron_smoke.py, test_shadow_predictions.py, test_dedup.py,
  test_cron_lock.py, test_prelog.py, test_p0_16_cron_endpoint.py),
  test_p1_remaining.py (_analyze_once coverage), and test_weather_markets.py/
  test_price_and_size.py for regression -- all pass except the one
  pre-existing, unrelated TestTemperatureTradeWiring failure already known
  from earlier in this session (confirmed via git stash before this work
  started).
  Log-only -- never wired into blended_prob/sigma/kelly. See ENABLEMENT
  TRIGGER below (unchanged from the original scoping) for what's required
  before that would ever be considered.
  Independent opus review (Agent) came back clean -- verified the fit's
  above/below/between sign conventions match _forecast_probability exactly,
  the +-inf handling in the vectorized norm.cdf call produces no NaN
  (checked under -W error::RuntimeWarning), the liquidity/volume gating
  composition has no off-by-one, the _ev_date_iso fix produces no dict-key
  mismatch between the real-date and test-double-string cases, the shared
  _market_implied_by_event dict is genuinely read-only from the
  ThreadPoolExecutor workers' perspective, the migration is balanced (35
  INSERT columns, 34 placeholders, 1 via datetime('now')), no code path
  serializes/iterates the full analysis dict in a way the new nested
  "market_implied" key could break, and the new tests are real inversions
  (not tautological). One minor, deliberately-left-as-is note: only
  implied_sigma is range-validated before a fit is accepted (0.1-50.0);
  implied_mean isn't -- fine per the reviewer's own assessment since this
  column is strictly log-only today, but worth a mental note if this
  signal is ever wired into anything that reads implied_mean directly.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  Every market comparison is per-bracket: parse_market_price mid
  (weather_markets.py:3083-3128) vs model prob, with per-market anchors
  _MARKET_ANCHOR_BETWEEN/ABOVE/BELOW (weather_markets.py:173-175).
  Nothing ever inverts the full sibling ladder (all brackets of one
  city/date, already fetched in the same scan) into a market-implied
  temperature distribution -- implied mean/sigma from a monotone CDF fit
  over cumulative bracket prices. The existing JOINT FULL-LADDER BRACKET
  SELECTION entry is about *sizing* across brackets; this is about
  *extracting the market's own forecast* as a signal. Uses: (a) a
  self-consistent anchor (individual mids can be stale/one-sided -- the
  fitted CDF pools the whole event book); (b) a scalar "market-implied
  mean minus model mean, F" logged per prediction -- directly comparable
  to run_trend_delta and testable against settled_temp_f with the same
  enablement-trigger shape; (c) research into which bucket types
  systematically misprice (favorite-longshot tilt on tails).

What it would look like:
  Helper that groups sibling markets by event (the parse machinery in
  parse_city_date :3448 already extracts city/date), sorts brackets, fits
  mean/sigma minimizing squared error to bracket mids weighted by
  liquidity, returns {implied_mean, implied_sigma, fit_residual}. Log into
  predictions (2-3 columns, same migration pattern as run_trend). Do NOT
  wire into blend until settled-data correlation check passes (same
  ENABLEMENT TRIGGER precedent as run_trend, above).

Why not now:
  - Needs thin-book handling (skip fit when fewer than ~3 two-sided
    brackets -- is_liquid gives the gate); value is research-first, so it
    competes with other log-only signals for the same "will anyone ever
    check back" risk this file already flags.
  - UPDATE 2026-07-18 (no code changed, precondition checked against live
    source): the thin-book gate this entry names as a blocker already
    exists -- is_liquid() is a real, shipped function (weather_markets.py,
    currently at line 3810; the :3777 line ref above has drifted from
    intervening edits but the function itself is unchanged in shape).
    There is no missing infrastructure and no data-accumulation wait here
    -- unlike the other log-only signal entries in this file (run_trend,
    candlestick capture, richer ML features), this one was never blocked
    on anything external. It's simply unstarted design/build work that
    lost out to higher-priority items every time priority was assigned.
    Genuinely ready to pick up whenever someone chooses to prioritize it
    over the other log-only candidates it competes with.

When to revisit: N/A, resolved. See the ENABLEMENT TRIGGER note (unchanged
  from original scoping) for when a future session should check whether
  enough settled-data correlation exists to consider wiring this into the
  blend -- not before then.

  paginated exactly like get_markets, but with one real behavioral
  difference found live-testing: Kalshi can return a non-empty cursor on
  what turns out to be the LAST page (an empty trades list on the next
  call is what actually signals "done"), so the pagination loop checks
  `not cursor or not page`, not cursor-truthiness alone like get_markets
  does -- mutation-tested this exact difference (a test using a distinct
  cursor value on the terminal empty page, specifically to isolate this
  check from the separate repeated-cursor guard, which would otherwise
  mask the mutation).

  names). trade_id (Kalshi's own globally-unique per-trade ID) is the

  existed only because candlesticks have no natural single-field ID.

[NBM PROBABILISTIC QUANTILES -- ORPHANED CONVERTER, MISSING FETCHER]
Priority: Low-Medium -- the consumer half already exists in-tree; only the
  fetch half is missing, but the fetch half needs real research.

Problem:
  nws.nws_prob_from_quantiles() (nws.py:324-376) is a complete,
  documented NBM-percentile->probability converter (linear ECDF over
  {10,25,50,75,90} percentiles with tail extrapolation) with zero
  production callers and zero code anywhere fetching NBM percentiles
  (repo-wide grep 2026-07-16: only its own definition). nws.py is outside
  tests/test_dead_code_scan.py's scope (paper/tracker/weather_markets
  only), so the scan will never surface it. NBM's quantile output (QMD)
  is a calibrated per-day, per-station uncertainty estimate -- a daily
  dynamic sigma that would sharpen the current per-month climate sigma
  (get_historical_sigma :2209) and capture skew a symmetric Gaussian
  can't.

What it would look like:
  Research pass first -- NBM percentiles live in the QMD grib products on
  NOMADS (not in the NBS text bulletins live-tested for the REAL NBM
  entry above, and not exposed by api.weather.gov); check whether IEM or
  another JSON-friendly mirror serves them before committing to grib
  parsing. If a clean source exists: fetch per station/day, feed
  nws_prob_from_quantiles as either the NWS-slot probability for tail
  buckets or a sigma source, gated/log-only first.

Why not now:
  - No verified JSON source yet (grib parsing would add a heavy
    dependency for one signal -- likely not worth it alone); do the
    source-hunting as part of the REAL NBM entry's IEM work since it's
    the same product family. If no clean source exists, decide
    wire-up-or-delete for the orphan explicitly and extend the dead-code
    scan to nws.py either way.

When to revisit:
  - Scoped together with REAL NBM VIA IEM NBS STATION BULLETINS above.

[FORECAST-CONDITION COVARIATES FOR SIGMA -- INCLUDING FIELDS ALREADY FETCHED AND NEVER READ]
Priority: Low-Medium -- sigma today conditions on city/month/horizon/spread
  but never on what kind of weather day it is; several inputs are already
  being paid for.

Problem:
  The daily forecast fetch requests only
  temperature_2m_max,temperature_2m_min,precipitation_sum
  (weather_markets.py:983); the temperature sigma path
  (weather_markets.py:5620-5660) uses climate sigma x horizon x spread,
  and regime.py conditions only on ensemble mean/std. No weather-type
  conditioning exists anywhere -- yet precip/frontal days have
  systematically larger high-temp errors and cloud-cover busts are the
  classic daily-high miss. Concretely unused today: precipitation_sum is
  fetched with every forecast and never consumed in the temperature path
  (grep of analyze_trade's temp section: precip only routes precip-market
  types at :5340-5350); Pirate Weather's wind_gust/_wind_gust_time_unix/
  _hourly_window_high_f are fetched and stored into the forecast dict
  (weather_markets.py:1097-1100, 2114-2119) with zero readers anywhere
  (repo-wide grep). The NBS bulletins from the REAL NBM entry above would
  add sky/gst/p12 in the same call.

What it would look like:
  Log 2-3 covariates (forecast precip_sum, sky/cloud, gust) into
  predictions alongside the existing run_trend columns (same v-migration
  pattern), correlate |settled_temp_f - forecast| against them once
  sample floors clear, then a bounded sigma multiplier for high-precip-
  probability days. Distinct from RICHER ML CALIBRATION FEATURES, which
  proposes *internal* features (ensemble spread, model disagreement,
  data_quality) -- this is external weather-type covariates; if the ML
  entry ships first, these become additional candidate features for the
  same GBM instead of a separate mechanism.

Why not now:
  - Same weeks-of-accumulation gate as every log-only signal; keep
    feature count small vs the 200-samples-per-city training gate the ML
    entry already flags. The dead wind_gust/_hourly_window_high_f fields
    deserve a wire-up-or-delete decision regardless (dict fields are
    invisible to the dead-code scan).

When to revisit:
  - Alongside RICHER ML CALIBRATION FEATURES -- decide then whether these
    are separate covariates or additional features for the same model.

[CROSS-CITY RECENT-ERROR POOLING -- SYNOPTIC-REGIME BIAS SHARE]
Priority: Low-Medium -- the spatial correlation structure is already
  learned and stored; it's only ever used to *penalize risk*, never to
  *improve the forecast*.

Problem:
  Bias correction is strictly per-city and slow: _get_combined_station_bias
  (weather_markets.py:303-337) blends a static table with
  tracker.get_dynamic_station_bias (min 10 samples, weeks of
  accumulation, 4h cache). Nothing uses the last 24-48h of realized
  errors in *other* cities to nudge today's forecast -- even though
  forecast errors are spatially correlated under a shared synoptic
  regime, and the bot already quantifies exactly those correlations
  (_CITY_PAIR_CORR paper.py:313-332; tracker.get_recent_city_correlations
  refreshed into monte_carlo.simulate_portfolio at monte_carlo.py:
  242-264) -- but solely for portfolio VaR. If the model ran 2F hot
  across the whole Gulf Coast group yesterday, today's NOLA/Houston
  forecasts are more likely hot too; the per-city dynamic bias can't see
  that for weeks.

What it would look like:
  tracker.get_regional_recent_bias(city, var, hours=48) --
  correlation-weighted mean of correlated cities' settled errors over the
  last 1-2 days (data already in outcomes.settled_temp_f; the
  correlated-group structure already in _CORRELATED_CITY_GROUPS
  paper.py:283-287), returned with sample count. Ship log-only (a
  regional_bias column beside run_trend), verify it actually correlates
  with same-day own-city error at settlement, then a small bounded lean
  capped well below _get_combined_station_bias's magnitude.

Why not now:
  - Settled-outcome latency (an error is only known after settlement +
    sync -- check whether "yesterday's" errors are actually available by
    today's scan time in practice); needs the same sample-floor and
    enablement-trigger discipline; low per-city row counts today (3-14
    per the 2026-07-12 audit) mean the pooled signal is the *point* but
    also hard to validate initially.

When to revisit:
  - Once per-city settled counts grow past the same floor used elsewhere
    (see DATA-DRIVEN SIGMA FROM SETTLED HISTORY's own count check).

[MARKET_LIFECYCLE_V2 WS CHANNEL -- LISTING-TIME AWARENESS]
Priority: Low -- real timing edge, but structurally blocked behind the
  always-on host decision.

Problem:
  Confirmed by direct docs fetch 2026-07-16, Kalshi's WS channel list is
  orderbook_delta, ticker, trade, fill, market_positions,
  market_lifecycle_v2, multivariate_market_lifecycle, multivariate,
  communications, order_group_updates, user_orders, cfbenchmarks_value,
  pyth_value -- this bot subscribes to exactly two (kalshi_ws.py:362) and
  the backlog covers trade/fill/order_groups, but market_lifecycle_v2
  (and user_orders) appear nowhere in repo or backlog (grep: zero hits
  for market_lifecycle). New daily temperature markets are discovered
  only when the next REST scan happens (get_weather_markets + 60s
  _MARKETS_CACHE_TTL :744-745, on cron cadence) -- hours after listing.
  Freshly listed markets have the widest spreads and least-informed
  quotes; the first maker quote at model fair value gets the best prices
  of the market's life, and the deferred candlestick entry-timing
  analysis can verify this from data already being captured (candles
  cover the full open->close window, so "edge vs hours-since-open" is
  computable today for settled markets).

What it would look like:
  Subscribe market_lifecycle_v2 in the (future) always-on watcher; on a
  new KXHIGH*/KXLOW* listing, run analyze_trade for that market
  immediately and post a resting maker order if gates pass. Cheap
  precursor available now with zero new infra: use the existing candle
  history (tracker.get_price_history) to measure whether early-window
  prices were actually more mispriced vs settlement -- do that before
  building anything live.

Why not now:
  - Meaningless without the always-on host (explicitly parked in the
    MOVE OFF LOCAL CRON entry, trigger = live trading imminent); do the
    candle-based "is early entry actually better" check first -- if edge
    doesn't decay with market age, this whole candidate dies cheaply.

When to revisit:
  - Once the always-on host decision executes. Note user_orders as a
    sibling channel to fold into the already-deferred fill-channel work
    when that resumes.

ARCHITECTURE & DESIGN-DEBT CANDIDATES -- 2026-07-16 whole-program scouting

[THE ONLY LIVE-ORDER PATH IS THE INTERACTIVE WATCH CLI -- NO HEADLESS TRADE-CYCLE ENGINE]
Priority: High -- a stated prerequisite for the already-decided VM move +
  deferred always-on watcher; this is the refactor that determines whether
  that work is a port or a rewrite.

Problem:
  There are two parallel scan pipelines, and the hardened one can't trade
  live while the live one isn't hardened. cron pipeline (cron.py:475
  _cmd_cron_body, ~2,100 lines): the production path -- kill-switch/
  override/accuracy-halt/graduation gates, consistency-violation halt
  (cron.py:1112-1136), batch cache prewarm, ThreadPoolExecutor scan via
  _enrich_and_analyze (cron.py:1369), is_stale exclusion, gate counters,
  shadow logging, tiered ctx.auto_place_trades(...) (cron.py:1886/1895)
  -- paper only; cron never passes live=True. watch pipeline (main.py:
  2822 cmd_watch): a `while True` terminal UI wrapping _analyze_once
  (main.py:1294) -- a *sequential* scan with different gates (skips
  days_out==0 at 1337, no consistency halt, no prewarm -- dedup/is_stale
  parity was added 2026-07-19, see the RESOLVED note below) -- and this
  is the *only* path that can place a live order
  (_auto_place_trades(..., live=live) at 2875-2877, then poll/reprice/
  exit-protection at 2878-2886). So when live trading starts, real money
  runs through the interactive-display pipeline while the
  production-hardened pipeline stays paper. And the deferred always-on
  watcher ("reacts between cycles") has no home: it would be a *third*
  hand-assembled sequence of scan->analyze->place->poll->reprice->
  protect, because that sequence exists only as inline orchestration
  inside two different functions, each with its own subset and ordering.
  The exit-protection calls are already duplicated verbatim between them
  (cron.py:757-768 vs main.py:2878-2886).

What it would look like:
  Extract a headless run_trade_cycle(client, mode: paper|live, triggers)
  engine owning the canonical ordered sequence (recover-pending -> settle
  -> scan -> analyze -> decide/place -> poll fills -> reprice -> position
  protection -> log), with the CLI display and the cron wrapper both
  becoming thin callers. The always-on watcher then becomes "call the
  engine's protection stage on WS events + the full cycle on a timer"
  instead of a third reimplementation. The CronContext injection seam
  (cron.py:78, main.py:208) is already halfway there -- the engine is
  mostly a matter of moving orchestration out of _cmd_cron_body/
  cmd_watch into it.

RESOLVED 2026-07-19 (smallest-safe-step piece only -- the full headless
  engine below is still open, unstarted): ported cron.py's per-ticker dedup
  + is_stale skip into main.py's _analyze_once, closing the feature-gap
  slice of this entry without the full reshuffle. main.py:1298-1327
  (immediately after `markets = get_weather_markets(client)`, before
  `total = len(markets)`) now builds a deduped/stale-filtered markets list
  via the identical loop shape cron.py's _cmd_cron_body already uses
  (dedup-by-ticker first via a _seen_tickers set, then weather_markets.
  is_stale() skip, with the same _log.debug counters for dedup/stale
  counts) -- `_analyze_once` and `_cmd_cron_body` now apply the same
  pre-analysis filtering to the same raw get_weather_markets() response.
  Traced both real callers of _analyze_once (cmd_analyze at main.py:2702,
  cmd_watch's loop at main.py:2924) and confirmed neither depends on
  duplicate-ticker or stale markets reaching enrich_with_forecast/
  analyze_trade -- `markets` is function-local and not read again after
  the loop except via `total`/`compute_market_implied_distributions`,
  both of which now correctly see the deduped count (matches cron.py's own
  "report post-dedup count in summary" comment). Checked the one test file
  that calls _analyze_once directly (tests/test_p1_remaining.py) plus
  cmd_watch/cmd_analyze's test files (test_trading.py, test_menu_ux.py,
  test_debug_fixes.py) -- none of their fixtures rely on duplicate tickers
  or on a stale (zero-volume, closing-soon) market being processed, so no
  existing test needed updating.
  New tests (tests/test_p1_remaining.py, TestAnalyzeOnceDedupAndStaleParity):
  a stale-market-skipped test mirroring test_cron_integration.py's
  test_cron_skips_stale_markets_before_analysis exactly (same fixture
  shape, same assertion), and a duplicate-ticker-dedup test. Both
  mutation-tested by reverting the main.py fix (git stash) and confirming
  both tests fail for the right reason (dedup count 2 instead of 1; the
  stale market reaching enrich_with_forecast), then restoring the fix and
  confirming they pass again.
  107 tests pass across tests/test_p1_remaining.py, test_trading.py,
  test_menu_ux.py, test_debug_fixes.py, test_cron_integration.py; ruff +
  ruff format + mypy clean on both changed files.
  Independent second-opinion review (Agent, opus): clean, no findings.
  Confirmed the ordering (dedup-add-to-seen before is_stale check) matches
  cron.py exactly, the debug-log duplicate-count math can't false-trigger,
  both real callers (cmd_analyze, cmd_watch) are safe against the `markets`
  reassignment (stale markets could only ever land in no_quote_opps since
  is_liquid() requires volume, so liquid_opps/auto-trading is unaffected;
  find_violations() now runs on the deduped set too, a benign side benefit
  removing spurious self-arb between a ticker and its own duplicate), and
  the new tests patch the correct targets given main.py's mixed

[RESOLVED 2026-07-20] WATCH/_analyze_once IS MISSING cron.py's MIN_MARKET_PROB_TO_BET_WITH /
MAX_MARKET_DIVERGENCE_RATIO DIRECTIONAL-CONSENSUS GATES
Priority: Medium -- a real, live-order-path gap, but narrower than it first
  looks (see "Why this is smaller than it sounds" below); no known incident,
  TRADING_PAUSED=true throughout.

Found: 2026-07-20, as an adjacency finding while shipping the days_out==0
  parity fix above (backlog.txt "THE ONLY LIVE-ORDER PATH... -- NO HEADLESS
  TRADE-CYCLE ENGINE"). Deliberately not folded into that change. Widened
  same day from one missing gate to two after an independent Agent(opus,
  effort=high) review of that fix's diff caught the same-day comment
  overclaiming both gates applied in main.py and, chasing that down, found
  MAX_MARKET_DIVERGENCE_RATIO was ALSO cron.py-only -- this session's first
  adjacency pass had only found MIN_MARKET_PROB_TO_BET_WITH.

Problem:
  cron.py's scan loop (cron.py:1546-1565) applies two gates beyond
  analyze_trade()'s own internal gates, both keyed on `_mkt_dir` (the
  market's own probability in the direction of `recommended_side` --
  market_prob if betting yes, 1-market_prob if betting no):
  1. `MIN_MARKET_PROB_TO_BET_WITH` (utils.py:189, 0.25): skip if the market
     gives our chosen side less than a 25% chance -- "the market is right
     nearly every time" at that level of disagreement (cron.py:1557-1559).
  2. `MAX_MARKET_DIVERGENCE_RATIO` (utils.py:183): skip if `_our_dir /
     _mkt_dir` (our probability in our chosen direction, divided by the
     market's) exceeds the ratio cap -- a second, ratio-shaped framing of
     "we disagree with the market too much" (cron.py:1560-1565).
  Grepped the whole repo for both constants: each appears only in cron.py
  and its own definition/fingerprint entry in utils.py -- zero occurrences
  in main.py or order_executor.py. watch/_analyze_once (the only pipeline
  that can place a live order) has never applied either check, for any
  market, not just same-day ones.

Why this is smaller than it sounds:
  analyze_trade() itself (weather_markets.py:7254-7272, "7d. Model-market gap
  gate") already rejects (returns None) any trade -- shared by both
  pipelines, since both call analyze_trade() -- when the RAW model
  probability and market probability disagree by more than 0.25, regardless
  of direction. So the bulk of what cron's two directional checks would
  catch is already caught upstream, for both pipelines equally.
  What 7d does NOT catch and cron's checks do: cases where the raw
  disagreement is under 0.25 but the market is still confidently against
  our chosen side -- e.g. market YES-price 20%, our forecast 35% YES: gap is
  15pp (passes 7d) but the market gives our side only a 20% chance (would
  fail cron's `_mkt_dir < 0.25` check, and likely the ratio check too). This
  can happen because 7d compares against the PRE-anchor raw model
  probability while cron's `_mkt_dir`/`_our_dir` read `analysis.get(
  "market_prob"/"forecast_prob")` (potentially blended/anchored) -- the
  gates are measuring related but distinct things, not one subsuming the
  others.

What it would look like:
  Port cron.py:1546-1565's exact `_mkt_dir`/`_our_dir` computation + both
  checks into main.py's `_analyze_once`, after the days_out==0 fall-through
  (same site as this entry's sibling fix above). Needs its own
  AskUserQuestion pass first though -- open scope questions not yet answered:
  (1) should it use `analysis.get("market_prob"/"forecast_prob")`
  (post-anchor, matching cron.py exactly) or something else; (2) does it
  need its own debug counters matching `_dbg["mkt_prob"]`/`_dbg[
  "divergence"]`'s style; (3) whether cmd_today (main.py:2298-2316, a
  separate display-only "what should I do today" command, NOT the
  live-order path) should get the same treatment for UI-recommendation
  parity, or is out of scope since it never places an order.

When to revisit:
  - No hard trigger -- this is a real, self-contained gap independent of the
    VM-move/live-trading-imminent trigger that gates the full headless-engine
    entry above. Reasonable to pick up any time; not urgent given
    TRADING_PAUSED=true and analyze_trade()'s 7d gate already covering the
    large-gap cases.

[PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-20] NO MARKET-TYPE SEAM -- TEMPERATURE IS THE ARCHITECTURE, NOT A MARKET TYPE
Priority: was Medium-High -- now Low-Medium. hourly-directional (KXTEMPxxxH)
  was the nearest stated expansion and did hit every one of these walls;
  shipping it (2026-07-20, commit 06269b4) closed the concrete complaints
  below via pragmatic single-source-of-truth fixes, not a formal interface.
  What's left (no MarketType protocol, check_series_drift() still KXHIGH/
  KXLOW-only) only pays off if rain/snow gets picked up next -- see the
  RESOLVED note below.

Problem:
  Market-type knowledge is not behind an interface; it's a set of
  string-match conventions repeated independently across the pipeline,
  and the deepest layer (ground truth/calibration) only has a concept of
  temperature at all. Dispatch: analyze_trade() (weather_markets.py:5145)
  is a ~1,660-line monolith whose market-type "routing" is two
  early-return fast-paths keyed on parsed condition type (precip at
  5340-5347, snow at 5350-5355); everything after line 5357 IS the
  temperature model. There is no third place to plug in an hourly-
  threshold model except a third inline fast-path. Variable derivation by
  ticker substring is duplicated: `var = "min" if "LOW" in series else
  "max"` exists independently at weather_markets.py:5414 and 6248,
  tracker.py:2544-2554 (settlement audit), and paper.py:1148-1154
  (_score_ensemble_members) -- four copies of the same convention, each
  of which a new market type must extend or silently mis-handle
  (paper.py's copy defaults unknown tickers to "max"). Ground truth is a
  temperature column: outcomes stores settled_yes + settled_temp_f
  (tracker.py:122, 310-314). The settlement-audit path explicitly bails
  for anything else -- tracker.py:2554: `return False  # precipitation or
  unknown -- skip`. Everything downstream of settlement -- EMOS training,
  data-driven sigma, dynamic station bias, per-model accuracy, ml_bias
  temperature scaling -- consumes settled_temp_f. A rain market can trade
  today (the precip fast-path exists) but can never learn: no ground
  truth is ever recorded for it, so it's permanently outside the
  calibration loop that is this bot's actual moat. Degraded analysis
  dicts already bite: the precip/snow fast-paths return reduced dicts
  (hardcoded "time_risk": "HIGH" at 4792/4999, no entry_price), which
  already silently disabled the reprice taker-cross for precip markets
  (documented as an "informational finding" in the maker-execution
  entry). check_series_drift() (weather_markets.py:3308) diffs only
  KXHIGH*/KXLOW* (3332-3339) against the hardcoded KNOWN_WEATHER_SERIES
  list -- already flagged in the hourly/rain entries, but note it's the
  same missing seam, not a separate fix.

RESOLVED 2026-07-20 (the concrete complaints above, via pragmatic fixes --
  NOT via the formal MarketType protocol this entry's "What it would look
  like" section describes; that part is still open, see below): shipping
  HOURLY-DIRECTIONAL TEMPERATURE MARKETS Step 2 (commit 06269b4) closed
  every specific verification point in this Problem section:
  - Third dispatch slot: `_analyze_hourly_trade()` (weather_markets.py) is
    now a genuine third branch in analyze_trade(), positioned before the
    precip/snow fast-paths -- "no third place to plug in" is no longer true.
  - Var-convention duplication: a `predictions.var` column (migration v53)
    is now the single source of truth. `paper._score_ensemble_members()`
    and `tracker.audit_settlement()` both prefer the stored value, falling
    back to ticker-substring derivation only for legacy pre-migration rows.
    The two remaining literal `var = "min" if "LOW" in series else "max"`
    copies in weather_markets.py are now purely internal to the daily
    model -- hourly bypasses them entirely.
  - Temperature-only ground truth: `outcomes.settled_value REAL`/
    `settled_var TEXT` (migration v50-v52, shipped in Step 1) are now
    actually populated -- `audit_settlement()` has a dedicated hourly
    branch that writes them before ever reaching the old `return False #
    precipitation or unknown -- skip` line.
  - No calibration-pool separation: `ml_bias.train_all_temperature_
    scaling()` now has a third `'hourly'` pool, explicitly excluded from
    `'sameday'`, with its own no-fallback `apply_temperature_scaling(pool=
    "hourly")` path.
  Of the 5-item MarketType protocol wishlist below, items 1 (series-prefix
  set), 2 (condition parsing), 3 (probability entry point), and 5
  (calibration-pool key) all now exist as concrete, market-type-specific
  implementations (item 4, ground-truth spec, shipped too). But there is
  still NO formal `MarketType` protocol/interface (grepped for `Protocol`/
  `class MarketType` across weather_markets.py and tracker.py -- zero hits)
  -- each of the 5 things is still a separate, hand-wired branch keyed on
  `_is_hourly`/ticker-prefix checks, not slots on a shared interface a third
  market type (rain/snow) could plug into without writing its own parallel
  branches from scratch. Also still true: `check_series_drift()` was NOT
  extended to cover KXTEMPxxxH -- a parallel mechanism
  (`refresh_hourly_target_hours()`) was added alongside it instead, doing
  target-hour recomputation rather than the same live-series-list-diff
  drift check. The precip/snow fast-paths' degraded analysis dicts
  (hardcoded time_risk, no entry_price) were also untouched by this
  commit -- re-verify those are still exactly as described if this entry
  is picked up again, since that part wasn't re-checked this session.

What it would look like:
  A MarketType protocol owning the five things currently keyed on string
  conventions: (1) series-prefix set for discovery/drift, (2) condition
  parsing, (3) probability model entry point (analyze(enriched,
  condition) -> analysis), (4) ground-truth spec -- what observable
  settles it and how to fetch it, (5) calibration-pool key (so hourly
  rows never pollute the daily 'sameday' T-scaling pool -- the exact
  separation the hourly backlog entry already demands). The outcomes
  table needs a generic settled_value REAL + settled_var TEXT shape
  instead of settled_temp_f. The temperature implementation would
  initially just be the existing code behind the interface -- the win is
  that hourly/rain get slots instead of fourth and fifth copies of the
  "LOW" in ticker convention.

Why not now:
  - The ground-truth generalization (settled_value/settled_var) is done --
    see RESOLVED note above. The remaining formal MarketType protocol only
    pays off if RAIN / SNOW / HURRICANE MARKETS (below) is actually picked
    up next -- don't build the abstraction speculatively for a third market
    type that doesn't exist yet; the concrete/pragmatic pattern hourly used
    (a dedicated function + a shared prefix dict + a stored var column) is
    proven now and can be repeated a second time for rain/snow just as
    cheaply as building the interface, unless a third type after that makes
    the interface's payoff clear.

When to revisit:
  - The moment RAIN / SNOW / HURRICANE MARKETS is actually greenlit -- at
    that point, decide whether a third repetition of the concrete pattern
    is still cheaper than building the formal protocol (it likely still is
    for a second repetition; the protocol pays off more clearly on a
    fourth+ market type). Also revisit check_series_drift() then -- it
    still needs the same KXTEMPxxxH-style parallel-mechanism treatment (or
    a real generalization) for whatever new series rain/snow adds.
