  mypy clean on all changed files (verified under the project's real
  py -3.12 interpreter, not the system `python` which resolves to 3.14
  on this machine and lacks ruff/mypy -- worth noting for future
  sessions on this machine).

Problem (as originally scoped, still accurate for the still-open full
Position read-model below):
  A "position" exists in two unrelated persistence models -- paper's JSON
  ledger (data/paper_trades.json, full read-modify-write under
  _DATA_LOCK, paper.py:87/107) and live's execution_log SQLite rows --
  and the live side reaches feature parity by adaptation and replication,
  not sharing. order_executor._get_live_open_positions()
  (order_executor.py:955) reshapes execution_log rows into "whatever keys
  paper's check functions happen to read (verified by reading both
  bodies)". _update_live_peak_profits() (order_executor.py:996)
  *replicates* paper's peak math because paper.update_peak_profits
  ignores its own parameter and re-reads paper's JSON internally --
  i.e., paper's functions are storage-coupled in ways discovered
  per-function. _check_live_model_exits() (order_executor.py:1214) is a
  ~100-line near-clone of _check_early_exits (order_executor.py:1625),
  built as a separate function "to avoid any risk of regressing the
  existing paper-only path". The divergence already produced asymmetry:
  the multiple-positions-per-ticker collapse bug was fixed on the live
  side only, with paper's identical pattern left in production
  (documented in the RESTING EXIT ORDERS resolution above). Beyond the
  structural glue, gate constants are hand-copied as bare literals: the
  24h settlement-convergence gate at four sites (paper.py:1339-1357,
  1431-1449; order_executor.py:1693-1713, 1277-1298), the 12h
  minimum-hold gate at three (paper.py:2185-2197; order_executor.py:
  1671-1683, 1263-1275) -- none in get_config_fingerprint(). Drift has
  already started at the doc level: _check_early_exits' docstring
  (order_executor.py:1628) says "shifted >15 percentage points" while the
  code gates on `shift > 0.25` (line 1715).

What it would look like:
  Two-tier fix. Now (DONE 2026-07-19, see resolution above): named module
  constants (EXIT_MIN_HOLD_HOURS=12, EXIT_SETTLEMENT_GATE_HOURS=24,
  MODEL_EXIT_SHIFT_PP=0.25) shared by both files and added to
  get_config_fingerprint(), plus one extracted _passes_exit_gates(...)
  -> bool used by all 5 sites. Later (still open): a Position read-model
  -- one dataclass with the fields the check functions actually consume
  (ticker, side, qty, entry_price, entry_prob, cost, peak_profit_pct,
  close_time), two PositionStore implementations (paper JSON,
  execution_log), and the stop-loss/breakeven/model-exit/peak logic
  operating solely on list[Position] + an injected exit(position, price,
  reason) callback. Fix update_peak_profits to actually operate on its
  parameter (thin paper wrapper keeps JSON persistence; live path calls
  the pure function), collapsing _update_live_peak_profits to
  persistence-only.

Why not now (for the remaining full read-model piece):
  - The full read-model touches paper.py's battle-tested check functions
    -- exactly what the 2026-07-13 session was avoiding -- so save it for
    when the next live-position feature (partial-fill handling is the
    likeliest) needs
    a third consumer to validate the interface against.

When to revisit:
  - Named constants + shared gate helper: DONE 2026-07-19, see resolution
    above. Full Position read-model: when the next live-position feature
    lands, using it as the third consumer that validates the interface.

[SIGNAL GRADUATION IS A CONVENTION, NOT A MECHANISM -- SIGNAL #3 REBUILDS RUN-TREND'S PLUMBING]
Priority: Medium -- the log-only->trigger->blend pattern is now this
  project's explicit strategy for all new alpha; its marginal cost is
  currently ~6 touch points per signal.

Problem:
  Run-trend established the graduation *pattern* but implemented it as
  bespoke wiring at every layer, so signals #3-#5 (trade-flow, AFD,
  richer-ML features are all queued in this file) each repeat it.
  Storage: one named migration per scalar (tracker.py:221-223, v40-v42)
  plus dedicated columns per signal -- predictions is now at schema v53
  largely from this accretion (was v42 when this entry was written; the
  hourly-directional work added var TEXT, one more accretion of the exact
  same shape this entry describes). API: a new named parameter on
  log_prediction() (tracker.py:610 run_trend: dict | None) -- the
  signature grows one kwarg per signal, forever. Threading: every
  log_prediction call site updated through order_executor's shared helper
  _prediction_kwargs_from_analysis (order_executor.py:1926) -- CORRECTION
  2026-07-20: main.py's two direct call sites no longer re-import
  get_forecast_run_trend_from_analysis locally; that specific duplication
  was fixed by [RESOLVED 2026-07-17] LOG_PREDICTION KWARGS ASSEMBLY
  TRIPLICATED (below) -- both call sites now route through the same shared
  helper. The core thesis (kwarg-growth-per-signal, no generic mechanism)
  is otherwise unaffected by that fix and still fully holds.
  Enablement: run-trend's trigger (sample floor + correlation check)
  exists only as backlog.txt prose that someone must remember to run by
  hand. Meanwhile the codebase already *has* an in-code activation
  mechanism -- sample-gated auto-activation with one-time notification
  (_regime_blend_active() weather_markets.py:3887 +
  _notify_feature_activation 3852, and siblings: PDO/PNA gate at 3912,
  MIN_BIAS_CORRECTION_TRADES) -- but it's re-derived per feature and was
  not used for run-trend. Blend entry (the eventual step): the core
  blend is a *positional 3-tuple* -- _blend_weights() returns
  (w_ensemble, w_climatology, w_nws) (weather_markets.py:3954-3962). Any
  signal graduating to a real blend weight either changes that arity
  everywhere or joins the growing chain of bespoke post-blend
  adjustments, which is how analyze_trade got to 1,660 lines.

What it would look like:
  (a) log_prediction(..., signals: dict[str, float] | None) persisting to
  a signal_values(prediction_id, name, value) table (or one JSON column,
  matching the blend_sources/run_trend_points precedent) -- new signal =
  new dict key, zero migrations, zero signature/call-site changes; (b) a
  small signal registry (name, extract(analysis) -> value(s),
  sample_floor, correlation_target) driving both a standing
  graduation-report command (runs every pending signal's enablement query
  against settled outcomes -- replaces the per-entry prose triggers) and
  the auto-activation notification machinery that already exists for
  regime/PDO; (c) leave blend *wiring* manual -- the deliberate human
  step is the point of the pattern -- but let graduated signals enter as
  named entries in a weights dict rather than tuple-position N+1.

Why not now:
  - Do (a)+(b) when the *next* log-only signal is built (trade-flow is
    queued post-Belgium) -- that's when the second data point proves/
    disproves the shape, and the cost is near-zero incremental to work
    already planned. Not worth a standalone pass while run-trend's own
    trigger hasn't fired.

When to revisit:
  - When PUBLIC TRADE-FLOW SIGNAL (or any other log-only signal above) is
    next picked up -- build the registry then, not before.

[THE ANALYSIS-DICT -> TRADE-RECORD BOUNDARY EXPLODES DICTS INTO NAMED SCALARS]
Priority: Medium -- sharpens the existing GENERALIZED PER-MODEL ACCURACY
  TRACKING entry with the structural root cause; read together.

Problem:
  The existing entry frames this as "per-model columns in tracker" -- but
  the tracker column is the *last* link of a six-hop scalar chain, and
  the chain's shape is the real cost. Per-model means travel: analyze_trade
  locals (weather_markets.py:5731-5732) -> return-dict keys (6775-6776)
  -> *named kwargs* at two independent placement call sites
  (main.py:3576-3577, order_executor.py:2663-2664) -> place_paper_order's
  signature (paper.py:853-854) -> trade JSON keys (957-958) ->
  _score_ensemble_members's hardcoded dict (paper.py:1174-1187) ->
  tracker.log_member_score. The comment at paper.py:1180-1186 states the
  consequence: ECMWF "can never earn a data-driven weight... permanently
  stuck at the static seasonal default" -- and the same is true for
  GEM/UKMO/WeatherNext or any future source. place_paper_order's
  signature is itself the pattern at scale: 19 named parameters, each a
  field some analysis produced, meaning *every* new per-trade datum (not
  just model means) pays the same multi-file kwarg-threading toll -- the
  same disease as log_prediction's kwarg growth in the SIGNAL GRADUATION
  entry above, at a different boundary.

What it would look like:
  One model_means: dict[str, float] key on the analysis dict (populated
  by _get_consensus_probs, which is already model-agnostic via
  _model_prob_and_mean -- the generic helper exists at the source end),
  passed through as a single kwarg -> stored as one JSON field on the
  trade record -> iterated by _score_ensemble_members (which already
  loops a dict at paper.py:1191, so the consumer end is *also* ready --
  only the transport is scalar). Keep icon_forecast_mean/gfs_forecast_mean
  as legacy read-fallbacks for settling old trades. This converts "add a
  model source" from a 6-file signature change into a fetch + one dict
  entry, which is precisely what GENERALIZED PER-MODEL ACCURACY TRACKING
  asks for -- that entry should be read together with this one when
  picked up, since the endpoints are already generic and only the
  transport chain needs replacing.

Why not now:
  - Same as GENERALIZED PER-MODEL ACCURACY TRACKING (weeks before learned
    weights activate, needs the which-ECMWF-product decision) -- but when
    picked up, do the dict transport *first*; instrumenting ECMWF through
    the scalar chain and then generalizing would do the plumbing twice.

When to revisit:
  - Same trigger as GENERALIZED PER-MODEL ACCURACY TRACKING -- do the
    dict-transport change as step one of that entry, not a separate pass.

[ONE-SHOT PROCESS LIFECYCLE IS BAKED INTO MODULE STATE -- THE ALWAYS-ON WATCHER INHERITS STALE-STATE HAZARDS]
Priority: Medium -- gated on the same trigger as the VM move; partially
  live *today* via loop/watch, which already call cmd_cron repeatedly
  in-process.

Problem:
  Correctness currently leans on process death as the cache-invalidation
  and config-reload mechanism. Import-time snapshots that feed live
  decisions: _CITY_WEIGHTS/_SEASONAL_WEIGHTS/_CONDITION_WEIGHTS load once
  at module import (weather_markets.py:748-750); _CONDITION_WEIGHTS feeds
  every trade's blend. In an always-on process, a recalibration writing
  new weight files changes nothing until restart. _LEARNED_WEIGHTS
  (2451-2453) is "cached after first load" with a log-*once* TTL warning
  flag -- a once-per-process warning is a once-per-*months* warning on a
  VM. Config frozen at import: utils.py alone has 41 module-level
  os.getenv constants. The operational model "edit .env -> next cron run
  picks it up" silently becomes "edit .env -> nothing happens" on a
  long-lived process. Per-cycle resource lifecycles: the WS client is
  constructed, subscribed, started, and torn down per cron cycle
  (cron.py:1038-1156, stop at 2668-2674) -- every fresh cycle starts with
  an empty book cache, which is exactly what caused the HIGH bug in the
  exit-protection review (REST-fallback shape on "the exact path the
  feature was built for"). An always-on design inverts this: the WS
  becomes the persistent event source and the scan becomes the periodic
  task -- none of the current orchestration is shaped for that
  inversion. Filesystem liveness protocol: cron lock, heartbeat, dead-
  man's-switch reading .cron_last_run mtime, _MONDAY_SWEEP_PATH touch-
  file -- a signaling protocol between *invocations* of a dying process.

What it would look like:
  An explicit cycle-scoped context (fits the headless trade-cycle engine
  entry above): weights/config refreshed at cycle start (or converting
  the import-time trio to the TTL-checked read-through pattern the
  forecast caches already use); log-once flags becoming log-once-per-
  cycle; WS lifted out of the cycle to process scope with reconnect/
  heartbeat ownership; an inventory pass over module globals in
  weather_markets.py/paper.py classifying each as (a) true constant, (b)
  TTL cache -- already safe, (c) load-once snapshot -- the hazard list.
  The existing autouse-fixture machinery (isolate_dynamic_sigma etc.)
  shows the project already knows which globals are dangerous -- that
  list is roughly the (c) list.

Why not now:
  - Same trigger as the VM move. But the inventory pass (c-list) is cheap
    and worth doing *before* the watcher design starts, because it sizes
    the real work; and any *new* module-global cache added between now
    and then should be TTL-checked rather than load-once, so the list
    stops growing.

When to revisit:
  - Same trigger as MOVE OFF LOCAL CRON -- HOST ON A SMALL ALWAYS-ON VM.
    The module-global inventory pass is cheap enough to do sooner, ahead
    of the watcher design itself.

Problem (as originally scoped, still accurate for historical context):
  CITY_COORDS is nominally data-driven (data/cities.json, weather_markets.py:

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] DISPUTED-ROW EXCLUSION PREDICATE HAND-COPIED ~40 TIMES IN tracker.py
Priority: was Medium -- same "one shared rule, many consumers, one gets
  missed" shape this project has hit 7+ times; the existing mutation
  tests protected the 30 *existing* filters but nothing forced a *new*
  query to add one.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  The 2026-07-12 disputed-outcome restoration added the literal predicate
  `AND (o.disputed IS NULL OR o.disputed = 0)` as a hand-copied string to
  every calibration query -- ~40 occurrences by the original estimate.
  The 30-filter mutation test proved existing filters worked, but the
  failure mode that mattered going forward was a NEW function joining
  outcomes on settled_yes and simply not knowing the rule exists -- exactly
  how the original 3-function scope grew to 30 in the first place.

What shipped:
  Took option (a) from this entry's own "what it would look like": a
  `CREATE VIEW IF NOT EXISTS outcomes_valid AS SELECT * FROM outcomes
  WHERE disputed IS NULL OR disputed = 0` in init_db() (right after the
  existing multiday_predictions view precedent), and migrated every
  consumer that should exclude disputed rows to join outcomes_valid
  instead of outcomes -- the view approach over the constant approach
  because it makes the correctness guarantee structural (join the right
  table) rather than "remember to paste the right string," and makes the
  guard test purely mechanical (flag any JOIN/FROM on the raw table
  outside a documented allowlist).

  Live re-count (2026-07-18) found the real number of JOIN/FROM outcomes
  sites was 49, not ~40 -- and a naive single-space regex only found 45 of
  those; 4 more (including get_emos_training_data and
  count_settled_west_coast_multiday) only surfaced after switching to a
  whitespace-tolerant `JOIN\s+outcomes` pattern, since tracker.py's SQL
  formatting inconsistently uses multiple spaces for column alignment
  (`JOIN   outcomes` vs `JOIN outcomes`). Of the 49: 31 already had the
  disputed filter (migrated to the view, predicate line removed -- pure
  refactor, no behavior change); 8 had NO filter and no comment explaining
  why, unlike the 9 legitimately-raw sites (purge_old_predictions:
  deletion by age; sync_outcomes: pre-outcome existence check;
  get_outcome_for_ticker: real position-resolution lookup that needs the
  actual current settlement regardless of dispute status; backfill_emos_
  data: data-repair, not a calibration consumer; get_disputed_count:
  definitionally counts the disputed rows; get_history: intentional raw
  audit listing).

  Those 8 -- count_settled_predictions, count_settled_predictions_rolling,
  count_settled_sameday_predictions, count_emos_ready_predictions,
  count_settled_below_predictions, count_settled_west_coast_multiday,
  get_emos_training_data, get_recent_city_correlations -- read as
  unaudited gaps, not deliberate choices, and were fixed in this same pass
  per explicit user sign-off (0 disputed rows existed in production at the
  time, so zero live impact when found, but get_emos_training_data
  directly trains the EMOS bias-correction model on settled_temp_f, and
  the other 6 feed sample-size gates that auto-activate live signals --
  e.g. weather_markets.py:776's _BELOW_GATE_MIN_SAMPLES check). Unlike the
  ANALYZE-TRADE EV/Kelly TAIL entry's divergences (where preserving
  precip/snow's different-but-plausible behavior was the right call), none
  of these 8 had any comment or rationale for the omission -- deferring a
  probably-just-missed filter to "someday" is exactly how the original
  3-function scope grew to 30.

  New tests: tests/test_tracker.py's TestDisputedOutcomeTracking class
  gained 7 new `_excludes_disputed` tests (before/after-equal on a
  synthetic disputed outlier row built to actually qualify for each
  function's other WHERE conditions -- e.g. the below-gate test needed
  condition_type='below', the EMOS tests needed ens_mean/settled_temp_f
  set via raw SQL since _log_settled doesn't expose them), joining the 31
  pre-existing ones (30-filter class plus TestStopLossAccuracy's own).
  tests/test_p9_p10.py gained a get_recent_city_correlations disputed-
  exclusion test using its existing multi-city correlation fixture, plus
  an extreme-value disputed pair that would flip the correlation from 1.0
  to -0.989 if not excluded. All 8 new tests mutation-tested (temporarily
  reverted each fix, confirmed the corresponding test fails with the
  correct real value, restored) before this shipped.

  New guard: tests/test_disputed_row_guard.py, matching test_dead_code_
  scan.py's allowlist-scan style -- regexes tracker.py for any JOIN/FROM
  on the raw outcomes table, asserts every hit is on a documented
  6-function allowlist (the legitimately-raw consumers above, plus
  init_db itself since the view's own definition must reference the raw
  table). Mutation-tested by adding a fake new unallowlisted query and
  confirming the guard fails, then reverting.

  Also fixed a transformation bug this same session caught before it
  shipped: the mechanical script used to migrate the 31 already-filtered
  queries had an off-by-N line-indexing bug (inserting the new view as one
  list element before computing deletion indices, rather than after) that
  deleted the wrong line at one site -- caught by running the existing
  tracker.py test suite immediately after the transformation, which failed
  loudly rather than silently. A second, narrower bug (a dropped trailing
  comma in get_stop_loss_accuracy's now-single-line SQL string, left over
  from deleting a two-string-literal concatenation) was caught the same
  way. Full tracker-adjacent test suite (912 tests across every file
  importing tracker.py) green before push.

Why not now (resolved):
  - Was gated on its own dedicated pass with the existing filter-test
    suite as the safety net -- done; see tests above.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] ANALYZE-TRADE PRICING/EV/KELLY TAIL TRIPLICATED ACROSS TEMP/PRECIP/SNOW PATHS
Priority: was Medium -- this block had already needed the same fix applied
  to every copy at least three times (the NO-sign inversion, the maker-fee
  migration), and it contained a fresh instance of the shadow-constant bug
  class the config guard can't see.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  The ~60-line tail (entry-price selection with the yes_ask / 1-yes_bid
  fallback chain -> net_ev -> net_edge cap 3.0 -> entry_side_edge NO-side
  fallback -> fee-adjusted kelly -> bayesian_kelly with NO-side CI flip
  -> CI-width scale `max(0.25, 1 - width*2)` -> condition_type scale ->
  cap) existed three times in weather_markets.py: precip path 4688-4757,
  snow path 4893-4964 (its own comment said "see _analyze_precip_trade's
  identical fix above" -- the copies were acknowledged in-source), and a
  divergent temperature variant 6521-6691 (adds time-decay, quality/
  anomaly/spread/bimodal scales the other two lack). Every historical fix
  to this logic had to be applied per-copy. Separately: the final Kelly
  cap was a naked `min(ci_adj_kelly, 0.25)` at 4757, 4964, and 6691 (0.33
  consensus variant at 6689) -- utils.KELLY_CAP (utils.py:105) is
  env-configurable, so setting KELLY_CAP in .env changed kelly_fraction's
  cap elsewhere but NOT these three ci_adjusted_kelly caps.

What shipped:
  Extracted `_price_and_size(blended_prob, prices, condition, rec_side, *,
  ci, consensus=False, extra_kelly_scales=(), time_decay=1.0) -> dict`
  (weather_markets.py, right after kelly_fraction) covering entry_price,
  payout, net_ev, net_edge, edge, entry_side_edge, fee_kel, ci_scale, and
  ci_adjusted_kelly (including the consensus bonus + cap). Precip and snow
  call it with condition/rec_side/ci only; temperature additionally passes
  consensus, extra_kelly_scales=(quality_scale, anomaly_scale, spread_scale,
  time_kelly_scale, _confidence_boost), and time_decay -- its near_threshold
  and bimodal-guard multipliers stay in analyze_trade itself since they
  apply *after* the shared cap step, not before it (folding them into
  extra_kelly_scales would have changed the interaction with the cap).
  Added utils.KELLY_CAP_CONSENSUS_MULT (default 1.32, so
  KELLY_CAP*MULT == 0.33 at current defaults) so the consensus ceiling
  moves with KELLY_CAP if it's ever tuned via .env, per this entry's own
  "decide deliberately" note -- went with the derived-multiplier option
  over an independent constant, since the two caps are conceptually the
  same knob at two confidence tiers, not two separate knobs.

  Verified via a pre-refactor A/B run (identical fixtures against git HEAD's
  weather_markets.py vs the extracted version) that every numeric field
  matched bit-for-bit across precip/snow/temperature, YES/NO sides, and
  consensus on/off, except two deliberate deltas:
    (1) net_edge off by ~1e-16 (float rounding-cadence noise from
        consolidating several separate round(x,6) calls into one chain --
        immaterial).
    (2) Temperature's NO-side entry_side_edge fallback (empty bid book):
        was using market_prob directly where precip/snow already used the
        correct 1.0-market_prob (with an in-source comment explaining why
        that's the fix) -- an unported bugfix, not a design difference.
        Confirmed live-impact via the same A/B fixture: old value 0.75,
        new (correct) value 0.05 -- the old formula could overstate
        entry_side_edge (which gates live trade execution) by up to
        ~0.7 on a NO-side signal against an illiquid book. Fixed as part
        of this consolidation per explicit user sign-off, flagged here and
        in the commit rather than silently folded in.
  The two other divergences found while reading the three copies
  (snow missing the consensus Kelly bonus precip has; precip's consensus
  bonus muted by staying capped at KELLY_CAP instead of reaching temp's
  higher consensus cap) were deliberately preserved as-is rather than
  fixed here, per user decision -- each is its own entry below.

  New tests: tests/test_price_and_size.py -- direct hand-computed-value
  unit tests on _price_and_size (YES/NO sides, empty-bid fallback, net_edge
  cap, consensus cap derivation, extra_kelly_scales composition,
  condition_type_scale, time_decay, and mutation-style checks that
  stripping ci_scale/consensus actually changes output), plus
  characterization tests driving _analyze_precip_trade/_analyze_snow_trade/
  analyze_trade end-to-end (the temperature case via the METAR-locked
  branch, which puts blended_prob under direct control and isolates this
  tail from the unrelated ensemble/consensus/climatology blend pipeline)
  pinned to the exact values observed in the pre-refactor A/B run.

Why not now (resolved):
  - Was gated on golden-value regression tests + opus review before
    touching this EV/sizing core -- both done (see tests above; opus
    review run before push).

When to revisit:
  - N/A, closed. See the two divergence entries below (still open) for
    the behavior differences found but deliberately not fixed here.

Priority: was Low-Medium -- narrow, single-path sizing question; not a

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: computed `snow_consensus` in _analyze_snow_trade

  wiring actually reaches _price_and_size's bonus, not just that the
  field is set; required a members list straddling the liquid-equivalent
  threshold since an all-agree members list degenerates the bootstrap CI
  to a point (ci_low==ci_high==1.0), which zeroes bayesian_kelly and would
  have masked the effect being tested. Existing TestSnowTradeWiring
  fixtures' "consensus" assertions updated from the stale "" to their
  real computed bool (False and True respectively) -- kelly/edge/
  entry_side_edge fields are untouched by this change since those are
  computed before the consensus branch in _price_and_size.
  Scoped test run (tests/test_price_and_size.py, test_phase2_batch_k.py,
  test_integration.py -- the only files exercising _analyze_snow_trade/
  _analyze_precip_trade/_price_and_size) passes except one pre-existing,

  caused by this change) -- see the new backlog entry below.

  new mutation test drew its bootstrap CI from _bootstrap_ci_precip's
  unseeded random.choices, so the two consensus/no-consensus calls got
  independent random CIs and the test was flaky (~2.5% false-fail,
  confirmed by the reviewer running it 400x) -- and, worse, weak (still
  passed ~50% of the time with the consensus wiring itself reverted, so
  it wasn't reliably proving what it claimed to prove). Fixed by pinning
  _bootstrap_ci_precip to a fixed CI via mock.patch.object so the two

  consensus only touches ci_adjusted_kelly (verified entry_price/net_edge/

  in _price_and_size), the existing TestSnowTradeWiring consensus
  assertions are deterministic and correct (not tautological), and no
  code outside weather_markets.py reads snow's "consensus" field in a way
  that would behave differently now that it's a real bool instead of ""
  (main.py's only consumer is guarded by isinstance(str), so a bool is
  skipped identically to the old falsy "").

Problem (as originally scoped):
  Found 2026-07-18 while consolidating the ANALYZE-TRADE PRICING/EV/KELLY
  TAIL (entry above). _analyze_precip_trade computes a `precip_consensus`
  signal (ensemble, climatology, and blended probability all agreeing on
  direction) and applies a x1.25 ci_adjusted_kelly bonus when it holds
  (weather_markets.py, precip path, pre-consolidation line 4805-4806).
  _analyze_snow_trade has no equivalent signal or bonus at all -- not a
  differently-computed version, just absent. Both paths derive ens_prob
  from the same _fetch_ensemble_precip() call, so a snow-equivalent
  consensus signal (ensemble/climatology/blend agreement) is cheap to
  compute the same way precip does.

What it would look like:
  Compute a `snow_consensus` signal in _analyze_snow_trade the same way
  precip_consensus is computed, and pass consensus=snow_consensus into the
  shared _price_and_size() call (already supports this via its `consensus`
  parameter -- no helper changes needed, just wiring at the snow call
  site). Decide whether the "consensus" field in snow's return dict
  (currently hardcoded to "" -- see the KALSHI CENTS/DOLLARS-adjacent
  triplication cluster note) should also start reporting the real bool,
  matching precip's return dict.

Why not now (original, superseded by resolution above):
  - Real live-sizing behavior change (raises snow's Kelly sizing on
    consensus trades) -- deliberately kept out of the pure-refactor
    consolidation above per the no-behavior-change-disguised-as-refactor
    convention. Low urgency: snow markets are a small fraction of current
    live volume relative to temperature.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18, discovered already-resolved] PRECIP CONSENSUS BONUS MUTED BY ITS OWN CAP -- NEVER REACHES TEMPERATURE'S HIGHER CONSENSUS CEILING
Priority: was Low-Medium -- same shape as the entry above, found in the same
  pass; a sizing-ceiling asymmetry, not a correctness bug.

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: while picking up this entry (in the same session as
  the SNOW entry above), live-verified the current shipped _price_and_size
  against this entry's own claim before touching anything -- confirmed the
  "muted cap" bug this entry describes NO LONGER EXISTS in the code the
  2026-07-18 consolidation actually shipped, even though this entry's own
  "what shipped" narrative says the divergence was "deliberately preserved
  as-is." _price_and_size's `if consensus:` branch applies the x1.25
  multiply AND the cap raise (KELLY_CAP -> KELLY_CAP*KELLY_CAP_CONSENSUS_
  MULT) together, unconditionally, for any caller that passes
  consensus=True -- it has no per-condition-type branching. Since
  _analyze_precip_trade already calls _price_and_size(consensus=
  precip_consensus), it already gets the cap raise today. Verified
  empirically, not just by code-reading: called _price_and_size directly
  with a precip-typed condition and a fixture engineered to cross the old
  0.25 cap (consensus=True result 0.264288, uncapped at 0.25, consistent
  with the 0.33 raised cap and inconsistent with the old muted one).
  Root cause: the consolidation's A/B safety net (see backlog.txt "ANALYZE-
  TRADE PRICING/EV/KELLY TAIL TRIPLICATED", point 11 of the implementation-
  style memory) never constructed a precip fixture whose pre-multiply
  ci_adjusted_kelly actually crossed the 0.25/0.33 boundary while
  consensus was also True -- the exact same cap-boundary blind spot class
  that entry's own net_edge bug came from, one level up. Surfaced this
  discrepancy to the user via AskUserQuestion before doing anything (per
  the "surface real scope/design decisions" convention) rather than
  silently either reverting or leaving it -- user chose to keep the
  current (already-shipped) behavior: precip consensus trades size up to
  0.33 same as temperature. No code change was needed for this entry;
  only this backlog description (which was describing pre-consolidation
  behavior, not what actually shipped) needed correcting.

Problem (as originally scoped, now confirmed already resolved by the
consolidation itself):
  Temperature's consensus bonus raises the ci_adjusted_kelly cap itself
  (KELLY_CAP * KELLY_CAP_CONSENSUS_MULT, 0.33 at defaults) when consensus
  holds, so a strong consensus trade can size up to 0.33. Precip's
  consensus bonus multiplies ci_adjusted_kelly by 1.25 but keeps the cap
  at plain KELLY_CAP (0.25) regardless -- so the x1.25 only ever changes
  the outcome when the pre-multiply value is already below ~0.20; above
  that, precip_consensus trades are capped identically to non-consensus
  ones. Unclear whether this is intentional (precip's higher irreducible
  uncertainty per _CONDITION_CONFIDENCE, 0.85-0.90 vs temperature's 1.00,
  already discounts precip sizing elsewhere) or an oversight from
  temperature's consensus-cap-raise never being ported to precip.

Why not now (original, superseded -- already resolved, see above):
  - Behavior-preserving refactor discipline again: this is a sizing
    judgment call (is precip's extra discount deliberate risk management
    or drift?), not something to decide as a side effect of a
    consolidation pass.

When to revisit: N/A, resolved (confirmed already-shipped behavior kept
  deliberately, per user decision 2026-07-18).

[RESOLVED 2026-07-19] KALSHI CENTS/DOLLARS PRICE NORMALIZATION IMPLEMENTED INDEPENDENTLY 3+ TIMES
Priority: was Medium -- this exact normalization has already produced two
  real bugs fixed one-copy-at-a-time (the zero-bid falsy bug in
  parse_market_price; the 2026-07-13 HIGH bug where the REST-fallback raw
  shape was read as dollar floats), and Kalshi is actively migrating
  shapes, so every new API shape must be taught to each copy separately.

RESOLVED 2026-07-19:
  Shipped utils.coalesce_market_price(market, *keys) -> float (order_
  executor's version verbatim, proven equivalent to weather_markets.
  parse_market_price's split _coalesce+to_float pair by tracing both
  bodies field-by-field before replacing either) plus 3 named key-pair
  constants (YES_BID_KEYS, YES_ASK_KEYS, NO_BID_KEYS) next to it, matching
  this entry's own plan almost exactly -- one deviation: placed in
  utils.py, not market_types.py, since market_types.py turned out (checked
  before deciding) to be a pure TypedDict-only module with zero runtime
  logic today, and utils.py is already the established home for shared
  runtime helpers both weather_markets.py and order_executor.py import
  from (no circular-import risk either way).
  order_executor._coalesce_cents_or_dollars deleted, all 7 call sites
  (6 call sites + 1 stale docstring reference) switched to the shared
  function + key constants. weather_markets.parse_market_price's nested
  _coalesce/to_float pair removed, un-nested to call the shared function
  directly -- the existing TestParseMarketPrice suite (incl. the L2-D
  integer-1/zero-bid-not-bypassed regression tests) needed zero changes
  and now doubles as regression coverage for the shared function.
  schema_validator.py's third, independently-drifted copy
  (_price_to_decimal) is where this consolidation found a REAL, live bug
  beyond the two the entry cites: unlike the other two copies,
  _price_to_decimal used a uniform `f > 1.0` check for every input type,
  so an integer value of exactly 1 (a genuine 1-cent bid/ask) was
  misclassified as already-decimal and returned as $1.00 instead of $0.01
  -- a 100x error, though low-severity in practice since this function
  only feeds a diagnostic range-check warning, never a live trading
  decision, and 1.0 still happens to pass the [0,1] range check so it
  never even triggered a false alarm. Independently corroborated by a
  pre-existing point-in-time audit doc (docs/grade_audit/outputs/
  schema_validator.py.md, graded 2026-06-29, found by this same session
  rather than trusted blind) that had already flagged the identical `f ==
  1.0` edge case as "theoretical... Kalshi bids are never exactly 1.00 in
  practice" -- the audit correctly identified the mechanism but
  under-stated it as purely theoretical without checking it against the
  other two (correct) copies' int-vs-float branching, which is exactly
  what this consolidation surfaces. Checked that audit doc's other two
  findings (validate_market's DEBUG-not-WARNING logging,
  validate_nws_response's missing ok=False) while in the file -- both
  already fixed in a prior session, stale claims, not re-flagged.
  A real design nuance this call site needed and the other two didn't:
  _price_to_decimal fails SOFT (returns None on unparseable input) since
  schema_validator.py's whole job is to never crash the caller on bad API
  data, while coalesce_market_price is deliberately left unguarded
  (matching order_executor.py's/weather_markets.py's original,
  already-accepted behavior -- both run inside a per-order/per-market
  try/except upstream and are meant to raise on genuinely malformed data
  so it's skipped, not silently treated as $0, which would be MORE
  dangerous for live trading than crashing that one iteration). Rather
  than weaken the shared function for its live-money callers, added a
  local `_safe_price()` wrapper in schema_validator.py (try/except around
  the shared call) that preserves _price_to_decimal's exact fail-soft
  contract. _price_to_decimal deleted; the presence-gate logic ("only
  validate range when both bid and ask are actually present") was
  preserved exactly (same None-check semantics as the original raw_bid/
  raw_ask computation, just restructured as a boolean instead of
  reconstructing the coalesced value twice).
  kalshi_ws.py's ticker-message parser and tracker.py's _candle_dollars
  left untouched, per this entry's own plan -- both are genuinely
  different input shapes (WS ticker messages are always already-dollar-
  format with no cents-int variant ever observed; candlestick sub-fields
  are always "_dollars"-suffixed, no ambiguity to resolve), not the same
  duplication class.
  20 new tests: utils.coalesce_market_price direct coverage (11 tests --
  cents-int, 1-cent boundary, dollar-float, dollar-string, cents-string,
  zero-bid-not-bypassed, first-key-wins, fallback-to-second-key,
  no-keys-defaults-to-zero, unparseable-raises, key-constants-match,
  order_executor-uses-the-shared-helper-not-a-local-copy -- the last one
  deliberately NOT an `is`-identity check against utils.
  coalesce_market_price, since this test file runs in the same pytest
  session as tests that call importlib.reload(utils) for unrelated
  reasons (see the main.py frozen-import entry above), which would make
  an identity check order-dependent/flaky); schema_validator's _safe_price
  + the fixed 1-cent bug + the fail-soft-on-garbage-input contract (4
  tests, tests/test_phase2_batch_l.py, replacing the deleted
  _price_to_decimal's own direct test). Mutation-tested the core int-vs-
  float boundary fix by flipping `v >= 1` to `v > 1` in the shared
  function and confirming it broke the new coalesce_market_price test, the
  new schema_validator tests, AND the pre-existing weather_markets L2-D
  regression test simultaneously (proving all 3 consumers now genuinely
  share one code path, not just three independently-passing copies), then
  restored.
  678 tests pass across the full regression sweep (every test file
  touching price parsing across weather_markets.py/order_executor.py/
  schema_validator.py/kalshi_client.py/paper.py); ruff + ruff format +
  mypy clean.
  Independent second-opinion review (Agent, opus) came back clean, and
  flagged one adjacency note (not fixed, pre-existing in all 3 original
  copies, not introduced by this consolidation): a STRING price of "1"
  (as opposed to int 1) hits coalesce_market_price's `isinstance(v, str)`
  branch, computes `float("1")=1.0`, and `1.0 > 1.0` is False, so it's
  returned as 1.0 ($1.00) instead of 0.01 -- the same bug class as the
  int-1 fix above, but for the string-cents path, which none of the 3
  original implementations ever handled correctly either. Extremely rare
  in practice (a bare cents-formatted string "1" rather than a dollar
  string like "0.01"); worth a real fix if coalesce_market_price is next
  open for other reasons, not urgent enough for a dedicated pass.

Problem (as originally scoped, still accurate for historical context):
  order_executor._coalesce_cents_or_dollars (order_executor.py:106-126)
  and the nested _coalesce + to_float pair inside
  weather_markets.parse_market_price (weather_markets.py:3089-3113)
  implement identical logic (None-skipping coalesce; str->float/100 if
  >1; int>=1 -> /100; float>1.0 -> /100), with the order_executor
  docstring admitting "Mirrors weather_markets.parse_market_price's
  coalesce so callers agree" -- a mirror enforced by nothing. The
  weather_markets copy is nested inside the function so it *can't* be
  imported, which is why the duplicate exists. schema_validator.py:34-61
  carries a third partial variant of the same legacy/current key-pair
  knowledge, tracker.py:926's _candle_dollars handles the candlestick
  flavor ("_dollars"/"_fp"), and kalshi_ws.py's ticker parser normalizes
  to dollars independently (its 0.0-missing-side sentinel caused the
  2026-07-12 one-sided-book review finding).

What it would look like: [DONE 2026-07-19, see resolution above]
  One `coalesce_market_price(d, *keys) -> float` in market_types.py (or
  utils.py -- shipped in utils.py, see resolution), used by
  parse_market_price (un-nest), order_executor (delete its copy), and
  schema_validator's range check; consolidate the key-pair lists
  ("yes_bid"/"yes_bid_dollars" etc.) as constants next to it. Existing
  tests become tests of the one helper. kalshi_ws's parse-time
  normalization can stay (different input shape) but should reference the
  same constants (left as-is, genuinely a different shape -- see
  resolution).

Why not now (resolved):
  - Touches live order pricing -- same review bar as the reprice work.
    Done as its own session rather than waiting for a Kalshi-API-shape
    change to force it, per explicit user request.

When to revisit:
  - N/A, closed.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] TWO FUNCTIONS NAMED _current_forecast_cycle -- ONE IS DEAD AND HIDES FROM THE DEAD-CODE GUARD VIA NAME COLLISION
Priority: was Low-Medium -- small cleanup, but it exposes a systematic blind
  spot in tests/test_dead_code_scan.py worth closing while it's cheap.

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: took the delete option (not the rename-to-
  _current_nwp_cycle alternative -- the 4-cycle granularity had no real
  consumer to preserve it for). Deleted weather_markets._current_forecast_cycle
  entirely; confirmed via grep zero remaining production references anywhere.
  Retargeted its two tests (tests/test_forecasting.py's TestForecastCycle)
  from the dead 4-cycle bare-string function onto order_executor.
  _current_forecast_cycle -- the real, live-used function, which had never
  had a direct correctness test of its own value logic before (every other
  test site only ever monkeypatches it away). Rewrote the boundary
  assertions for its actual 2-cycle (00z/12z), date-prefixed format.
  Deleted the now-duplicate dead tests in tests/test_phase4.py's
  TestCurrentForecastCycle (renamed to TestLogPredictionForecastCycle once
  only its unrelated log_prediction test remained).

  Fixed the actual guard blind spot in tests/test_dead_code_scan.py per
  this entry's own suggestion: split _called_in() into _bare_called_in()/
  _alias_called_in(), and added _resolve_prod_evidence() which, when
  checking whether a candidate function has a real caller in another file,
  first checks whether that other file independently defines its own
  module-level function of the same name (precomputed once via a
  funcs_by_file dict, not re-parsed per candidate). If it does, only an
  explicit alias-import call still counts as evidence -- a bare same-name
  call in that file is its own self-reference, never the candidate's,
  matching how Python name resolution actually works. 4 new synthetic-
  source tests (TestSameNameCollisionResolution) exercise this directly:
  the collision-not-counted case (the actual bug this closes -- confirmed
  by hand that it fails under the old logic if reverted), two no-collision
  baseline cases proving normal alias/bare cross-file calls still count,
  and a mutation-proof case proving an explicit alias import still counts
  even when the other file also defines its own colliding name (rules out
  the fix over-suppressing real evidence). 127 tests pass across
  tests/test_dead_code_scan.py + test_forecasting.py + test_phase4.py, plus
  every test file touching order_executor._current_forecast_cycle
  (test_execution_proof.py, test_p0_10_paper_prelog.py,
  test_prediction_kwargs.py, test_shadow_predictions.py,
  test_trade_improvements.py -- 32 passed). Lint/mypy clean.

  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- clean, no HIGH/MEDIUM issues.
  Verified by hand that the collision logic matches real Python name
  resolution (a bare call in a file that defines its own same-named
  function can only ever resolve to that file's own definition, never
  another file's), that the fix only ever makes the guard MORE aggressive
  (can't introduce a false "live code flagged dead"), and that the
  synthetic tests are genuine regressions rather than passing vacuously.
  Two LOW cosmetic notes, both applied: renamed the now-misleadingly-named
  test_phase4.py class, and removed a harmless-but-confusing no-op
  _strip_def_line call in the collision branch (the only checks that run
  there -- alias-call and string-reference matching -- can't match a `def
  name(` line either way, so stripping it changed nothing).

Problem (original framing, resolved above):
  order_executor.py:78-87 defines _current_forecast_cycle -> 2 cycles/day,
  date-prefixed ("2025-05-15_12z"), used everywhere real (order dedup,
  execution_log rows, all log_prediction forecast_cycle values via
  main.py:68's import). weather_markets.py:819-832 defines a *different*
  _current_forecast_cycle -> 4 cycles/day, bare "12z". The
  weather_markets one has zero production callers (grep: only
  tests/test_forecasting.py:398,414 import it; its neighbor
  _ttl_until_next_cycle is the one weather_markets actually uses). Two
  functions with the same name and the same conceptual job but
  incompatible formats is exactly the "same concept represented
  differently" trap -- and worse, the dead-code guard can't see it: the
  scan is regex-over-source (\bname\s*\(, per its own docstring), so
  order_executor's five call sites of its *own* _current_forecast_cycle
  make the weather_markets one look called. Any future dead function that
  happens to share a name with a live one in another scanned file gets
  the same free pass.

[PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-19] ForecastCache EXISTS, BUT ~14 HAND-ROLLED TTL DICTS DO THE SAME JOB
Priority: was Low-Medium -- consistency/tooling debt, not a live bug; each
  hand-rolled cache re-implements expiry slightly differently and each
  needs its own test-isolation hook.

PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-19: before touching anything, did a full survey
  (via a dedicated Explore pass) of every remaining cache this entry lists,
  since the original text's own line numbers/shapes had drifted and only 2
  of ~14 were actually checked in detail before. Findings that changed the
  scope from what this entry originally implied:
  - `_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE` (weather_markets.py) has NO TTL at all -- a
    permanent memoization dict, not a `(value, ts)` cache. Migrating it
    would be a real behavior change (introducing expiry where none existed),
    not a pure refactor.
  - `_DYNAMIC_BIAS_CACHE` (weather_markets.py) stores a 3-tuple
    `(value, count, ts)` -- a different shape needing the count folded into
    the stored value rather than the timestamp slot.
  - nws.py's 5 cache dicts: 2 are permanent (no TTL, same behavior-change
    risk as _MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE), 1 (`_station_cache`) is disk-persisted
    across process restarts via `.nws_station_cache.json`, and 3
    (`_forecast_cache`, `_obs_cache`, `_precip_cache`) stamp with wall-clock
    `time.time()` instead of monotonic time -- migrating those would be a
    real semantic change, not mechanical, plus `_forecast_cache` alone is
    referenced in 4 test files.
  - climate_indices.py's `_indices_cache` and climatology.py's `_MEM_CACHE`/
    `_sigma_mem_cache`: none store a timestamp in the entry at all --
    freshness is tracked via a sibling module variable or disk-file mtime
    instead. Forcing these into ForecastCache's per-entry model means
    restructuring the freshness mechanism, not swapping a declaration.
  - ml_bias.py's 3 "caches" aren't even TTL'd keyed dicts -- one is a bare
    `tuple | None`, all 3 are load-once memoization backed by pickle/HMAC or
    JSON disk files. Don't belong in this refactor at all.
  User chose (after reviewing this survey) to migrate only the genuinely
  clean, same-shape group now and leave everything above explicitly
  documented as out of scope, rather than force a shape mismatch or an
  accidental behavior change onto code that currently works fine.
  Migrated (8 caches, all plain `(value, ts)` or already-per-entry-TTL
  shapes, all sharing ForecastCache's exact semantics with zero behavior
  change): weather_markets.py's `_NBM_CACHE`, `_ECMWF_CACHE`,
  `_PRECIP_ENSEMBLE_CACHE`, `_HRRR_CACHE`, `_WEATHERAPI_CACHE` (the
  original 5-cache recommendation below), plus `_CONSENSUS_CACHE` (turned
  out to already use the exact `(value, ts, ttl)` per-entry-TTL shape
  `ForecastCache.set_with_ttl()` wants -- an even cleaner fit than the
  original 5), mos.py's `_MOS_CACHE`, and metar.py's `_METAR_CACHE`.
  Real subtlety handled, not glossed over: `_NBM_CACHE`/`_ECMWF_CACHE`/
  `_HRRR_CACHE`/`_WEATHERAPI_CACHE`/`_MOS_CACHE`/`_METAR_CACHE` all
  negative-cache a real `None` result (a known-failed fetch, to avoid
  hammering a dead endpoint within the TTL window) -- plain
  `ForecastCache.get()` can't distinguish "no entry" from "entry present
  with value None," so a naive `.get() is not None` port would have
  silently defeated negative caching (every call to a known-dead endpoint
  would re-fetch instead of respecting the TTL). All 6 read sites use
  `get_with_ts()`'s explicit `hit` boolean instead. `_PRECIP_ENSEMBLE_CACHE`
  and `_CONSENSUS_CACHE` never store bare `None`, so their read sites use
  the simpler `.get()` pattern already established by weather_markets.py's
  pre-existing `_ensemble_cache`/`_forecast_cache`.
  Also found and simplified, while migrating `_NBM_CACHE`: the "don't
  clobber a still-fresh OTHER-var cache entry" check (added 2026-07-17, see
  REAL NBM VIA IEM NBS STATION BULLETINS) previously computed
  `now - raw_ts >= TTL` by hand -- `ForecastCache.get()` already returns
  None for both "no entry" and "expired," exactly the "missing or stale"
  condition that check needed, so it collapses to a plain
  `.get(key) is None`. **Correction (opus review caught this, not
  self-caught):** not quite behavior-identical in one narrow case --
  `.get()` also can't distinguish a fresh negative-cached `None` (a prior
  failed fetch) from "no entry," so this now overwrites a fresh-but-failed
  OTHER-var entry with real data from the current successful fetch, where
  the old raw-timestamp check would have preserved the stale failure.
  Reviewed and accepted as a strict data-quality improvement (the
  replacement is always a genuine max/min derived from the same successful
  response, never a worse or wrong value) rather than reintroducing the
  manual timestamp check just to avoid it -- documented in-code at the call
  site so a future reader tracing this exact discrepancy isn't left
  guessing.
  Updated 4 test files that directly patched these caches as raw dicts or
  hand-seeded raw tuples (test_ecmwf.py, test_nbm.py, test_metar.py,
  test_weather_markets.py) to construct/patch a real `ForecastCache()`
  instance instead -- `.clear()` calls elsewhere (conftest.py's autouse
  METAR-cache fixture, test_mos.py, test_phase2_batch_a.py,
  test_forecasting.py's HRRR test) needed no changes since `.clear()` is
  already a ForecastCache method with identical semantics.
  New regression tests (one per negative-caching cache -- the single most
  important correctness property this migration had to preserve): each
  calls the fetch function twice against a mocked-to-fail backend and
  asserts the SECOND call does not re-invoke the mock, proving a negative-
  cached result is actually respected rather than silently re-fetched every
  call. Mutation-tested directly: temporarily reverted `_NBM_CACHE`'s read
  site to a naive `.get() is not None` check, confirmed the new test failed
  with the exact predicted symptom (a 2nd IEM/Open-Meteo call), then
  restored the real fix -- validates the same pattern used identically
  across all 6 negative-caching sites.
  433 tests pass across every affected file (test_ecmwf.py, test_nbm.py,
  test_weather_markets.py, test_forecasting.py, test_phase4.py,
  test_metar.py, test_mos.py, test_mos_nbs.py, test_phase2_batch_a.py,
  test_forecast_accuracy.py, test_price_and_size.py, test_cron_integration.py,
  test_p1_remaining.py); ruff + ruff format + mypy clean on all 3 changed
  source files (weather_markets.py, mos.py, metar.py).
  Scope decision made explicitly via AskUserQuestion before writing any
  code (twice -- once on discovering the wrinkled caches, once again after
  the full survey), not assumed.

FURTHER RESOLVED 2026-07-19 (same day, second pass): user asked to "migrate
  the rest." Before touching anything, re-derived the "still open" list
  above from source rather than re-asserting it (user explicitly asked to
  review the recommendation) -- this caught that the first pass's own
  characterization had OVERSTATED the risk on 5 of the 10 remaining
  non-ml_bias.py caches:
  - `_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE`: confirmed tiny real key-space ((city, days_back),
    ~20-40 entries), no disk persistence, "session cache" by its own
    comment -- genuinely safe to migrate permanent-by-design.
  - nws.py's `_gridpoint_cache`: turned out simpler than described -- no
    timestamp tuple at all today (bare key->value), tiny key-space, no
    disk persistence. Safe.
  - nws.py's `_forecast_cache`/`_obs_cache`/`_precip_cache`: the "wall-clock
    vs monotonic is a real semantic change" framing from the first survey
    didn't hold up on direct inspection -- none of the 3 ever negative-
    cache (every write site stores a real result; every failure path
    returns without writing), none persist to disk, and nothing anywhere
    reads the stored timestamp for any purpose besides "how long ago" --
    switching to ForecastCache's monotonic clock is a pure robustness
    improvement (immune to system clock adjustments), not a risky change.
  - climate_indices.py's `_indices_cache`: also overstated -- it already
    used `time.monotonic()` via the sibling `_indices_loaded_at` variable
    (the first survey conflated it with nws.py's wall-clock group), and its
    single-slot shape maps directly onto `.set_with_ttl("latest", result,
    ttl)`. Its "don't cache an all-zero failure" logic (H-17) just means
    skipping the `.set()` call on that path -- exactly current behavior.
  Confirmed genuinely hard on re-check (this part of the first survey held
  up): `_station_cache` (nws.py) really does need a whole-dict dump/load
  that ForecastCache has no enumeration API for; climatology.py's
  `_MEM_CACHE`/`_sigma_mem_cache` really are a different architecture
  (load-once-per-process, gated by disk-file mtime on first load only, not
  an in-memory TTL at all -- forcing a ForecastCache TTL onto this would
  either no-op or introduce new re-fetch behavior mid-process).
  User confirmed (via AskUserQuestion, presented with the corrected
  breakdown): migrate the 7 confirmed-safe caches now, leave the 3
  genuinely-hard ones + ml_bias.py's 3 documented as out-of-scope (see
  below, updated from the first pass's list).
  Migrated 7 more: weather_markets.py's `_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE` (permanent,
  `ttl_secs=float("inf")`) and `_DYNAMIC_BIAS_CACHE` (count folded into the
  stored value, `(dyn_bias, count)` instead of `(dyn_bias, count, ts)`);
  nws.py's `_gridpoint_cache` (permanent), `_forecast_cache`, `_obs_cache`,
  `_precip_cache`; climate_indices.py's `_indices_cache` (the
  `_indices_loaded_at` sibling global deleted entirely, no longer needed).
  None of these 7 ever negative-cache a bare `None`, so all use the simpler
  `.get()` pattern (no `get_with_ts()` needed, unlike 6 of the first 8).
  Updated 4 more test files with raw-dict/stale-global references
  (test_forecasting.py's `_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE` patch, test_phase2_batch_c.py's
  3 direct `_indices_cache`/`_indices_loaded_at` reassignments -- rewritten
  to construct/patch a real ForecastCache and use `.set_at()` to simulate an
  already-expired entry instead of hand-setting a fake timestamp global,
  test_phase2_batch_d.py's raw `_precip_cache["NYC"] = (...)` seed rewritten
  to `.set_at()` and its `isinstance(nws._precip_cache, dict)` assertion
  corrected to `isinstance(..., ForecastCache)`).
  Mutation-tested the riskiest of the 7 (climate_indices.py's restructuring,
  since it's the only one that changed the actual freshness mechanism, not
  just the storage): temporarily disabled the cache-read in `get_indices()`,
  confirmed the existing `test_cache_served_within_ttl` test failed with the
  predicted symptom (4 fetch calls instead of 2), restored the fix. The
  other 6 didn't need a fresh mutation test -- the existing TTL-expiry tests
  (already updated to use `.set_at()` for expired-entry simulation) exercise
  the same real property directly.
  319 tests pass across every affected file (test_forecasting.py,
  test_http.py, test_phase2_batch_c.py, test_phase2_batch_d.py,
  test_weather_markets.py, test_phase4.py) plus the full first-pass
  regression set re-run clean; ruff + ruff format + mypy clean on all 3
  changed source files (weather_markets.py, nws.py, climate_indices.py).
  Independent opus review: clean, 2 non-blocking observations initially --
  (1) `get_indices()` caches under one single "latest" key regardless of
  `target_month`/`target_year` params; (2) test_forecasting.py's
  `_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE` test mock uses a plain `ForecastCache()` (4h default
  TTL) rather than mirroring production's `ttl_secs=float("inf")` --
  harmless for a synchronous test that never waits 4+ hours, left alone.

  FOLLOW-UP, same day -- (1) upgraded from "non-blocking, pre-existing" to
  a real fix after re-checking the actual blast radius rather than taking
  the "pre-existing, low-impact" framing at face value: `get_indices()`'s
  sole real caller passing explicit args is `temperature_adjustment(city,
  target_date)` (weather_markets.py), called from `analyze_trade()` --
  weather_markets.py:6057 -- once per scanned market, using THAT market's
  own `target_date`. cron.py/`_analyze_once` scan many markets per cycle;
  any two markets whose `target_date`s fall in different calendar months
  (routine for multi-day-out markets near a month boundary) would share the
  single "latest" cache slot -- whichever market's (year, month) got cached
  first would silently answer for every other market's climate-index
  adjustment for the rest of that cache's 24h TTL, corrupting the real
  climatological-probability blend `analyze_trade()` uses for live
  trade decisions. Not hypothetical, not pre-existing-and-therefore-fine --
  a real, currently-reachable bug in the live pipeline (this migration
  didn't introduce it, the single-slot key already existed before, but it
  deserved fixing rather than leaving alone once the actual reach was
  traced). Fixed: cache now keyed by `(year, month)` instead of a fixed
  "latest" string -- `year`/`month` computation moved before the cache
  lookup (previously computed only in the fetch-miss branch, after the
  lookup). H-17's "don't cache an all-zero failure" behavior, thread safety
  (`_indices_lock` still wraps the full read-check-fetch-write sequence),
  and the negative-caching-never-happens property are all unchanged.
  New regression test (`test_different_target_months_do_not_clobber_each_
  other`) calls get_indices() for two different (target_month, target_year)
  pairs against mocked fetch data with distinct values per month, asserting
  each call gets its own correct result rather than the second clobbering
  into the first's cache slot. Also fixed 3 test_phase2_batch_c.py sites
  that hand-seeded the cache under the old hardcoded "latest" string (which
  would now silently never be found by the real (year,month)-keyed lookup,
  making those tests pass for the wrong reason -- an always-empty cache,
  not a correctly-detected-expired one) to seed under the real current
  (year, month) key instead. Mutation-tested the new test directly:
  reverted to the shared "latest" key, confirmed it failed with the exact
  predicted symptom (April's call returning March's cached month), restored
  the fix. (2) left as-is, per the original assessment -- still correctly
  harmless.
  301 tests pass (test_phase2_batch_c.py, test_weather_markets.py,
  test_phase4.py, test_forecasting.py); ruff + ruff format + mypy clean.
  Independent opus review: clean, and surfaced one bonus finding beyond
  what this fix set out to address -- under the old shared "latest" key,
  `get_enso_index()` (always current month, zero args) and
  `temperature_adjustment()` (target month, which can differ from current
  month for any multi-day-out market) also clobbered EACH OTHER's cache
  slot, not just different markets' `temperature_adjustment()` calls
  clobbering each other. The `(year, month)` keying fix resolves this
  cross-contamination too, at no extra cost -- noted here since it wasn't
  part of the original bug report but is a real, strictly-better side
  effect of the same fix.

Problem (original framing, migrated caches now resolved above -- remaining
scope unchanged):
  forecast_cache.py's ForecastCache is the purpose-built abstraction
  (TTL, per-entry set_with_ttl, used by weather_markets._ensemble_cache:398,
  _forecast_cache:505, tracker._run_trend_cache:2715 (new 2026-07-16),
  config._paper_min_edge_cache:158). But the majority of caches hand-roll
  the dict[key, (value, ts)] + `time.monotonic() - ts < TTL` idiom:
  weather_markets._NBM_CACHE/_ECMWF_CACHE/_PRECIP_ENSEMBLE_CACHE
  (1610-1613), _HRRR_CACHE (1705), _WEATHERAPI_CACHE (1775),
  _MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE (2644), _CONSENSUS_CACHE (4288), _DYNAMIC_BIAS_CACHE
  (166); mos.py:59 _MOS_CACHE; metar.py:79 _METAR_CACHE; nws.py:44-49
  (five separate dicts); climate_indices.py:29; climatology.py:52,252;
  ml_bias.py:29-31. Variations that already exist between copies:
  monotonic vs wall-clock timestamps, negative-result caching (the new
  _run_trend_cache added its own separate 30-min negative TTL -- a
  feature every fetch cache arguably wants, implementable once in the
  class), and per-cache clear() fixtures in tests (conftest.py:108 clears
  _METAR_CACHE by hand; the climatology isolation fixture is another
  one-off).

What it would look like (the 15-cache clean group -- the original 5 +
_CONSENSUS_CACHE/_MOS_CACHE/_METAR_CACHE from the first pass, plus
_MAE_WEIGHTS_CACHE/_DYNAMIC_BIAS_CACHE/_gridpoint_cache/_forecast_cache/
_obs_cache/_precip_cache/_indices_cache from the second): [DONE, see
resolution notes above]

What's still open (confirmed genuinely hard on the second pass's re-check,
not just first-pass caution -- see the survey above for why each one
resisted the corrected, more thorough re-derivation):
  - `_station_cache` (nws.py): persists via a whole-dict dump/load
    (`_save_station_cache`/`_load_station_cache`), a pattern ForecastCache
    has no enumeration API for. Needs either extending the shared
    ForecastCache class with a new capability (touches every already-
    migrated cache, including live-trading-adjacent `_ensemble_cache`) or
    staying a plain dict permanently.
  - climatology.py's `_MEM_CACHE`/`_sigma_mem_cache`: a genuinely different
    architecture -- load-once-per-process, freshness gated by disk-file
    mtime checked only on first load, not an in-memory TTL at all. Forcing
    a ForecastCache TTL onto this would either no-op or introduce new
    re-fetch behavior mid-process that doesn't exist today.
  - ml_bias.py's 3 caches: not TTL'd keyed dicts at all (pickle/HMAC/JSON-
    backed load-once singletons, one isn't even a dict) -- excluded from
    this refactor permanently, not just deferred.
  - Add optional negative-TTL support to ForecastCache once (generalizing
    the run-trend pattern) -- not needed by anything migrated across either
    pass (none of the 15 needed a shorter miss-TTL than their hit-TTL
    except _CONSENSUS_CACHE, which already had per-entry TTL support before
    any of this).
  - A single clear_all_forecast_caches() registry to collapse the per-cache
    conftest fixtures -- still just 1 real fixture (METAR's) plus a handful
    of inline .clear() calls in test files; not enough of them yet to
    clearly pay for a registry.

Why not now (for the remaining 3 genuinely-hard caches):
  - `_station_cache` needs a real API-design decision (extend the shared
    ForecastCache class, or don't) that affects every other cache using it,
    not just this one -- worth its own scoped look, not a drive-by.
  - climatology.py's 2 need a real architectural call (does this become a
    ForecastCache-backed design, keep the disk-mtime-gated load-once
    pattern, or something else) -- not a live bug, and forcing a decision
    here risks getting it wrong for the sake of closing out a backlog item.

When to revisit:
  - `_station_cache`: whenever nws.py is next open AND someone wants to
    make the ForecastCache-enumeration-API call deliberately, not as a
    side effect of something else.
  - climatology.py's 2: whenever climatology.py is next open for other
    reasons, with the same discipline -- re-derive from source, don't
    batch-assume they're now safe just because most of the rest turned
    out to be.
  - ml_bias.py's 3: not applicable -- permanently excluded.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] execution_log.py's SWALLOWED-ALTER MIGRATIONS vs tracker.py's VERSIONED IDIOM
Priority: was Low-Medium -- worked fine so far, but the live-execution feature
  stream (7 new columns across 07-12/07-13 alone) is growing the weaker
  idiom fastest, and its failure mode is silent.

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: ported to tracker.py's PRAGMA user_version cursor,
  taking the "freeze current 16 ALTERs + CREATE TABLEs as migrations 1..N"
  option from this entry's own "what it would look like" (not the shared-
  helper option -- kept the ~25-line runner duplicated per-file rather than
  touching tracker.py's already-tested version, matching this project's
  minimal-blast-radius convention). Base `CREATE TABLE orders` now holds
  only the 10 columns that predate this migration list (id, ticker, side,
  quantity, price, order_type, status, response, error, placed_at); all 16
  previously-migrated columns (fill_quantity through entry_prob) now exist
  ONLY as _MIGRATIONS entries -- matching tracker.py's own convention of
  never touching the base CREATE TABLE again once versioning exists, and
  eliminating the prior duplication where a column was declared in both the
  CREATE TABLE and a swallowed ALTER. _run_migrations() mirrors tracker.py's
  version exactly: PRAGMA user_version as cursor, writes it after each
  applied step (crash-safety), and distinguishes "duplicate column"/"already
  exists" (case-insensitive message match) from a genuine OperationalError,
  which now propagates instead of being silently swallowed -- the actual bug
  this entry existed to fix. Traced by hand and confirmed via a new test:
  a real pre-existing on-disk DB (already has all 16 columns from the old
  CREATE TABLE, PRAGMA user_version still 0 since it was never set) self-
  heals cleanly -- every ALTER hits "duplicate column", gets caught, cursor
  catches up to 16, no crash, no data loss.

  5 new tests (tests/test_execution_log.py::TestSchemaVersionMatchesMigrations,
  mirroring tracker.py's own guard class): _SCHEMA_VERSION==len(_MIGRATIONS),
  PRAGMA user_version==_SCHEMA_VERSION after init_log(), all 16 migrated
  columns present on a genuinely fresh DB (proving the migrations run for
  real, not just no-op against a CREATE TABLE that already had them), a
  mutation-style test proving a genuine OperationalError (bad-table-name
  ALTER, not a duplicate-column message) actually propagates through
  init_log() -- the direct regression test for the original swallowed-error
  bug -- and the legacy-DB self-heal scenario built as a real pre-versioning
  table, not simulated. 33/33 tests in the file pass; also ran every test
  file elsewhere in the repo that imports execution_log (dedup, live
  execution, paper, trading gates, trade improvements, risk control,

  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) per this project's mandatory-review
  convention -- came back clean. Specifically traced: no column present in
  both the base CREATE TABLE and a migration (which would make that
  migration a guaranteed permanent no-op masking whether the cursor
  advances correctly); every column any function in the file reads/writes
  resolves to either the base table or a migration; the pre-existing-DB
  self-heal scenario by hand; thread-safety of _run_migrations running
  inside the existing double-checked _init_lock (no new issue -- only one
  thread ever runs migrations, flag flips true only after they complete);
  and that the new tests genuinely exercise real code paths rather than
  passing vacuously. One LOW note, not a bug: execution_log's
  _run_migrations catches `sqlite3.OperationalError` specifically where
  tracker.py's catches bare `Exception` -- correct and actually tighter for
  a list that's 100% ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN today; worth revisiting only if
  a future migration here is a CREATE UNIQUE INDEX over dirty data (would
  raise IntegrityError, which should propagate anyway, so still desired
  behavior).

Problem (original framing, resolved above):
  tracker.py migrations are versioned (_MIGRATIONS list + PRAGMA
  user_version cursor, tracker.py:30-255) with guard tests asserting
  _SCHEMA_VERSION == len(_MIGRATIONS) -- and this exact machinery just
  caught and self-healed a real drift on 2026-07-16 (see the FORECAST
  RUN-TO-RUN TREND SIGNAL entry above). execution_log.py instead
  re-attempts a flat list of 16 ALTER statements on every process init
  inside `except sqlite3.OperationalError: pass` (execution_log.py:
  106-129). Structural problems: (a) a genuine OperationalError (locked
  DB, disk error) on a *needed* ALTER is indistinguishable from
  "duplicate column" and is silently swallowed -- the column just doesn't
  exist and the first INSERT referencing it fails later, far from the
  cause; (b) no version cursor means no way to write a data-backfill
  migration (only additive ALTERs are expressible); (c) every new
  live-execution feature grows the list, so the two files' migration
  styles diverge further with each shipped entry.

What it would look like: [DONE, see resolution notes above]

Why not now (resolved):
  - Was gated on doing it while live=1 rows were still empty (the easiest
    this migration would ever be) -- done while that was still true;
    ENABLE_MICRO_LIVE remained False throughout, untouched by this change.

When to revisit:
  - N/A, closed.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] utils.utc_today() SAYS "USE EVERYWHERE INSTEAD OF date.today()" -- 17 SITES STILL DON'T
Priority: was Low-Medium -- a recognized, already-bitten bug class with a
  stated convention and zero enforcement. One instance (2026-07-16's own
  new code) was found and fixed that session; the remaining sites were
  unaudited.

Problem (as originally scoped):
  utils.py defines utc_today() with the docstring "Use everywhere instead
  of date.today()", and the codebase had two documented scars from
  ignoring it: web_app.py's WA-timezone comment and the 07-13 test
  failures where fixtures built from local date.today() disagreed with
  simulate_portfolio's utc_today() frame. tracker.py's run-trend fetcher
  was the same bug, confirmed and fixed 2026-07-16. ~17 more sites were
  listed as unaudited, with no guard test to catch a new one.

What shipped:
  Live re-scan (2026-07-18) found 19 real call sites (line numbers had
  drifted from the original list), individually read for actual
  materiality before touching anything:
  - 10 were genuine UTC/local-calendar mismatch risk and got the
    utc_today() swap: tracker.py's _fetch_previous_run_daily (the
    sibling this entry explicitly flagged -- its own sibling
    _fetch_previous_run_leads already proved the mismatch is real on
    this machine); main.py's cmd_watch_settle and the interactive-menu
    "due trades" warning (both gate paper-trade settlement on
    target_date <= today -- live-relevant, traced target_date's actual
    runtime provenance back through order_executor.py to confirm it's
    genuinely the UTC-anchored market date, not assumed); backtest.py's
    run_backtest and run_walk_forward (cutoffs feed a UTC min_close_time
    filter against Kalshi's API and a market_date >= ? SQL filter);
    climate_indices.py and climatology.py (month/year-boundary only,
    negligible materiality, but same convention, free fix); main.py's
    backup-filename timestamp and cmd_forecast CLI display; web_app.py's
    today_forecasts dashboard API (display-only, but visible to a human).
  - 2 were left exactly as-is with documented reasons, added to the new
    guard test's allowlist: cloud_backup.py's 30-day-retention prune
    (this entry's own original text already pre-judged this correctly)
    and cron.py's once-a-day prod reminder (has its own idempotency
    check, a few hours of drift is harmless).
  - 1 site (backtest.py's fetch_archive_precip) turned out to have ZERO
    callers anywhere in real code (verified: only referenced in generated
    doc artifacts, not even in tests/) -- its sibling
    fetch_archive_precip_prob is the one actually wired into
    run_backtest and makes its own independent API call. Deleted the
    dead function entirely per user sign-off rather than fixing a
    timezone bug in unreachable code; it was also invisible to
    test_dead_code_scan.py's existing guard, which only scans
    paper.py/tracker.py/weather_markets.py, not backtest.py.
  - 1 site (main.py:2360, cmd_today's manual-trade feature-importance
    logging) was NOT actually a timezone bug at all, found by re-checking
    the analysis (user explicitly asked for a second pass on the initial
    categorization, which caught this): best_a.get("target_date") is an
    ISO STRING (weather_markets.py's analyze_trade return dict stores
    target_date.isoformat(), not a date object), and the code did
    `str_value - date.today()` -- always raising TypeError, silently
    swallowed by an enclosing `except Exception: pass`. record_feature_
    contribution is called from nowhere else in the entire codebase, so
    this had likely never successfully recorded a contribution since it
    was written. Fixed by extracting the computation into a new
    main._feature_importance_days_out(target_date_str) helper (parses
    the string properly, uses utc_today(), returns 0 on any parse
    failure) -- extracted specifically so it's unit-testable in isolation
    from cmd_today's large, untested interactive CLI flow.

  New guard: tests/test_date_today_guard.py, matching test_dead_code_
  scan.py's / test_disputed_row_guard.py's allowlist style, but scanning
  every top-level production .py file (not a fixed list -- real sites
  turned up in 6 different files, so hardcoding a file list would
  reproduce the exact "one gets missed" shape this guard exists to
  prevent). Uses Python's tokenize module to mask out STRING/COMMENT
  token spans before pattern-matching, not a per-line "#"/'"""'-prefix
  check -- the first version of this guard false-positived on its own
  new _feature_importance_days_out docstring, which mentions
  "date.today()" as explanatory prose on an interior line that starts
  with neither marker (a multi-line-docstring blind spot the simpler
  per-line check couldn't see). Locked in as its own regression test
  using a synthetic in-memory source string. Mutation-tested (injected a
  fake unallowlisted date.today() call, confirmed the guard fails, then
  reverted).

  New tests: tests/test_tracker.py's TestFetchPreviousRunDailyUsesUtcToday
  (mutation-tested against requests.get's call_count directly, not just
  the return value -- the function's own broad `except Exception: return
  None` around the HTTP call means a correct early-return and a bad
  mutation that proceeds to a live call are otherwise indistinguishable
  by return value alone, both give None); tests/
  test_feature_importance_days_out.py (6 tests covering the extracted
  helper; mutation-tested two ways -- reverting the helper to the raw
  str-minus-date expression (no try/except) reproduces the exact
  TypeError that was previously silently swallowed by cmd_today's own
  except clause; reverting only the subtraction while keeping the
  helper's own try/except (a subtler, more realistic mutation) still
  fails 2 of 6 tests via a value mismatch (0 instead of the correct
  days_out) rather than a raised exception, since that except clause
  catches the TypeError internally -- an opus review caught that the
  original draft of this note overstated this second case as "4 of 6
  fail with the exact TypeError," corrected here).

[RESOLVED 2026-07-19] DEAD TAKE-PROFIT PLUMBING STILL RUNS EVERY WATCH CYCLE AFTER THE FEATURE WAS DECLINED
Priority: was Low -- vacuous no-op, but it's a decided-against feature whose
  machinery still executes, prints user-facing messaging, and carries

  anything: confirmed via a whole-repo grep (not just paper.py) that

  Deleted: the exit_target param + docstring line + stored trade-record

  test_check_exit_targets_no_side_uses_no_bid_not_no_ask,
  test_check_exit_targets_no_side_fires_at_correct_price -- the class's

  tests/test_debug_fixes.py) that build literal trade-record dicts
  including an inert `"exit_target": None` key -- unrelated to the

  worth the unrelated diff churn to strip it out.
  Traced all 3 real (non-test) place_paper_order callers (main.py:3641,
  order_executor.py:2683, web_app.py:2797) to confirm none pass
  exit_target and all use keyword args exclusively past the first 4

  test_menu_ux.py, test_debug_fixes.py, test_p1_remaining.py,
