  mypy clean on all 3 changed files.

FOLLOW-UP, same day, pushed separately: the independent Agent(opus) review
  of the deletion above surfaced one adjacency note -- paper.export_
  trades_csv() (paper.py:2120) derives its csv.DictWriter fieldnames from
  trades[0].keys() alone (trades are append-ordered, so trades[0] is the
  OLDEST record) with DictWriter's default extrasaction="raise" -- any
  later trade with a key the oldest one lacks crashes the export. This is
  pre-existing (not introduced by the exit_target deletion, and already
  catalogued as a LOW finding in docs/audit_findings.md) -- caused by
  schema GROWTH (a field added to place_paper_order after the oldest
  on-disk trade was placed), not shrinkage: the review's own follow-up
  check confirmed exit_target's removal is actually the safe direction
  (old trades keep the key, new ones lack it, which trades[0]-keyed code
  handles fine either way) -- corrected a first-draft code comment that
  had this backwards. User asked to fix it regardless, since the growth
  direction is a real, live, already-reachable crash. Checked the other 2
  csv.DictWriter sites in
  the repo (tracker.py:2294, web_app.py:1347) first -- both derive
  fieldnames from tracker.get_history()'s SQL rows, which are uniform per
  query regardless of age (unlike paper.py's independently-evolved JSON
  records), so neither is actually vulnerable to this bug class; scope
  confirmed narrow to paper.py alone. Fixed by unioning every trade's keys
  (first-seen order) into fieldnames instead of reading only trades[0],
  with restval="" so any trade missing a given key renders an empty cell
  instead of raising -- handles both schema growth (a newer trade has a
  field older ones lack) and schema shrinkage (an older trade has a field,
  like exit_target, that newer ones no longer do) correctly. New
  regression test (test_export_trades_csv_handles_heterogeneous_schema)
  builds two trades then directly mutates the on-disk JSON to strip a
  field from the oldest and add a field only the newest has, asserting the
  export doesn't raise and both fields get their own column; mutation-
  tested via git stash (confirmed it fails with the exact predicted
  `ValueError: dict contains fields not in fieldnames` against the
  reverted code, then restored). 152 tests pass in tests/test_paper.py
  (172 including test_debug_fixes.py); ruff + ruff format + mypy clean.

Problem (original framing, resolved above):
  The 2026-07-13 resting-exits research established that nothing in the
  repo ever sets exit_target ("fully dead -- threaded through
  place_paper_order's signature and checked by check_exit_targets(), but
  ... none of them ever actually sets it") and the user explicitly
  declined building take-profit. The plumbing was left in place:
  paper.py:849 (parameter), 866 (docstring), 955 (stored on every trade
  as None), check_exit_targets (paper.py:1561-1603, filters to
  exit_target is not None -> always empty), and main.py:2908-2922 calls
  it every cmd_watch cycle with a green "[Auto-exit] ... reached
  take-profit target" print that can never fire. Four test classes
  (tests/test_paper.py:880-1039) keep the dead path green. Invisible to
  test_dead_code_scan.py because the function has a real caller -- the
  deadness is in the data (no producer of the field), a shape the guard
  doesn't model.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-18] TEST-ORDER-DEPENDENT importlib.reload(order_executor) BROKE main.py's FROZEN-IMPORT IDENTITY CHECK
Priority: was Medium (CI-breaking, safety-adjacent test coverage) -- now Low
  (fixed; only a cousin risk remains, see below)

RESOLVED 2026-07-18: found via real GitHub Actions CI failure output (not a
  local repro -- this repo's local .env masked half of it, see below) after
  pushing the execution_log migration and _current_forecast_cycle cleanup
  commits. Two independent pre-existing bugs, neither caused by those two
  commits, both exposed by the same CI run:
    1. tests/test_execution_stability.py::test_gfs_window_disabled_with_
       zero_lockout did `importlib.reload(order_executor)` to pick up a
       monkeypatched GFS_LOCKOUT_MINS env var. Reloading a module rebinds
       EVERY function in it to a new object -- including
       _prediction_kwargs_from_analysis, which main.py had already imported
       once at process-import time and never re-imports. Since
       test_execution_stability.py sorts alphabetically before
       test_prediction_kwargs.py, this reload made main.py's frozen
       reference permanently diverge from order_executor's live one for the
       rest of the session, breaking test_prediction_kwargs.py's
       `main._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis is
       order_executor._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis` identity check (the
       actual regression guard the LOG_PREDICTION KWARGS ASSEMBLY entry
       shipped). Confirmed by hand via git stash/pop: reverting the fix and
       running both files together reproduces the exact CI failure;
       restoring it removes it. Fixed by replacing the reload with
       `monkeypatch.setattr(order_executor, "_GFS_UPDATE_LOCKOUT_MINS", 0)`
       -- the function only reads that one env-derived constant (its
       sibling _GFS_UPDATE_HOURS_UTC is a hardcoded literal, not
       env-derived, so no coverage was lost), matching this suite's own
       dominant convention elsewhere (test_live_execution.py's
       `monkeypatch.setattr(order_executor, "MIN_EDGE", ...)`).
    2. tests/test_trading_gates.py's test_blocks_when_live_trading_not_
       enabled and test_blocks_when_live_trading_env_absent both called
       gate.check() with no client and patched `main.KALSHI_ENV` -- but
       LiveTradingGate.check()'s no-client fallback reads
       os.getenv("KALSHI_ENV") directly (a 2026-07-09 fix, documented in
       the method's own docstring), never touching main.KALSHI_ENV. The
       patch was a pure no-op in this code path. It passed locally only
       because this dev machine's real, gitignored .env sets
       KALSHI_ENV=prod, loaded into the real os.environ via load_dotenv()
       at import time -- GitHub Actions has no .env, so
       os.getenv("KALSHI_ENV", "demo") returned "demo" there, blocking on
       "not prod" before ever reaching the LIVE_TRADING_ENABLED check these
       two tests actually exist to verify. Read all 16 uses of
       patch("main.KALSHI_ENV", ...) in the file before scoping the fix --
       the other 14 either also set the real env var via
       patch.dict(os.environ, _PROD_ENV) (redundant but harmless), pass an
       explicit client (bypassing the os.getenv fallback entirely), or
       deliberately prove a client's base_url overrides a stale env value
       (test_client_base_url_wins_over_stale_kalshi_env_*). Two more
       (test_check_or_raise_raises_when_blocked,
       test_micro_live_blocked_by_gate) are the same no-op pattern but
       happen to still pass on CI because os.getenv's "demo" default
       coincides with the blocked outcome they assert -- fragile but not
       currently broken, left alone. Fixed the two genuinely broken tests
       by moving KALSHI_ENV into their existing patch.dict(os.environ, ...)
       calls, matching the sibling test_blocks_when_not_prod (already
       fixed for this exact reason in an earlier session).
  Independently reviewed (Agent, opus) -- clean. Verified the setattr fix
  loses no coverage (only env-derived constant the function reads), the
  patch.dict `clear=True` site restores every real env var except the one
  intentionally-removed flag (no PATH-clearing risk, and the gate returns
  before ever importing paper.py in that branch), and no pytest-xdist
  parallelism concern (not installed; os.environ mutation wouldn't cross
  worker processes even if it were). Checked every OTHER cross-module
  identity assertion in the suite for the same reload-vs-frozen-import
  vector -- only one structural cousin exists
  (test_backtest.py's backtest._WEATHER_SERIES is wm.KNOWN_WEATHER_SERIES),
  and it self-heals since weather_markets is never reloaded anywhere.

Problem (original framing): N/A -- found and fixed in the same investigation,
  not a pre-logged backlog item.

Why not now: N/A -- fully resolved.

When to revisit:
  - N/A for the two fixed bugs. See the follow-up cousin-risk note below for
    something worth a future look, not an active bug.

[PARTIALLY RESOLVED 2026-07-19] main.py's FROZEN `from utils import ...` COULD REPEAT THE SAME IDENTITY-DIVERGENCE BUG -- utils IS RELOADED BY ~6 TESTS
Priority: Low -- latent structural risk, not a current bug; nothing today
  asserts an identity check that would catch it firing.

RESOLVED 2026-07-19 (partially -- the audit below found the entry's own
  "likely possible for most/all of them" framing overstated; only 2 of the
  7 real reload(utils) call sites could actually be converted):
  Audited all 7 call sites individually (the entry said "~6 tests" but
  test_p9_p10.py and test_sameday_reserve.py each reload twice, for 7
  total) rather than trusting the "likely possible for most/all" claim at
  face value. Found two genuinely different shapes:
  (a) 3 reload(utils) call sites across 2 files (test_kalshi_ws.py's
  test_stale_entry_returns_none; test_sameday_reserve.py's _patch_env and
  _patch_dynamic_env helpers, used by 10 tests) use reload(utils) purely as
  a means to get a downstream
  function (kalshi_ws.get_cached_mid_price, order_executor.
  _sameday_effective_cap) to observe a new constant value -- exactly the
  order_executor._prediction_kwargs_from_analysis shape this entry was
  modeled on. Confirmed both downstream functions do a function-local
  `from utils import X` fresh on every call (not a frozen copy), so
  monkeypatch.setattr(utils, "X", value) reproduces the exact same
  observable effect with none of the whole-module rebind risk. Converted
  both -- reload(utils) is now gone from these 2 files entirely.
  (b) The other 4 sites (test_p9_p10.py's test_enable_micro_live_defaults_
  false / test_brier_alert_threshold_default, test_risk_control.py's
  test_drawdown_halt_default_is_20pct, test_starting_balance.py's
  test_utils_exports_starting_balance) assert directly on utils.<CONST>
  itself -- the test SUBJECT is utils' own `float(os.getenv(...))`
  module-level parsing logic. Converting these to monkeypatch.setattr
  would make them tautological (assert a value you just set equals
  itself), testing nothing about production code. Left these as
  reload(utils) -- genuinely the correct tool for what they verify, not
  an oversight.
  Since 4 reload(utils) sites remain and genuinely can't be eliminated,
  the underlying hazard for main.py's frozen `from utils import (...)`
  (line 94) is only reduced, not closed -- any of those 4 tests can still
  cause main.is_trading_paused/MIN_ARB_EDGE/MIN_EDGE/STRONG_EDGE to
  diverge from utils' live copies for the rest of a pytest session if a
  future identity-check test is ever added and happens to run after one
  of them. Took this entry's own second option for the remaining risk:
  documented the hazard directly in main.py's import block (a comment
  above the `from utils import ...` line explaining the mechanism,
  naming is_trading_paused as the highest-risk symbol since it's a
  function object, and pointing at this backlog entry) rather than adding
  a new test that would itself demonstrate/cause the exact divergence
  it's warning about -- that would be introducing the failure mode to
  prove it exists, not fixing anything.
  27 tests pass in the 2 converted files; scoped as low-risk since the
  conversions only change *how* a constant is set for a test, not what's
  asserted. No new tests needed -- the existing tests already
  differentiate outcomes by the patched values (e.g. slots=0 vs slots=2
  producing different expected caps across the existing test suite),
  which is itself adequate coverage that the monkeypatched attribute
  really flows through to the function under test (spot-verified by hand:
  temporarily setting utils.WS_CACHE_TTL_SECS to a huge value flips
  get_cached_mid_price's result from None to a real price, confirming the
  attribute is what's actually read).

Problem (as originally scoped, still accurate for the un-converted 4 sites
and the remaining latent main.py risk):
  main.py:94 does `from utils import MIN_ARB_EDGE, MIN_EDGE, STRONG_EDGE,
  is_trading_paused` once at process-import time -- the exact same frozen-
  import shape that caused the order_executor bug above. utils.py is
  reloaded by ~6 tests (test_kalshi_ws.py:234, test_p9_p10.py:620/629,
  test_risk_control.py:371, test_sameday_reserve.py:17/123,
  test_starting_balance.py:36), each to pick up an env-var-driven constant
  the same way test_execution_stability.py's now-fixed reload did for
  order_executor. No test today asserts `main.<symbol> is
  utils.<symbol>` the way test_prediction_kwargs.py does for
  order_executor, so nothing currently fails -- but if such a test is ever
  added (a very plausible next step, since it's the same defensive pattern
  that caught the order_executor bug), or if any of those 6 reloads is ever
  reordered to run before a test relying on main.py's frozen utils symbols
  behaving identically to utils' live ones, the same bug class recurs.

What it would look like:
  Either audit whether any of the reload sites could instead monkeypatch
  the specific derived constant directly (DONE 2026-07-19 for 3 of 7 --
  see resolution above; the other 4 genuinely can't, they test utils' own
  parsing), or document the frozen-import hazard directly in main.py's
  import block so a future contributor adding an identity check knows to
  check for this (DONE 2026-07-19, see resolution above).

Why not now (for the remaining 4-site latent risk):
  - Not a live bug -- no identity assertion exists yet to trip it, and the
    4 remaining reload(utils) sites are the correct tool for what they
    test (utils' own env-var parsing), not something to work around.
    Genuinely closable only by a larger restructuring (e.g. an autouse
    fixture that reasserts main.py's frozen symbols after any utils
    reload) that isn't worth it for a risk with no current trigger.

When to revisit:
  - If a new main.py <-> utils identity-check test is ever added (it would
    immediately surface whether the remaining 4 sites actually cause
    trouble in practice), or test_p9_p10.py/test_risk_control.py/
    test_starting_balance.py is next open for other reasons.

[RESOLVED 2026-07-19] AUTO UN-RETIREMENT -- RETIRED FORECASTING METHODS COULD NEVER GENERATE FRESH RECOVERY EVIDENCE
Priority: Medium -- surfaced by manually un-retiring 'ensemble' on
  2026-07-19 (justified by the letter of the existing rolling-Brier-
  recovery rule) and then investigating, unprompted, why the "recovery"
  looked thin: a direct DB query showed only 1 ensemble prediction logged
  since its 2026-07-10 retirement (an unsettled shadow row from 07-11) --
  the manual un-retirement was real by the rule as written, but the rule
  itself was measuring stale evidence, not genuine recovery.
======================================================

Problem:
  analyze_trade()'s retired-method gate (weather_markets.py, "Retired
  strategy gate" comment) returns None immediately once `method` resolves
  to a currently-retired value -- before log_prediction() or shadow-
  logging (order_executor._log_shadow_predictions, which only ever
  operates on markets that already produced a real analysis dict) can run.
  So a retired method can structurally never generate a new prediction,
  ever, while retired. auto_retire_strategies()'s rolling-Brier "recovery"
  guard (rolling_brier <= threshold skips re-retirement) was built to stop
  a stale lifetime average from masking real improvement, but with zero
  fresh rows possible, "rolling last-20" for a retired method is just
  whatever pre-retirement predictions haven't yet rolled off -- it
  necessarily converges toward "looks recovered" over time regardless of
  whether the method's forecasts have actually gotten any better, purely
  because old bad predictions age out of the window with nothing behind
  them. There was no automatic path back to trading at all -- only the
  manual `python main.py retire-strategies` / unretire_strategy() CLI path
  existed, and even that had no fresh-evidence signal to act on.

What it would look like (built and shipped 2026-07-19):
  An isolated "probation" checker, structurally unable to affect the live
  scan/trading path, that gives a retired method a controlled way to prove
  itself:
  - analyze_trade(enriched, *, bypass_retirement_check=False) --
    weather_markets.py:5546. New keyword-only param (all ~19 real call
    sites are positional, so this is a zero-behavior-change default for
    every one of them); when True, the retired-method gate no longer
    short-circuits, so the full analysis (including Kelly) runs and
    returns a complete dict even for a retired method.
  - is_probation column (tracker.py predictions table, migration v50,
    _SCHEMA_VERSION 49->50) + is_probation param on log_prediction(),
    mirroring is_shadow's exact shape (including the MIN()-based UPSERT
    merge semantics: a later real write always clears it, a probation
    write can never re-flag an already-real row). Kept as its own column
    rather than folded into is_shadow so the probation query stays a
    clean is_probation=1 filter without needing to also exclude ordinary
    shadow rows for other (non-retired) methods.
  - tracker.brier_score_probation_rolling(method, window=20,
    min_samples=15) -- deliberately separate from
    brier_score_by_method_rolling() (which intentionally does NOT filter
    is_probation, since a probation row is a real forecast and should
    feed the live retirement-decision Brier too). The auto-unretirement
    decision specifically needs a signal that's *exclusively* fresh,
    deliberately-generated post-retirement evidence -- otherwise a rolling
    window still mostly full of old pre-retirement rows would look
    "recovered" long before any genuine new evidence exists, which is the
    exact gap this entry is about. Same days_out=0 exclusion via
    multiday_predictions as every other method-level Brier query.
  - weather_markets.check_retirement_probation(client) -- once per day
    (RETIREMENT_PROBATION_PATH state file, same gate shape as
    check_series_drift()/log_city_registry_report()), own try/except,
    never raises, no-ops immediately if nothing is currently retired.
    Samples up to 25 markets (random.sample) via get_weather_markets(client)
    -- 60s-cached, so calling it again right after cron's main scan is
    normally a cache hit -- runs analyze_trade(bypass_retirement_check=True)
    on each, and logs a probation prediction (is_shadow=True,
    is_probation=True) only for markets whose *resolved* method (dynamic
    per-market, not knowable in advance) is currently retired. Then checks
    brier_score_probation_rolling() for every retired method and calls the
    existing tracker.unretire_strategy() the moment it clears
    _PROBATION_UNRETIRE_THRESHOLD=0.25 -- the same bar
    auto_retire_strategies() uses to retire in the first place, not a
    stricter one, because unretire_strategy() already writes a 72h
    re-retirement-immunity pin, which is what actually protects against
    flapping (no separate hysteresis buffer needed).
  - Wired into cron.py right after log_city_registry_report()'s call site,
    same isolation contract (own try/except at the call site too).

  Design decision surfaced to the user rather than guessed: presented 3
  initial auto-unretirement approaches (all rejected -- "rethink these
  options"), then a 4th ("isolated probation checker, completely outside
  the live scan/trading path") was proposed and explicitly approved
  ("yes, that sounds right -- build it") before any code was written.

  Verified end-to-end with real (non-mock-everything) tests: hand-computed
  Brier arithmetic against a seeded temp DB (15 correct probation
  predictions -> Brier exactly 0.01), mutation-tested to confirm the
  is_probation=1 filter and the days_out=0 / non-probation-row exclusions
  are load-bearing (removing the filter measurably polluted the score:
  0.01 -> 0.0706), and 9 new behavioral tests for
  check_retirement_probation() itself (no-op when nothing retired, once-
  per-day gate, never-raises, logs only for markets whose bypass-resolved
  method is retired, auto-unretires only when probation Brier clears
  threshold and not when it's still bad or still None/insufficient-
  samples) -- each mutation-tested by temporarily breaking the guard being
  tested and confirming the corresponding test fails with the predicted
  symptom, then restoring. Also found and fixed a real pre-existing gap in
  tests/test_p0_11_retired_strategy.py's own fixture while writing the new
  bypass tests: _make_enriched() had no title (direction-keyword parsing
  requires one) and an all-identical 12-member ensemble (trips the
  degenerate-ensemble gate) -- both invisible before because none of that
  file's 4 original tests ever needed a non-None result, only new bypass
  tests that actually need Kelly to run exposed them. Full scoped
  regression (test_retirement_probation.py, test_p0_11_retired_strategy.py,
  test_p9_p10.py, test_shadow_predictions.py, test_series_drift.py,
  test_city_registry_report_logging.py, test_tracker.py, plus all 5 cron
  test files) -- 391 passed. ruff + mypy clean on every changed file.

  Independent opus second-opinion review (before push, per standing
  workflow) found no real bugs -- independently re-derived the migration's
  column/placeholder/param counts, independently re-ran
  brier_score_probation_rolling against its own real temp DB, traced all
  ~19 analyze_trade call sites to confirm bypass_retirement_check is inert
  everywhere except check_retirement_probation's own call, and confirmed
  the 72h re-retirement-immunity pin (is_strategy_pinned gate inside
  auto_retire_strategies) is actually wired up to protect against
  flapping. Two low-severity notes, both addressed: (1) is_stale(m) moved
  inside the per-market try/except (weather_markets.py) so a crash there
  (is_stale has a documented history of TypeError on malformed
  volume_fp/open_interest_fp) skips just that one market instead of
  aborting the whole day's probation run; (2) added 5 committed,
  non-mocked integration tests (tests/test_tracker.py
  TestIsProbationColumn) covering the is_probation column round-trip,
  probation-vs-real-row isolation, the min_samples gate, and both
  directions of the MIN() upsert merge -- previously only manually
  mutation-tested during development, not committed as regression
  coverage.
